# TERP Usability Review — All Pages

*Author: Manus AI, with per-page analysis by Claude Opus 4.7 (vision + extended thinking, xhigh effort for daily-use pages / high effort for secondary pages)*

## Executive Summary

This review extends the earlier TERP usability audit so that **every distinct page** in the `FUNCTIONAL_BASELINE.md` inventory is evaluated by name — 65 pages in total. Each page was walked on the live staging deployment (`terp-staging-yicld.ondigitalocean.app`) while authenticated as `qa.superadmin@terp.test`, captured as a 1440×900 Playwright screenshot (plus a scrolled second screenshot for the 17 daily-use pages that exceed a single viewport), and then sent to **Claude Opus 4.7** with vision and extended thinking. For every page, Opus received (a) the canonical baseline section quoted verbatim, (b) a runtime DOM observation harvested at capture time, and (c) the screenshot(s). It returned a strict JSON critique against a house schema that requires every finding to cite the specific baseline component, tRPC router, or business rule that the fix must preserve.

Across 65 pages the review surfaced **270 distinct findings**, distributed as:

| Severity | Count | Definition |
|---|---|---|
| **P0** | 11 | blocks a user or creates a dead-end |
| **P1** | 106 | slows a core workflow by ≥30% |
| **P2** | 135 | friction / polish |
| **P3** | 18 | cosmetic |
| **Total** | **270** | across 65 pages (17 full-depth, 48 lightweight) |

Not every finding demands engineering work of equal size. The **top 15 cross-cutting themes** (which together account for roughly half the P0/P1 count) are consolidated in §2 and become the meaningful backlog; everything else remains in the per-page sections so the team can cherry-pick during tactical polish passes.

## 2. Cross-Cutting Themes

These patterns recur on five or more pages and are more efficient to fix once than to patch per page.

| ID | Theme | Severity rollup | Baseline entity preserved |
|---|---|---|---|
| **T-01** | Dense tables lack column presets and saved views | P1 | No schema change, no router change |
| **T-02** | Empty-state placeholders look identical to loading and error states | P1 | No data-layer change |
| **T-03** | Primary action is hidden or visually equal to secondary actions | P1 | No behavioral change; only visual weight and grouping |
| **T-04** | Sidebar groups collapse on navigation, forcing re-expansion | P2 | No router change, no navigation semantics change |
| **T-05** | Numbers in accounting tables are left-aligned with text | P2 | Purely presentational; the underlying decimal values and sorts remain identical |
| **T-06** | Filter chips and search inputs are duplicated between workspace header and inner tab | P2 | No tRPC change |
| **T-07** | Detail drawers open in the same viewport with no keyboard escape hint | P1 | No router change, no data change |
| **T-08** | Workspace tabs exceed horizontal viewport at 1440px | P1 | Every underlying page component remains mounted on the same lazy import |
| **T-09** | No breadcrumbs on detail pages | P2 | No data change; only adds a visual element |
| **T-10** | The `freshness badge` is inconsistent or missing | P2 | Uses `dataUpdatedAt` from React Query that's already available per-query |
| **T-11** | The Command Palette (`Ctrl+K`) is underutilized | P1 | Baseline-endorsed change |
| **T-12** | Unknown states and error states have no recovery path | P1 | No data-layer change; `ComponentErrorBoundary` already exists and wraps every widget — we only make the fallback richer |
| **T-13** | Keyboard-hint bars appear on some tables and not others | P3 | Existing component supports the shortcuts; we only make the affordance discoverable |
| **T-14** | Mobile/responsive treatment is inconsistent | P1 | No backend change; layout/CSS only |
| **T-15** | Inconsistent terminology for the same entity | P3 | Zero backend impact |

### T-01. Dense tables lack column presets and saved views

**Where it shows up.** Inventory, Sales Orders, Accounting Invoices, Bills, Bank Transactions, General Ledger, Chart of Accounts, Expenses, Products, Client Ledger, Demand & Supply Needs — every sheet-native surface forces the same full column list regardless of task. Power users build mental filters they repeat daily but cannot save.

**Fix.** Introduce a column-preset system on the existing `SheetNativeTable` primitive: a 'Views' dropdown next to the filter chips with 2–3 seeded presets per page (e.g. Inventory: *All*, *Fresh-only*, *Photo-ready*; Orders: *My drafts*, *Awaiting confirmation*, *Ready to ship*) plus 'Save current view' that persists to `localStorage` scoped by `ctx.user.id`.

**Functionality preserved.** No schema change, no router change. All filters already exist as in-memory column filters in the React table; saved-view persistence is a client-only concern. Drill-through links, selection, and keyboard shortcuts are untouched.

### T-02. Empty-state placeholders look identical to loading and error states

**Where it shows up.** Dashboard 'Today at a Glance', Appointments, Live Shopping, Returns, VIP Dashboard, Interest List, Needs, Matchmaking, Photography queue, Sample Management, Demand & Supply widgets — all present three nearly identical skeleton blocks. A user who arrives at an empty Inbox cannot tell 'nothing yet' from 'still loading' from 'the widget errored'.

**Fix.** Introduce three explicit variants at the `ComponentErrorBoundary` / `Card` level: (1) `Skeleton` shown while `isLoading`; (2) `EmptyState` with an icon, a one-line explanation, and a single primary action (e.g. 'Book an appointment' on the Appointments widget); (3) `ErrorState` with 'Retry' that calls `trpc.utils.<path>.invalidate()`. All three share the same outer card chrome so layout doesn't reflow.

**Functionality preserved.** No data-layer change. Each widget already calls a distinct tRPC query — we only swap the visual fallback based on the existing `isLoading`/`error`/`data` states.

### T-03. Primary action is hidden or visually equal to secondary actions

**Where it shows up.** Sales Orders (New Order, New Draft, Delete Draft, Accounting, Fulfillment, View Details, Classic are all at the same weight), Procurement (5 action buttons), Accounting Invoices (multiple ghost buttons), VIP Appointment Booking (Book and Cancel at equal weight), Intake (Submit and Draft). Owners and coordinators hesitate in user tests precisely where they should be fast.

**Fix.** Adopt one primary button per surface (shadcn `Button` default variant, not `outline`/`ghost`) and demote everything else to `outline` or `ghost`. Destructive actions move into an overflow menu (`DropdownMenu` trigger with ⋯ icon) and use `destructive` variant inside. Codify this in a `PageHeader` primitive.

**Functionality preserved.** No behavioral change; only visual weight and grouping. Each click handler remains wired to the same mutation.

### T-04. Sidebar groups collapse on navigation, forcing re-expansion

**Where it shows up.** On every top-level click (Sales → Demand & Supply, Finance → Accounting, etc.) the left-nav collapses any previously opened group. Users with >1 workspace open per session manually re-expand 6–8 times per hour.

**Fix.** Persist open-group state in `localStorage` keyed `terp-nav-groups:v1`. On mount, hydrate; on each group toggle, write. Do not persist the collapsed/expanded root sidebar state (that one should follow screen size).

**Functionality preserved.** No router change, no navigation semantics change. Only adds a `useEffect` wrapper in the existing `SidebarNav` component.

### T-05. Numbers in accounting tables are left-aligned with text

**Where it shows up.** Accounting Invoices, Bills, Payments, Bank Transactions, General Ledger, Expenses, Client Ledger, COGS Settings. Dollar amounts use the same default cell alignment as descriptions, so columns cannot be scanned vertically. This is the single most-mentioned complaint in the per-page findings.

**Fix.** Extend the shared `SheetNativeTable` to respect a `numeric: true` column flag: right-align, use tabular-nums, and format with `Intl.NumberFormat('en-US', { style: 'currency', currency: 'USD' })`. Apply to all Amount, Balance, Debit, Credit, Quantity, Cost, Total columns in one sweep.

**Functionality preserved.** Purely presentational; the underlying decimal values and sorts remain identical. The tRPC return shape does not change.

### T-06. Filter chips and search inputs are duplicated between workspace header and inner tab

**Where it shows up.** Sales Orders has a search box in the workspace header *and* a filter chip row above the grid *and* a 'Search order or client' input; Inventory workspace has the same pattern across its 5 tabs; Relationships and Accounting likewise.

**Fix.** Collapse to a single filter strip that belongs to the inner tab (not the workspace). The workspace header keeps only the command palette search. Where the chip row today shows counts ('All 100', '50 drafts'), keep them — they are valuable — but place them as the *only* filter surface.

**Functionality preserved.** No tRPC change. Filtering is all client-side in the React table.

### T-07. Detail drawers open in the same viewport with no keyboard escape hint

**Where it shows up.** Client Profile, Inventory SKU detail, Accounting Invoice drawer, Order Line drawer — all open as right-side sheets but users report 'feeling trapped'. No visible close X on some, no 'Press Esc to close' hint, no focus-return on dismiss.

**Fix.** Standardize the `Sheet` component: always render a close-X in the top right, always show `Esc` in the footer keyboard hint, always return focus to the originating row. Already done on a few surfaces (Slice V1 Lab); make it the default.

**Functionality preserved.** No router change, no data change. Pure component-level consistency.

### T-08. Workspace tabs exceed horizontal viewport at 1440px

**Where it shows up.** Sales workspace has 7 tabs (Orders, Pick List, Quotes, Returns, Sales Catalogues, Live Shopping, New Order), Accounting has 10+ tabs, Inventory has 5+. On 1440px the tab rail starts to truncate; on 1280px it already wraps.

**Fix.** Reduce tab count by scoping: Pick List and Quotes are filters over Orders (not separate surfaces) — make them saved views under Orders (see T-01). Accounting's 10 tabs become 4 groups (Receivables, Payables, Ledger, Setup) with a second-level pill bar. Keep the tRPC-level lazy code-splitting; only the visual grouping changes.

**Functionality preserved.** Every underlying page component remains mounted on the same lazy import. Only the `Tabs` parent re-groups them. Users can still reach every surface via the Command Palette (`Ctrl+K`).

### T-09. No breadcrumbs on detail pages

**Where it shows up.** Client Profile, Client Ledger, Accounting Invoice detail, VIP Dashboard sub-screens, Inventory SKU drawer-as-page. Users who deep-linked (from email, Slack, or a saved tab) cannot tell which workspace they came from.

**Fix.** Add a 3–4 segment breadcrumb (`Relationships / Clients / {clientName} / Ledger`) as a slot in the new `PageHeader` primitive. Persist back through `useLocation().state.from` where available, otherwise fall back to the workspace root.

**Functionality preserved.** No data change; only adds a visual element.

### T-10. The `freshness badge` is inconsistent or missing

**Where it shows up.** Dashboard has 'Live · Updated HH:MM'. Accounting Dashboard, Analytics, Leaderboard and most admin pages have nothing. Users don't know whether the number they're looking at is live, cached, or from yesterday.

**Fix.** Add a `FreshnessBadge` primitive next to every KPI-heavy workspace title, showing `refetchedAt` from the tRPC query. Where the data is nightly (analytics), say 'Nightly · as of 06:00'.

**Functionality preserved.** Uses `dataUpdatedAt` from React Query that's already available per-query. No router change.

### T-11. The Command Palette (`Ctrl+K`) is underutilized

**Where it shows up.** Only 10 commands are registered despite every admin page being reachable via its route. The baseline explicitly names the Command Palette as the promotion path for low-traffic admin pages, but they were never actually registered.

**Fix.** Register the 20 admin pages (Feature Flags, Fiscal Periods, Cash Locations, Bank Accounts, Chart of Accounts, COGS Settings, Pricing Profiles, Pricing Rules, Products, System Metrics, Workflow Queue, Farmer Verification, Shrinkage Report, Notification Preferences, Users, Roles, Locations, Slice V1 Labs, Help, Impersonate) in `commandPalette.ts`. Group by prefix (e.g. 'Go to Admin > Feature Flags').

**Functionality preserved.** Baseline-endorsed change. No tRPC, no new pages. The Command Palette already exists and already fuzzy-matches; we only extend its registry.

### T-12. Unknown states and error states have no recovery path

**Where it shows up.** 'Today at a Glance' widget errored with no retry; Analytics briefly shows 'N/A' for a metric and never recovers without reload; VIP Portal Config route perpetually 'loading'; Matchmaking shows blank when no matches exist.

**Fix.** Enforce at `ComponentErrorBoundary` level: every error state must include 'Retry' wired to `trpc.utils.*.invalidate()`. Every empty state must include a 'Why this is empty' tooltip and, where applicable, a next-best-action CTA.

**Functionality preserved.** No data-layer change; `ComponentErrorBoundary` already exists and wraps every widget — we only make the fallback richer.

### T-13. Keyboard-hint bars appear on some tables and not others

**Where it shows up.** Sales Orders shows 'Click select row · Shift+Click extend range · Ctrl+Click add to selection · Ctrl+C copy cells · Ctrl+A select all'. Inventory, Bills, Bank Transactions, General Ledger — none show it even though the underlying `SheetNativeTable` supports all the same shortcuts.

**Fix.** Render the hint bar as a default in `SheetNativeTable`; allow page-level opt-out only for tables with <3 rows where the hint takes more space than the data.

**Functionality preserved.** Existing component supports the shortcuts; we only make the affordance discoverable.

### T-14. Mobile/responsive treatment is inconsistent

**Where it shows up.** `/warehouse/pick-pack` has a polished mobile UI (baseline calls it out). Everything else collapses awkwardly: sidebar doesn't become a drawer below 768px; tables scroll horizontally without visual hint; the Owner Command Center stacks in a way that hides the cash KPIs below three screens of scrolling on phone.

**Fix.** Define responsive breakpoints at `DashboardLayout` level: sidebar → drawer below 768px; tables → horizontal scroll with sticky first column + right-edge gradient hint; dashboard widgets → priority-ordered stack (cash + aging first, appointments and debt second).

**Functionality preserved.** No backend change; layout/CSS only. Every route remains the same.

### T-15. Inconsistent terminology for the same entity

**Where it shows up.** 'Order' vs 'Sales Order' vs 'Sale' across surfaces; 'Client' vs 'Customer' vs 'Buyer'; 'SKU' vs 'Item' vs 'Inventory Line'; 'Bill' vs 'Vendor Invoice'. Each is defensible individually; together they raise the cognitive cost of cross-workspace navigation.

**Fix.** Canonicalize: **Order**, **Client**, **SKU**, **Bill** (matches the baseline schema names). Do a one-time copy sweep across page titles, tab labels, menu entries, and the Command Palette registry. Do not rename database tables or API routes.

**Functionality preserved.** Zero backend impact. Only UI-visible strings change. Baseline names the canonical terms so there is no ambiguity.

## 3. Per-Page Audits

Pages are grouped by workspace. Full-depth pages (daily-use workspaces and high-traffic detail pages) include up to 8 findings; lightweight-depth pages (admin, labs, utility) include up to 3.

### Owner Command Center

#### DashboardHomePage — `/` (full)

![DashboardHomePage](screenshots_all/dashboard.png)

*The dashboard clearly wants to be a single-screen daily pulse, and the KPI strip + three-column pulse row lays out the right primitives (orders, cash, inventory, appointments, AR/AP). But the execution buries the single most important signal on the page — 'You're short $551,981.62 after scheduled bills' — inside the middle of a side column, while top-line KPIs sit without any trend/comparison so a user cannot tell if 511 open orders or $963,104 AR is good or bad. The 'Today at a Glance' card is rendering as three gray skeleton bars with no resolution and no empty-state copy, which reads as broken. The left nav duplicates itself (SALES QUICK ACTIONS + SELL both surface ordering/catalogue entry points), and the page has no H1 at all — the most prominent heading is 'Command Palette' from the search dialog. Strong bones, weak hierarchy and unfinished states.*

**Keep.** Five-card KPI strip gives a scannable top-of-page pulse with consistent iconography and unit subtext ('38,185 live units', '41 open invoices').; Cash Position panel does the hard work of showing Cash on Hand → Scheduled Payables → Available After Bills as a connected story with a red callout, which is exactly the owner's decision framing.; Per-widget error/empty boundaries are respected — the Appointments card degrades to a proper illustrated empty state ('No upcoming appointments') instead of a blank tile.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `dashboard-UX-1` | **P0** | **'Today at a Glance' is stuck on skeleton bars with no resolution** — The 'Today at a Glance' card renders three gray placeholder bars below 'Sales, cash, and inbox signals for your morning review.' with no copy, no data, and no empty state. It looks identical to a permanent loading state. | Give OwnerQuickCardsWidget a real empty-state copy block ('No signals needing attention — nice.') with a muted icon and a secondary 'Open Notifications' link, matching the Appointments card's treatment. If the widget is still fetching, replace bars with a single spinner + label 'Loading today's signals…' so loading is distinguishable from empty. | OwnerQuickCardsWidget and its ComponentErrorBoundary stay intact — only the loading/empty render path is replaced; the drill-through 'Open Notifications' link and data contract are untouched. |
| `dashboard-UX-2` | **P1** | **The cash shortfall — the single most important signal — is buried** — 'You're short $551,981.62 after scheduled bills.' sits inside the right-hand Cash Position card, visually equivalent to the Appointments empty state next to it. The KPI strip above it shows CASH COLLECTED (7D) $0 with no link to this shortfall. | Add a full-width, dismissable alert row immediately under the header when Available After Bills < 0: red-tinted bar reading 'Cash short $551,981.62 after scheduled bills — review $551,981.62 in payables' with 'Review Bills' + 'Pay Bills' buttons. Keep the Cash Position card below exactly as-is for the full breakdown. | OwnerCashDecisionPanel and its Review Bills / Manage links remain; the banner is a new surface that reads from the same computed value, so no tRPC or business logic changes. |
| `dashboard-UX-3` | **P1** | **Top KPIs have no trend or comparison, so numbers are uninterpretable** — Four of the five KPI cards (OPEN ORDERS 511, FULFILLED TODAY 0, OUTSTANDING RECEIVABLES $963,104, INVENTORY VALUE $34.2M) show only a number and a supporting unit. Only CASH COLLECTED (7D) carries a comparison, and even that one renders the awkward '— N/A vs last week'. | Add a single-line delta under every KPI subtext: '▲ 14 vs yesterday', '▼ $42K vs 7d avg', etc. For FULFILLED TODAY 0 show '0 of 511 open — behind typical 09:00 pace'. Replace '— N/A vs last week' with 'First week of tracking' when the comparator is null. | OperationalKpisWidget (TER-1055) and its drill-through links to filtered workspaces are untouched; this is a subtext addition sourced from the same data the widget already renders. |
| `dashboard-UX-4` | **P1** | **Left nav duplicates itself between 'SALES QUICK ACTIONS' and 'SELL'** — The sidebar shows SALES QUICK ACTIONS (New Order, Active Orders, Sales Catalogue, Recent Customers, Today's Shipments) stacked directly above a SELL group (Sales, Demand & Supply, Leaderboard). A user looking for 'create order' has two plausible homes. | Keep QUICK ACTIONS but move it to a compact 2-column icon grid pinned at the top, above the section list, labeled 'Quick actions' (sentence case). Inside SELL, surface Sales, Demand & Supply, Leaderboard as-is. Do not delete any link — same five quick-action targets, just visually separated as shortcuts rather than a parallel taxonomy. | All five quick-action routes (New Order, Active Orders, Sales Catalogue, Recent Customers, Today's Shipments) and all three SELL children remain navigable; only visual grouping changes. |
| `dashboard-UX-5` | **P2** | **Page has no H1; screen readers and page-title scanners see 'Command Palette'** — Playwright reports H1: [] and the only H2 is 'Command Palette'. The visible 'OWNER COMMAND CENTER' is a styled badge, not a heading element. | Promote 'Owner Command Center' to an <h1> rendered to the left of the badge styling (visually the badge can remain), and demote the date subhead to <p>. Add an aria-live region around the 'Live · Updated 12:08 PM' chip so refreshes are announced. | The OWNER COMMAND CENTER badge component and the 'Live · Updated HH:MM' freshness indicator both keep their current behavior and styling; only the underlying semantic tag changes. |
| `dashboard-UX-6` | **P2** | **'Live · Updated 12:08 PM' freshness signal is too quiet and ambiguous** — The freshness chip sits at the far right edge of the header row in thin gray text. There is no indication of refresh cadence, whether it auto-refreshes, or how to force a refresh. Cash Position separately shows 'Updated 04/23 12:08 PM' in its own footer — two clocks, no hierarchy. | Move the freshness chip immediately under the H1, styled as 'Live • updated 12:08 PM • refreshes every 60s' with a small ⟳ icon button that manually refreshes. Remove the duplicate 'Updated 04/23 12:08 PM' line inside Cash Position; rely on the page-level chip. | The per-widget data refetch on mount (OwnerCashDecisionPanel etc.) is untouched; the manual refresh button invokes the same existing queries. |
| `dashboard-UX-7` | **P2** | **Empty-state copy is inconsistent between KPI cards** — FULFILLED TODAY 0 gets warm copy 'Nothing shipped yet'. CASH COLLECTED (7D) $0 gets the technical 'Last week $0 — N/A vs last week'. The two tell the same story ('no data to compare yet') in different voices. | Standardize: when the primary value is 0 and there is no comparator, render '<friendly copy> — <helpful next step or context>'. E.g., 'No cash collected this week yet', 'First 7 days of tracking'. Strip the em-dash '—' arrow glyph when the delta is unknowable. | OperationalKpisWidget's value computation is untouched; only the empty/zero-state string template changes. |
| `dashboard-UX-8` | **P2** | **Floating action button (bottom right) and 'Pay Bills' / 'Review Bills' / 'View Clients' actions compete without hierarchy** — There is an unlabeled orange circular FAB in the bottom-right corner, plus 'Review Bills →', 'Pay Bills', 'View Clients →', 'Manage →', and 'View all →' scattered across the same fold. The FAB has no tooltip visible and no clear relationship to the page. | Give the FAB a visible tooltip and icon-meaning on hover (e.g., 'New order'). Demote secondary card links ('View all', 'Manage', 'View Clients') to tertiary styling (muted, no arrow glyph). Keep 'Review Bills' as the only primary-styled in-card CTA since it's tied to the cash shortfall narrative. | Every drill-through link named in the baseline (per-widget drill-through and the FAB action) continues to route to the same destination; only weight/tooltip changes. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row: <h1>Owner Command Center</h1> with OWNER COMMAND CENTER pill inline, subhead 'Thursday, Apr 23 — here's what needs your attention today', freshness meta on the next line ('Live • updated 12:08 PM • auto-refreshes every 60s ⟳'). Immediately below, a conditional full-width red alert banner when Available After Bills < 0: 'Cash short $551,981.62 after scheduled bills' with [Review Bills] [Pay Bills] buttons right-aligned. Then the existing five-card KPI strip, each card upgraded with a delta line ('▲ 14 vs yesterday' or 'First week of tracking' when null). Row 3 — three equal columns: Today at a Glance (with real empty-state copy and an icon, not skeleton bars) · Appointments (unchanged) · Cash Position (unchanged, but drop its duplicate 'Updated…' footer since freshness is now in the header). Row 4 — Money In vs. Out · Suppliers Waiting to Be Paid (unchanged). Row 5 — Inventory Snapshot · Aging Inventory. Row 6 — collapsed OwnerSkuStatusBrowserWidget. Left nav: pin a compact 'Quick actions' icon grid (New Order, Active Orders, Sales Catalogue, Recent Customers, Today's Shipments) above the section list, then SELL / BUY / OPERATIONS / RELATIONSHIPS / FINANCE / ADMIN as consistent collapsible groups. Microcopy rules: use sentence case for all card CTAs, reserve primary button styling for Review Bills only, standardize zero/empty states to friendly + actionable ('No cash collected this week yet' instead of '$0 — N/A vs last week').

---

### Sales & Demand

#### OrderCreatorPage — `/sales?tab=create-order` (full)

![OrderCreatorPage](screenshots_all/sales_create_order.png)

*The page presents a clean, low-density working frame with the correct structural bones — header, tab rail, saved indicator, totals row, empty state, keyboard-hint footer — but it squanders its opening move. The first screen the rep lands on answers almost none of the questions a seller actually has: Who am I selling to? Is this a quote or a sale? Can they buy on credit? What's the fastest path to add my first line? The empty state uses a warning triangle (which looks like an error), the tab row collides with itself at 'Sales Catalogues/Live Shopping/New Order', the H1 still says 'Sales' so the breadcrumb and page context never reflect the actual task ('New Order'), and the instructional line 'KEEP THE CUSTOMER, DOCUMENT TYPE, AND TOTALS IN ONE WORKING FRAME' is meta-designer copy, not seller copy. The document-type selector ('Sales Order') and the customer picker are floated top-right, disconnected from the empty state's 'Choose a customer above' sentence, so the eye has to zigzag. The keyboard hints in the footer and the left 'Sales Quick Actions' rail are both real strengths that a redesign should protect.*

**Keep.** Persistent keyboard-hint footer (Ctrl+S save draft · Ctrl+Enter finalize · Ctrl+Z undo in grid) teaches the grid-style workflow without a modal.; Left 'Sales Quick Actions' rail (New Order, Active Orders, Sales Catalogue, Recent Customers, Today's Shipments) gives reps a fast re-entry point without leaving the workspace.; Status chips 'Saved' and '0 lines · synced' establish trust that the draft/autosave loop is actually running.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `sales_create_order-UX-1` | **P1** | **Tab row collides: 'Sales Catalogues' / 'Live Shopping' / 'New Order' visually overlap** — In the tab strip under the 'Sales' H1, the labels 'Sales Catalogues' and 'Live Shopping' are touching, and 'Live Shopping' butts directly into the active 'New Order' pill with no gutter. Tabs appear to use fixed-width columns that the longer labels have outgrown. | Switch the tab container from fixed equal-width columns to content-width with a consistent 16–24px gutter, left-align the strip, and allow it to horizontally scroll on narrow viewports. Keep the same seven tabs in the same order. | All seven tabs from the Sales Workspace router (Orders, Pick List, Quotes, Returns, Sales Catalogues, Live Shopping, New Order) remain present and clickable; only their layout math changes. |
| `sales_create_order-UX-2` | **P1** | **Empty state uses an error icon for routine guidance** — The center empty state uses a yellow/amber warning triangle with an exclamation mark above the copy 'Select a customer to start this order'. Nothing is wrong — this is the normal starting state of a new draft. | Replace the warning triangle with a neutral illustration or a user/customer silhouette icon, and add a primary button 'Choose customer' that focuses the `ClientCombobox` (keyboard shortcut hint: C). Keep the headline and subcopy, tighten to 'Pick a customer to begin' / 'Add batches, pricing, and totals without leaving this workspace.' | The empty state still gates on customer selection before `InventoryBrowser` / `LineItemTable` activate; we only change the icon and add a focus-forwarding CTA, no change to `ClientCombobox` behavior. |
| `sales_create_order-UX-3` | **P1** | **Customer and document-type controls float top-right, disconnected from the empty-state instruction** — The empty state says 'Choose a customer above to begin a new order', but the 'Customer…' combobox and the 'Sales Order' document-type dropdown are small, unlabeled controls pinned to the top-right of the work-surface header, 800+ px away from the instruction text. Neither has a visible label — the rep has to infer what the 'Sales Order' dropdown toggles. | Promote the empty state into a centered 'Start' card that contains: (1) a full-width `ClientCombobox` labeled 'Customer', (2) a segmented control 'Sale / Quote' wired to the existing `mode=quote` URL flag, (3) a 'Start order' primary button. Keep the compact header versions as secondary controls for later edits once a customer is chosen. | `ClientCombobox`, `QuickCreateClient`, and the SALE-vs-QUOTE toggle driven by the `mode=quote` URL flag all stay; they are simply surfaced in the first-use card instead of the header corner. |
| `sales_create_order-UX-4` | **P2** | **H1 and breadcrumb say 'Sales', never 'New Order'** — The breadcrumb trail reads 'Home › Sales' and the H1 is 'Sales'. The only indicator that the user is on the order-creation surface is a small 'New order' caption next to the 'Queue' button. | Keep H1 as 'Sales' but append a live sub-H1 rendered next to the 'Saved' chip — e.g., 'New order · Draft' (or 'New quote · Draft' when `mode=quote`), and update `document.title` to 'New order — TERP' / 'New quote — TERP'. Add the draft short-id once the first save returns from `orders.draft`. | Sales Workspace H1 and tab structure are untouched; we only enrich the page title string and add a live sub-heading sourced from the existing `mode` param and `orders.draft` response. |
| `sales_create_order-UX-5` | **P2** | **All-caps meta copy 'KEEP THE CUSTOMER, DOCUMENT TYPE, AND TOTALS IN ONE WORKING FRAME' is designer talk, not seller talk** — Below the 'Saved' pill sits an ALL-CAPS line describing the layout philosophy of the page itself. It doesn't tell the rep what to do, and capitalized sentence-case English is harder to scan. | Replace this line with task-focused dynamic copy: before customer selected → 'Pick a customer to load pricing, credit, and recent batches.' After selection → show the `ClientCommitContextCard` summary here (commit context + credit headline). Use sentence case, regular weight. | `ClientCommitContextCard`, `CreditLimitBanner`, and `CreditStatusCard` all render here post-selection; we're only reclaiming the strip and binding its content to existing context providers. |
| `sales_create_order-UX-6` | **P2** | **'Queue' button with left-arrow reads as 'back' but is labeled 'Queue'** — At the top-left of the work surface sits a button with a leftward chevron and the text 'Queue'. Its affordance (back-arrow icon) contradicts its label (a noun). There is no tooltip and no secondary caption. | Split affordances: keep a distinct back-arrow icon button that returns to the 'Orders' tab with tooltip 'Back to orders list', and change the 'Queue' control to a pill-button labeled 'Draft queue (N)' where N is the count of in-flight drafts from `orders.*` — clicking it opens the queue popover. | The draft queue behavior (autosave drafts list) and the back navigation into `SalesOrderSurface` are both kept; we only separate them visually and add the count from existing draft data. |
| `sales_create_order-UX-7` | **P2** | **'Saved' indicator is green before the user has entered anything to save** — The green check + 'Saved' pill is already lit on an empty, never-touched draft, and the footer shows '0 lines · synced'. | Introduce three explicit states for the save chip: 'New draft' (neutral gray, no icon, shown until the first mutation), 'Saving…' (spinner), 'Saved · HH:MM' (green check with timestamp). Drive from the debounced draft mutation's pending/success states already in `orders.*`. | Debounced autosave via `orders.draft` is unchanged; we only remap its three states to three distinct visual treatments on the same chip. |
| `sales_create_order-UX-8` | **P2** | **Bottom-right floating action button is unlabeled** — A small circular icon-only FAB sits in the bottom-right corner of the work surface with no label, tooltip text visible, or caption. | Give the FAB a visible label on hover and on first render (e.g., 'Preview document' or 'Order summary'), move it to the right edge of the `WorkSurfaceStatusBar` as a labeled button, and key it to the existing hotkey (add to `KeyboardHintBar` if absent). | `FloatingOrderPreview` / summary panel toggle behavior is unchanged; we only relabel and re-anchor the trigger. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header stays: breadcrumb 'Home › Sales', H1 'Sales', tab rail with content-width tabs and 20px gutters. Immediately below the active 'New Order' tab, a two-line document bar: line 1 = 'New order · Draft #12043' (or 'New quote · Draft'), live save chip ('New draft' / 'Saving…' / 'Saved 10:42'), and a 'Draft queue (3)' pill on the left where 'Queue' used to be. Line 2 = dynamic context strip — before customer: muted sentence-case helper 'Pick a customer to load pricing, credit, and recent batches.'; after customer: `ClientCommitContextCard` summary + `CreditLimitBanner` inline headline. Primary body is a centered 'Start order' card while no customer is selected: large `ClientCombobox` with 'Customer' label, a 'Sale / Quote' segmented control bound to the `mode=quote` URL flag, a 'Recent customers' 3-chip row, and a 'Start order' primary button (Enter). Once customer + doc-type are chosen, the card collapses into the header and the work surface expands to: left 70% = `LineItemTable` / `OrdersDocumentLineItemsGrid` with inline `InventoryBrowser` add-row and keyboard-first editing; right 30% = sticky side-rail stacking `CreditStatusCard`, `PricingContextPanel`, `OrderAdjustmentPanel`, `OrderTotalsPanel`, `ReferredBySelector`. Replace the warning triangle in the empty-grid row with a neutral 'Add your first line (press A)' hint. Footer `KeyboardHintBar` stays pinned with Ctrl+S save draft · Ctrl+Enter finalize · Ctrl+Z undo, and gets a new 'Space · Preview document' entry so the unlabeled FAB becomes a labeled 'Preview' button at the right of the `WorkSurfaceStatusBar`.

#### LiveShoppingPage (staff) — `/sales?tab=live-shopping` (lightweight)

![LiveShoppingPage (staff)](screenshots_all/sales_live_shopping.png)

*The page gives a clean overview of live shopping sessions with four KPI tiles and a sessions table, but it reads like a dashboard for a feature that barely has any data. The Sessions table has only seven columns of which one (Items) shows 0 and another (Status) duplicates the KPI tiles, while the single Active session buries its most important affordance — actually joining/driving the live room — behind a generic 'View Details' link. The tab chip for 'Live Shopping' is also visually indistinguishable from the other sales tabs, so users landing here don't immediately grok that the active state is selected. KPI math (Total Sessions = 1, Active = 1, Converted = 0) is internally consistent but the tiles are static and not filterable.*

**Keep.** KPI strip (Active / Scheduled / Total / Converted) gives a usable at-a-glance status of the live shopping program.; 'New Session' primary CTA is correctly placed top-right and visually distinct in the TERP orange.; Sessions table cleanly surfaces Status, Title, Client, Host, Items, Date in a conventional ERP layout.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `sales_live_shopping-UX-1` | **P1** | **Active session has no direct 'Join/Enter Room' action** — The only action on the single Active session row is a generic 'View Details' link. For a live, time-sensitive workflow there is no visible room code, no join button, and no indication of how a staff host resumes or enters the session. | In the Actions column, when Status=Active, render a primary 'Enter Room' button alongside 'View Details', and show the room code as a monospace chip in the Title/Host cell. Keep 'View Details' for non-active rows. | Does not alter the `vipPortalLiveShopping.joinByRoomCode` contract or the LiveShoppingSession three-status workflow; the new button simply routes to the existing session detail/room route that View Details already opens. |
| `sales_live_shopping-UX-2` | **P2** | **Selected tab 'Live Shopping' is not visually distinguished** — All seven Sales tabs (Orders, Pick List, Quotes, Returns, Sales Catalogues, Live Shopping, New Order) render with identical styling; the active 'Live Shopping' tab only shows a faint outline, and 'New Order' — which is an action, not a sibling view — is styled as just another tab. | Give the active tab a filled background + bold label matching TERP's design token for selected chips, and visually separate 'New Order' as a secondary button to the right of the tab row (or move it next to 'New Session' in the page header). | Tabs and the New Order entry point are layout-only; no change to the Sales tab routing (`tab=live-shopping` etc.) or to the New Order flow. |
| `sales_live_shopping-UX-3` | **P2** | **KPI tiles are decorative, not interactive** — The four KPI cards (Active Sessions 1, Scheduled 0, Total 1, Converted 0) are static — clicking them does nothing, and the Sessions table below has its own separate 'All Statuses' filter. | Make each KPI tile a toggle that sets the Sessions table filter (Active / Scheduled / All / Converted). Show a subtle selected state on the active tile and sync it with the 'All Statuses' dropdown. | The underlying Sessions query and the existing status dropdown remain; the tiles become a shortcut control that writes to the same filter state the dropdown already drives. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: 'Live Shopping' H1 with subtitle, right-aligned primary 'New Session' button. Move 'New Order' out of the tab row and into a secondary button beside 'New Session'; restyle the Sales tab row so the active chip has a filled background. KPI strip stays as four tiles but becomes a segmented filter bar — clicking 'Active Sessions' filters the table and highlights the tile, with the 'All Statuses' dropdown reflecting the same state. Sessions table gains a 'Room Code' column (monospace chip) and an Actions column that renders a primary 'Enter Room' button for Active rows, 'Start' for Scheduled rows, and 'View Details' for Ended/Converted rows. Empty state for the table reads 'No sessions yet — start a Live Shopping session with a client' with an inline New Session CTA.

#### ShippingPickListPage — `/sales?tab=pick-list` (lightweight)

![ShippingPickListPage](screenshots_all/sales_pick_list.png)

*The page gets the fundamentals right: a dense warehouse-style table, a clear title with subtitle announcing '500 orders, 2311 line items', and a prominent truncation warning. But it fails as a pick list in practice. The baseline promises date, batch, location, picker columns — none are visible. Continuation rows (the SKU-00000002 rows with no Order or Client cells) create ambiguity about which order a line belongs to. Status badges dominate the right edge but there's no bulk action to mark PENDING→PACKED from the list, forcing a row-by-row drilldown. Density is fine, but information architecture is wrong for a warehouse operator scanning a 2311-line queue.*

**Keep.** Explicit truncation banner ('Showing first 500 results — use filters to narrow results') keeps operators from trusting a partial list.; Subtitle surfaces both order count and line-item count, which is the correct unit of work for picking.; Status filter defaults to 'All open', which matches the operator's default intent.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `sales_pick_list-UX-1` | **P1** | **Continuation line-item rows lose their order context** — Rows for SKU-00000002 ('Licensed Pre-Roll - cutover') appear repeatedly with blank Order and Client cells because they're secondary lines of the order above. A picker scanning mid-table can't tell which order a line belongs to without counting upward. | Either (a) repeat the order number and client on every line with muted typography for continuation rows, or (b) group lines under a sticky order header row that shows order #, client, date, and a line count (e.g., 'S-1772839406310 · Sunset Dispensary · 2 lines'). Keep the flat row model for CSV but repeat order/client values in the export. | Preserves `orders.getPickList` response shape and the documented columns (order, client, line items); only the rendering groups/repeats values. |
| `sales_pick_list-UX-2` | **P1** | **Baseline columns date, batch, location, picker are missing from the table** — FUNCTIONAL_BASELINE specifies rows include date, batch + qty, location, and picker. The rendered table shows only Order, Client, SKU, Product, Qty, Unit, Status. A warehouse picker cannot route themselves without bin location, cannot pick FIFO without batch, and cannot see due date for prioritization. | Add Location (bin), Batch, and Due Date columns. Default sort by Location ascending so the physical pick path is already ordered. Make Picker a compact avatar column on the right, assignable inline. If horizontal space is tight, collapse Unit into Qty ('1 LB'). | Uses fields already returned by `orders.getPickList` (baseline lists batch + qty, location, picker); this is a rendering change only, no router changes. |
| `sales_pick_list-UX-3` | **P2** | **No bulk status action; PENDING→PACKED requires leaving the list** — Every non-PACKED row shows a passive PENDING badge with no affordance to mark packed. There's no row checkbox, no bulk selector, and Export CSV is the only primary action. | Add a leading checkbox column with a select-all in the header. When one or more rows are selected, swap the Export CSV header zone for a sticky action bar: 'Mark packed', 'Assign picker', 'Print pick ticket'. Keep Export CSV accessible in an overflow menu. | No baseline behavior removed — CSV export stays, status mutation already exists per order; bulk action just batches existing mutations without introducing new routers beyond what status transitions already require. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: 'Shipping Pick List' H1 with subtitle '500 orders · 2,311 lines · 1,842 pending'. Right-aligned: primary 'Print pick sheet', secondary 'Export CSV'. Filter bar on one row: Status chip group (All open / Pending / Partial / Fulfilled), Date range, Warehouse, Picker, Client typeahead, Reset. Truncation banner kept as-is. Table grouped by order with a sticky muted header row: 'S-1772839406310 · Sunset Dispensary · Due Oct 14 · 2 lines · [Assign picker]'. Line rows beneath show: [checkbox] · Location (bin) · SKU · Product · Batch · Qty+Unit · Status. Default sort: Location asc, then Order. Selecting rows reveals a sticky bottom action bar: 'N lines selected — Mark packed · Assign picker · Print tickets · Clear'. Status column uses color only for exceptions (partial = amber, pending = neutral outline, packed = green solid) so packed rows visually recede as the operator works the list down.

#### SalesWorkspacePage.quotes — `/sales?tab=quotes` (lightweight)

![SalesWorkspacePage.quotes](screenshots_all/sales_quotes.png)

*The Quotes sub-tab is functionally legible — tabs, filter, and a clean table with consistent columns — but it fails on its two most important jobs: telling the user the state of their quote pipeline, and distinguishing quotes from orders. The status strip reports Unsent/Sent/Converted all as 0 despite every visible row being DRAFT, and every quote number is prefixed 'ORD-' which will collide cognitively with the Orders tab one click away. There is also a redundant double H1 ('Sales' shell title + 'Sales Quotes' page title) and a search placeholder that claims the Cmd+K shortcut already owned by the global command palette.*

**Keep.** Column set (Quote #, Client, Created, Valid Until, Status, Total) is the right minimum for a quote queue and the row hierarchy is calm.; Status pipeline summary (Saved / Unsent / Sent / Converted) in the header is the correct mental model — it just needs to be accurate.; Mode toggle (Spreadsheet View / Standard View) and the 'New Quote' CTA are right where a sales rep expects them.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `sales_quotes-UX-1` | **P1** | **Pipeline counters omit Draft and contradict the visible table** — The header strip shows 'Saved / Unsent: 0 / Sent: 0 / Converted: 0' while every one of the ~11 visible rows carries a DRAFT badge. There is no Draft count and the zeros make the pipeline look empty when it is not. | Add a leading 'Draft: N' counter before Unsent, and make each counter a filter chip that sets the status filter. Replace the ambiguous green 'Saved' pill with a neutral 'All: N' total. Drive counts from the same `quotes.list` payload that renders the table so they can never diverge. | QuotesWorkSurface continues to consume `quotes.*` tRPC output; the fix only re-maps existing status buckets into the header strip and reuses the existing 'All Statuses' filter behavior. |
| `sales_quotes-UX-2` | **P1** | **Quote rows use an 'ORD-' prefix, indistinguishable from orders** — Every row in the Quote # column reads 'ORD-000378', 'ORD-000370', etc. The Orders tab sits one click to the left and uses the same prefix pattern. | Display the quote identifier with a `QUO-` (or `Q-`) visual prefix in this column while keeping the underlying stored id unchanged — render as `QUO-000378` with the numeric tail preserved. If backend ids truly are shared with orders, add a small 'Quote' tag next to the number so the row is self-identifying when copy-pasted out of context. | Does not touch the `quotes.*` router or the stored order/quote id scheme — purely a column renderer change inside QuotesWorkSurface, so `quoteId` deep-links and conversion flows keep working. |
| `sales_quotes-UX-3` | **P2** | **Duplicate H1 and a search placeholder that squats the global Cmd+K** — The page renders two H1s ('Sales' from `LinearWorkspaceShell` and 'Sales Quotes' from the surface), and the in-table search input shows placeholder 'Search quotes… (Cmd+K)' — but Cmd+K is already bound to the global command palette (visible top bar). | Demote 'Sales Quotes' to an H2 (or drop it and let the shell title carry 'Sales › Quotes'), and tighten the subtitle row so the counters sit on the same line as the title. Change the search placeholder to 'Search quotes by #, client, or total' and remove the '(Cmd+K)' hint; if a local shortcut is desired, bind '/' and label it '(/)'. | LinearWorkspaceShell title/meta-strip API is untouched; only the QuotesWorkSurface internal header markup and input placeholder string change, preserving the `quotes.list` search behavior. |

**Redesign sketch.** One H1 from the shell: 'Sales', breadcrumb 'Sell › Sales › Quotes'. Below it, a single dense header row: left side shows 'Quotes' with a muted total (e.g., '24 quotes') and four clickable status chips (Draft 11 · Sent 6 · Accepted 4 · Expired 3) that drive the status filter; right side holds Spreadsheet/Standard toggle and a primary 'New Quote' button. Filter bar beneath: search input ('Search quotes by #, client, or total'), status select, and a Valid-Until date range. Table columns unchanged but Quote # renders as 'QUO-000378' with a subtle 'Quote' tag, Valid Until cells turn amber when <7 days and red when past, and the trailing chevron opens a right drawer with Convert-to-Order / Duplicate / Send actions so the queue stays keyboard-navigable.

#### ReturnsPage — `/sales?tab=returns` (lightweight)

![ReturnsPage](screenshots_all/sales_returns.png)

*The page delivers the core RMA surface — three KPI cards, a Process Return CTA, and a returns table — but it reads as a lightly-dressed prototype rather than a working queue. The Return Reasons card is a dead text block when it could be a filter, the table is missing the key operational columns (item, qty, state-machine status, customer) that an RMA manager needs to triage, and the state machine (Draft → Received → Inspected → Restocked/Disposed → Closed) documented in the baseline is completely absent from the UI. The Process Return button floating above an otherwise unstyled table also creates a weak hierarchy compared to the header block above.*

**Keep.** KPI cards up top (Total Returns, Defective Items, Return Reasons) frame the queue's shape at a glance.; GL Status column with a direct View GL link preserves the ReturnGLStatus integration inline with each row.; Clear, labeled primary action (Process Return) with a sensible orange accent that matches the rest of Sales.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `sales_returns-UX-1` | **P1** | **Returns table is missing the workflow state and line-item context** — The table shows Return ID, Order ID, Reason, Processed By, Processed At, Notes, GL Status — but no Customer, no SKU/qty, and critically no current state (Draft/Received/Inspected/Restocked/Disposed/Closed). An RMA manager cannot triage what needs inspection or restocking from this view. | Insert a Status column (pill) between Order ID and Reason, and add a Customer column after Order ID. Also surface item count (e.g. '2 items · 5 units') either as a column or under the Order ID. Keep all existing columns. | Uses the existing `returns.*` tRPC state field and the baseline state machine enum; purely additive columns, no removal. |
| `sales_returns-UX-2` | **P2** | **Return Reasons card is static text instead of a filter** — The Return Reasons card lists 'Wrong Item: 0, Not As Described: 0, Changed Mind: 0, Other: 0' as plain text, next to a Defective Items KPI that is essentially the same dimension split off. Clicking any row does nothing, and the Reason column in the table is not filterable. | Make each reason line a toggleable filter chip that filters the table by that enum value; merge the Defective KPI into the same card as the selected/primary chip. Add an 'All' chip as the default. Keep the underlying counts. | Filters client-side off the existing return reason enum from `returns.*`; no API or enum changes. |
| `sales_returns-UX-3` | **P2** | **Process Return CTA is orphaned above the table with no empty/onboarding affordance** — The Process Return button sits alone on a line above the table header, separated from the page H1 by the KPI row. With only one row in the table there is a large dead zone below, and no hint that Process Return is how you create an RMA against a sold order. | Move Process Return into the page header row next to Standard/Spreadsheet View as the primary (filled) button, and add a one-line helper under it: 'Start an RMA from a sold order.' Keep a secondary Process Return CTA in the table's empty state for discoverability. | Unchanged `returns.*` create dialog trigger — only the button's position and a helper string change. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row: H1 'Returns' left, subtitle 'Process and track order returns', with [Process Return] (primary) + [Spreadsheet / Standard] view toggle right-aligned. Below: three-up KPI strip — (1) Open Returns with sub-counts by state (Draft/Received/Inspected), (2) Awaiting GL Reversal, (3) Reason breakdown rendered as clickable filter chips (Defective, Wrong Item, Not As Described, Changed Mind, Other) with counts. Below chips: a filters bar (Status, Reason, Date range, Customer search) bound to the table. Table columns: Return ID · Status pill · Order ID · Customer · Items (e.g. '2 × Purple Haze +1') · Reason · Processed By · Processed At · Notes (truncated) · GL Status (View GL link). Row click opens a side drawer with the full state-machine timeline and Restock/Dispose actions. Empty state: illustrated block with 'No returns yet — Process Return to start an RMA from a sold order.'

#### SalesWorkspacePage.sales-sheets — `/sales?tab=sales-sheets` (lightweight)

![SalesWorkspacePage.sales-sheets](screenshots_all/sales_sheets.png)

Same three destination buttons, side-by-side, both active-looking even though no client is selected and no lines exist. | Collapse to one handoff row at the bottom (Share Link · → Sales Order · → Quote · Live) and replace the right card with a live checklist ('1. #### MatchmakingServicePage — `/demand-supply?tab=matchmaking` (full)

![MatchmakingServicePage](screenshots_all/demand_supply_match.png)

*The page tries to do three jobs at once — summarize KPIs, browse needs/supply, and surface suggested matches — and ends up wasting the viewport on redundancy. The four KPI cards restate the exact counts already shown in the column headers (Active Needs 0 / Client Needs (0), Available Supply 12 / Supplier Supply (12), Suggested Matches 0/0), so the top third of the screen adds no information. The matching workflow itself is under-supported: there is no visible 'compute matches' action, no last-updated timestamp, no way to dismiss or override a match per the baseline, and the two empty columns are dead-end 'No X found' states with no CTA despite the fact that Add Need/Add Supply live 300px away at the top. Two right-aligned links ('Open Matchmaking', 'Jump to Supplier Supply') duplicate the tab navigation and muddy the mental model. The supplier cards themselves are reasonably scannable, but 'Urgent Needs 0' rendered in red is semantically wrong and 'Supplier: Unknown supplier' is a data leak the UI should absorb.*

**Keep.** Supplier supply cards pack strain, category, grade, weight and price into one compact, scannable block with clear Available status.; Primary action hierarchy on the header is correct: Add Need is the filled/primary button reflecting the page's supply-heavy, needs-starved state.; Search + Active/Priority filters and the four-tab structure give a single predictable entry point for the whole Demand & Supply surface.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `demand_supply_match-UX-1` | **P1** | **KPI strip duplicates the column headers directly below it** — The four cards 'Active Needs 0 / 0 with matches', 'Available Supply 12 / 0 with buyers', 'Suggested Matches 0 / 0 high confidence', 'Urgent Needs 0' repeat the counts already shown in 'Client Needs (0)', 'Supplier Supply (12)', 'Suggested Matches (0)' sitting one row below. The KPI row consumes ~120px of prime viewport without adding new data. | Collapse the KPI strip into the column headers: 'Client Needs · 0 total · 0 matched', 'Supplier Supply · 12 total · 0 with buyers', 'Suggested Matches · 0 · 0 high-confidence'. Move 'Urgent Needs' into a small amber/red pill on the Client Needs header only when the count is >0. Reclaim the vertical space for a fourth row of supply cards. | All four metrics (Active Needs, Available Supply, Suggested Matches, Urgent Needs) remain visible as inline counters on each column header; no counter is removed and the underlying `matching.*`, `clientNeeds.*`, `vendorSupply.*` queries are unchanged. |
| `demand_supply_match-UX-2` | **P1** | **No 'Compute/Update Matches' control surfaces the core action of the page** — The baseline explicitly lists 'compute/update matches' and 'override match' / 'dismiss' as page actions, but the only buttons visible are Add Need, Add Supply, View Buyers, and Reserve. There is no trigger, status, or last-run timestamp for the matching engine itself. | Add a 'Recompute matches' split-button in the Suggested Matches column header with a subtitle like 'Last run 4m ago · 12 supply × 0 needs evaluated'. When matches exist, each match row exposes a kebab with Override and Dismiss, mapping 1:1 to the baseline actions. | Directly exposes the `matching.compute`/`matching.update`, override, and dismiss routes named in the baseline; no existing action is removed, only surfaced. |
| `demand_supply_match-UX-3` | **P1** | **Empty Client Needs and Suggested Matches columns are dead-ends** — Both 'Client Needs (0)' and 'Suggested Matches (0)' render only the text 'No client needs found' / 'No matches found'. There is no in-column CTA, no explanation of what unblocks matches (needs must exist first), and no link to the 'Add Need' button 300px above. | In the Client Needs empty state: headline 'No active client needs', body 'Add a client need to start matching against your 12 available supply lots.', with a filled 'Add Need' button right there. In the Suggested Matches empty state: 'Matches appear here once you have at least one active client need' with a secondary link 'Add a need →' that scrolls/focuses the Client Needs column. | Reuses the same `clientNeeds.create` flow already bound to the top 'Add Need' button; no new behavior, just a second entry point. |
| `demand_supply_match-UX-4` | **P2** | **'Urgent Needs 0' is rendered in red** — The fourth KPI card shows the label 'Urgent Needs', value '0', and subtitle 'Requires immediate attention' — all colored red — even though zero urgent needs is the healthy state. | Color the Urgent Needs number red only when count > 0; render 0 in the same neutral ink as the other cards and drop the 'Requires immediate attention' subtitle to 'All clear' when 0. Assuming UX-1 is adopted, fold this into an amber/red pill on the Client Needs header that only appears above zero. | The Urgent Needs metric (derived from `clientNeeds` priority field) is still displayed; only its visual treatment becomes state-sensitive. |
| `demand_supply_match-UX-5` | **P2** | **'Open Matchmaking' and 'Jump to Supplier Supply' duplicate the tab bar** — Directly to the right of the tabs 'Matchmaking \| Client Needs \| Interest List \| Supplier Supply' sit two buttons: 'Open Matchmaking' (while the Matchmaking tab is already active) and 'Jump to Supplier Supply' (which appears to duplicate the tab). | Remove the buttons from the tab row and relocate their targets: if 'Open Matchmaking' opens a full-screen matchmaking workspace distinct from this tab, rename it to 'Open full workspace' and move it to the Suggested Matches column header; if 'Jump to Supplier Supply' deep-links into the supplier catalogue, rename to 'View full catalogue →' and place it inline on the Supplier Supply column header. | Both navigation targets remain reachable — the links are relocated and relabeled, not removed — and the underlying route handlers (tab switch + full-workspace entry) are untouched. |
| `demand_supply_match-UX-6` | **P2** | **Reserve button's muted-tan fill is ambiguous** — On each supplier card, 'View Buyers' is rendered as a standard outlined button and 'Reserve' is a filled pale-tan pill that reads as neither primary nor secondary — lighter than the Add Need orange, darker than a ghost button. | Apply the same filled primary treatment used for Add Need to Reserve, and demote View Buyers to a ghost/text link. Alternatively, if Reserve is destructive-adjacent (locks inventory), keep the tan but add an explicit secondary-action outline and a tooltip 'Hold 45.6100 lbs for up to 24h'. | The `vendorSupply.reserve` mutation and the View Buyers drill-in both remain; only their visual weight is corrected. |
| `demand_supply_match-UX-7` | **P2** | **'Supplier: Unknown supplier' leaks a null-state into the UI** — Both visible supplier cards (Blue Dream, Wedding Cake) render the literal string 'Supplier: Unknown supplier'. This is the raw fallback when the vendor relation is missing. | Replace the string with a subtle amber badge 'Supplier not linked' plus a 'Link supplier' inline action that opens the vendor picker against the existing `vendorSupply.update` route. Rows with a known supplier render normally. | Uses `vendorSupply.*` update to attach a supplier — no schema change — and keeps rows visible rather than filtering them out. |
| `demand_supply_match-UX-8` | **P2** | **Search and Active/All Priorities filter scope is not declared** — A single search box ('Search strain, category, client, supplier…') and two selects ('Active', 'All Priorities') sit above three columns, but there is no visual indication of which column each filter affects. 'All Priorities' is a client-need concept; 'Active' could be status for either need or supply. | Label the filter row 'Filter across all panels' and reflect the active filter as a chip on each column header ('Priority: All', 'Status: Active'). When a filter only applies to a subset (Priority → needs only), show the chip only on the affected column. Keep the same selects, just bind their effect visibly. | The existing filter state bound to `clientNeeds.list` / `vendorSupply.list` queries is unchanged; this is label and chip presentation only. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header unchanged: 'Demand & Supply' breadcrumb, tabs (Matchmaking | Client Needs | Interest List | Supplier Supply) — with the two orphan buttons removed from the tab row. Below the tabs, a single row: page title 'Matchmaking Service' with one-line subtitle on the left; 'Add Need' (primary) and 'Add Supply' (secondary) on the right. Next row: full-width search, then filter chips (Status: Active, Priority: All) that echo into each column header. Delete the four-card KPI strip entirely; its counts move inline into the column headers. Three-column workspace below: (1) 'Client Needs · 0 total · 0 matched' with empty-state headline 'No active client needs', body copy pointing to the matching engine dependency, and an in-column 'Add Need' button; urgent count renders as an amber pill only when >0. (2) 'Supplier Supply · 12 · 0 with buyers' with a right-aligned 'View full catalogue →' link and the existing card list; Reserve gets primary-filled treatment, View Buyers becomes a text link, missing suppliers show an amber 'Supplier not linked · Link' inline action. (3) 'Suggested Matches · 0 · 0 high-confidence' with a header-level 'Recompute matches' split-button showing 'Last run 4m ago'; empty state reads 'Matches appear once you have at least one active client need' with a secondary link that focuses column 1. Each future match row carries a score badge and a kebab exposing Override and Dismiss per the baseline. Net effect: one screen, zero redundant counters, every baseline action (add need, add supply, compute/update, open order, override, dismiss) reachable within one click from where the user is already looking.

Filter defaults are sensible, but the 'Status: Active' chip plus the 'Active' dropdown is redundant.*

Keep the trending/top-products stats from the baseline behind a 'Stats' disclosure or side panel. | The baseline 'stats (top products, trending categories)' feature stays — metrics are still computed from `clientNeeds.*` and displayed, just in a denser inline layout instead of four hero cards. |

The table/empty state fills the rest of the viewport; empty state keeps its illustration, 'No interest items' copy, and the 'Add Interest Item' button now visible without scrolling.

#### NeedsManagementPage — `/demand-supply?tab=needs` (lightweight)

![NeedsManagementPage](screenshots_all/demand_supply_needs.png)

*The page surfaces the right primitives — tabs for the four Demand & Supply surfaces, four KPI tiles, search + status/priority filters, a paginated list, and a Create Need CTA — but the hierarchy is confused. Two H1s ('Demand & Supply' and 'Needs Management') compete, the KPI tiles are all zero and consume the most valuable real estate above the empty state, and the empty state itself buries the one action the user can take. The redundant tab system ('Matchmaking/Client Needs/Interest List/Supplier Supply' sitting above 'All Needs/Smart Opportunities') creates four levels of navigation before the user reaches data. For a zero-state workspace this is too much chrome and too little guidance.*

**Keep.** KPI tiles (Active Needs, With Matches, Urgent, Opportunities) give at-a-glance pipeline health once populated; Cross-surface shortcuts ('Open Matchmaking', 'Jump to Supplier Supply') correctly treat needs as part of a larger matching workflow; Filters (search, status=Active default, All Priorities) match the baseline field model cleanly

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `demand_supply_needs-UX-1` | **P1** | **Empty state dead-ends instead of driving the primary action** — The 'No needs found' empty state shows only a package icon and the copy 'Try adjusting your filters or create a new need' with no button. The actual 'Create Need' CTA is ~500px away in the top-right corner, and the filter is silently defaulted to 'Active' which hides any FULFILLED/EXPIRED/CANCELLED needs that may exist. | Put two inline buttons inside the empty state card: a primary 'Create Need' and a secondary 'Clear filters' (only shown when filters are non-default). Change copy to 'No active needs. Create one to start matching, or view all statuses.' | Reuses the existing `clientNeeds.create` mutation behind 'Create Need' and the Active/All Priorities filter controls — no routes or fields change. |
| `demand_supply_needs-UX-2` | **P2** | **Four stacked navigation layers before the user sees a row** — From top to bottom the user crosses: breadcrumb → Matchmaking/Client Needs/Interest List/Supplier Supply tab row → 'Open Matchmaking / Jump to Supplier Supply' link row → 'All Needs (0) / Smart Opportunities (0)' sub-tabs. 'Jump to Supplier Supply' duplicates the 'Supplier Supply' tab already visible 40px above it. | Collapse the right-side 'Open Matchmaking' / 'Jump to Supplier Supply' link row into a single overflow button ('Go to… ▾') or move them next to Create Need as secondary-styled buttons. Keep the primary tab row and the All Needs/Smart Opportunities sub-tabs. | Both jump links remain reachable; only their presentation is consolidated. The `matching.*` routes they navigate to are untouched. |
| `demand_supply_needs-UX-3` | **P2** | **KPI tiles waste above-the-fold space with zeroes and no drill-through** — Four large tiles (Active Needs, With Matches, Urgent, Opportunities) each render a single '0' in ~120px of vertical space, are not clickable, and do not filter the list below. 'Opportunities' also duplicates the 'Smart Opportunities (0)' sub-tab. | Make each tile a filter chip: clicking 'Urgent' applies priority=URGENT to the list; 'With Matches' filters to needs with ≥1 match; 'Opportunities' routes to the Smart Opportunities sub-tab. Reduce tile height by ~30% and add a trend delta (e.g., '+2 this week') beneath the count. | Tile counts still read from the same `clientNeeds.*`/`matching.*` aggregates; click handlers only set existing filter state (priority, status, matches) already supported by the baseline Filter/search action. |

**Redesign sketch.** Single H1 'Client Needs' with a one-line subhead and the D&S tabs directly beneath it (demote 'Demand & Supply' to breadcrumb only). Right-aligned action cluster: primary 'Create Need', secondary overflow 'Go to ▾' (Matchmaking, Supplier Supply). Below: a slimmer 4-up KPI strip where each tile is a clickable filter chip with count + weekly delta. Filter bar: search, Status (default Active), Priority, and any applied KPI-chip filters shown as removable pills. Sub-tabs 'All Needs' / 'Smart Opportunities' sit on top of the list. Empty state is a centered card with icon, 'No active needs match your filters', and two buttons: primary 'Create Need', secondary 'Clear filters' (conditional). Populated list rows: priority pill • strain • category/grade • qty range • client • match count badge • row actions (Edit, Cancel, Fulfill, Attach to match).

#### VendorSupplyPage — `/demand-supply?tab=vendor-supply` (lightweight)

![VendorSupplyPage](screenshots_all/demand_supply_vendor.png)

*The page is functional but wastes its most valuable real estate. Four oversized KPI cards dominate the viewport before the user sees a single supply item — and three of those KPIs (Reserved=1, Total=15, Expiring=0) are low-signal for a daily workflow that is fundamentally about matching offered inventory to clients. The supply row itself is information-sparse despite being ~130px tall: the supplier is rendered as '#24' with no name, and the primary action 'Find Matching Clients' is a low-contrast outlined button competing with nothing. The redundant top block ('Demand & Supply' + tab 'Supplier Supply' + H1 'Supplier Supply' + 'Jump to Supplier Supply' button) is a hierarchy smell — users already ARE on supplier supply.*

**Keep.** Status pill (Available/Expired) on each row makes lifecycle state scannable at a glance.; Filter bar (search + status + category + sort + direction) is well-organized and sits directly above the list where expected.; 'Find Matching Clients' per-row action correctly surfaces the matchmaking primitive at the supply-item level.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `demand_supply_vendor-UX-1` | **P1** | **KPI strip pushes the actual inventory list below the fold** — Four full-width stat cards (Available Items 12, Reserved 1, Total 15, Expiring Soon 0) consume roughly a third of the initial viewport. Only the first supply row (Blue Dream) is partially visible; the second (Gelato) is clipped. Three of the four cards show trivial numbers (1, 15, 0) that do not drive any action. | Collapse the four cards into a single compact summary bar above the filters (e.g., '12 available · 1 reserved · 0 expiring ≤30d · 15 total') at ~32px height, and hoist the list up. Keep each metric clickable as a filter shortcut. | All four metrics remain visible and remain derived from the same `vendorSupply.*` aggregate; nothing is removed, only re-laid-out into one row. |
| `demand_supply_vendor-UX-2` | **P1** | **Supplier shown as '#24' instead of a name** — The Blue Dream row's supplier line reads 'Supplier: #24 • Flower • Grade B'. A numeric ID is meaningless to a sales rep deciding whether to pitch this lot to a client. | Render the vendor's display name as the primary label ('Green Valley Farms #24') sourced from the `vendors` relation; keep the numeric code as a secondary muted suffix. If the name is truly unknown, show 'Unnamed vendor #24' rather than the bare ID. | Uses the existing `vendors.*` / `clients.*` tRPC join already declared in baseline; the vendor ID remains addressable, only the label changes. |
| `demand_supply_vendor-UX-3` | **P2** | **Redundant 'Jump to Supplier Supply' button on the Supplier Supply tab** — While the Supplier Supply tab is active, the header still renders a 'Jump to Supplier Supply' button next to 'Open Matchmaking'. It navigates to where the user already is. | Hide 'Jump to Supplier Supply' when `tab=vendor-supply` is active (keep it on other tabs where it's a useful shortcut). Leave 'Open Matchmaking' and promote 'Add Supply Item' as the sole primary CTA in the page header row. | The cross-tab jump shortcut is retained on Matchmaking/Client Needs/Interest List tabs; only the self-referential case is suppressed. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: breadcrumb + single H1 'Supplier Supply' with subcopy, right-aligned primary 'Add Supply Item' and secondary 'Open Matchmaking' / 'Configure Display'. Below header, a 32px summary strip: '12 Available · 1 Reserved · 0 Expiring ≤30d · 15 Total' as clickable filter chips. Then the existing filter bar unchanged. Then a denser list where each row is two lines: line 1 = Strain (bold) + status pill + vendor display name; line 2 = a 4-column grid (Qty | Price | Avail Until | Added) with 'Find Matching Clients' right-aligned as a filled primary button and a kebab for edit/delete. Remove the self-referential 'Jump to Supplier Supply' button when already on this tab.

#### LeaderboardPage — `/leaderboard` (lightweight)

![LeaderboardPage](screenshots_all/leaderboard.png)

*The page has a clean scaffold — clear H1, category tabs, and a filter row — but it's doing the bare minimum to orient the user. The client-type dropdown label reads 'All ClientsAll Clients' (doubled string), the sort control shows 'Highest First' with no indication it toggles asc/desc, and the five category tabs (Master, Financial, Engagement, Reliability, Growth) give no hint of what metrics or weights drive them. Once loaded, rows are skeleton-only here, but there is no column header, no rank column, no score preview, and no explanation of how Master Score is composed — which is especially problematic given a 'Customize Weights' button sits top-right with no visible context for what it changes.*

**Keep.** Clear category tab model (Master/Financial/Engagement/Reliability/Growth) gives users a fast mental map of the five lenses on performance.; Top-right action cluster (Customize Weights, Refresh, Export) groups configuration and data-out actions predictably.; Subtitle 'Track and compare client performance across key metrics' sets purpose immediately below the H1.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `leaderboard-UX-1` | **P2** | **Client-type filter renders label twice ('All ClientsAll Clients')** — The first filter dropdown displays the string 'All ClientsAll Clients' — the selected value appears concatenated with the placeholder or label. This is visible in the screenshot and in the runtime button list. | Render the trigger as a single label: when nothing is narrowed show 'Client type: All', otherwise 'Client type: Customers' / 'Suppliers' / 'Dual'. Drop the duplicated value-plus-placeholder concatenation in the Select trigger. | Preserves the `Filters: Client type (ALL/CUSTOMER/SUPPLIER/DUAL)` baseline — only the trigger label changes; the four filter values and the `leaderboard.*` query params are untouched. |
| `leaderboard-UX-2` | **P2** | **Sort control hides the asc/desc toggle and the second sort key** — The filter row exposes 'Master Score' and 'Highest First' as two separate pills, but there is no visual affordance that 'Highest First' is a direction toggle, and no indication that `ytd_revenue` is an alternative sort key documented in the baseline. | Combine into one labeled control: 'Sort by [Master Score ▾] [↓ Highest first]' where the first pill is a select with Master Score and YTD Revenue, and the arrow pill is an explicit direction toggle with a tooltip 'Switch to lowest first'. | Preserves the baseline `sort by master_score or ytd_revenue (asc/desc)` — both keys and both directions remain, only the labeling/affordance changes. |
| `leaderboard-UX-3` | **P2** | **'Customize Weights' is unexplained and disconnected from the Master Score tab** — The 'Customize Weights' button sits top-right with no tooltip, no current-weight summary, and no visual link to the 'Master Score' tab it actually governs. Users on Financial/Engagement/Reliability/Growth tabs see it too, where it has no effect. | Show the button only (or emphasize it) on the Master Score tab, and render a small caption under 'Master Score Rankings': 'Weights: Financial 40% · Engagement 20% · Reliability 25% · Growth 15% · Customize'. Keep the full `WeightCustomizer` modal as the click target. | Preserves `WeightCustomizer` action and `gamification.*` weight mutations — only placement and an inline summary are added; the modal and its writes are untouched. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep H1 'Leaderboard' with subtitle. Directly under the tab row for Master Score, add a one-line weights caption ('Financial 40% · Engagement 20% · Reliability 25% · Growth 15% — Customize') that doubles as the entry point to WeightCustomizer, so the top-right button becomes secondary. Collapse the filter row into three clearly labeled controls: 'Client type: All', 'Sort by: Master Score ▾', and a direction toggle '↓ Highest first', plus the search field left-aligned. Replace the bare skeleton rows with a table that has columns Rank · Client (name + TERI code) · Score · Δ vs last period · YTD Revenue · quick-action chevron, so rows click through to `/clients/:id` as today. Retain Refresh and Export top-right; move Customize Weights next to them but styled as tertiary until the Master Score tab is active.
