### Inventory, Warehouse & Catalog

#### InventoryWorkspacePage.inventory — `/inventory?tab=inventory` (full)

![InventoryWorkspacePage.inventory](screenshots_all/inventory.png)

*The page correctly anchors Inventory as the Operations home and exposes the right tab set, but the default kanban-by-status board fights the default 'Live' filter: three of four columns render 'No batches' while the only populated column ('Live') shows a cramped 100-item scroll, and the rightmost 'Quarantined' column is visibly clipped off the canvas. The card body is also too thin for a THCA wholesale tool — Qty and price without THCA%, weight, location, COA status, or age means buyers and operators cannot triage from this surface and must click into every batch. Finally, the left rail is titled 'SALES QUICK ACTIONS' on what is explicitly the Inventory workspace, creating an off-topic primary nav. The KPI strip (303 batches / 38,185.26 units / $34,215,625.44 value) and the tab structure are strong; the board metaphor itself is not the problem, the filter+view coupling and card density are.*

**Keep.** The KPI strip with batches / units / value anchors the workspace with portfolio-level truth at a glance.; Tab order (Inventory → Direct Intake → Product Intake → Shipping → Photography → Samples) mirrors the real physical lifecycle of a batch and should be preserved.; Batch cards lead with the SKU/lot code in a monospace chip, which matches how ops teams actually refer to inventory on the floor.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `inventory-UX-1` | **P1** | **Status filter 'Live' and kanban columns double-filter, leaving 3 of 4 lanes empty** — The toolbar status selector is set to 'Live' while the board renders four status lanes — Awaiting Intake (0), Live (100), On Hold (0), Quarantined (clipped). Three columns permanently say 'No batches' and consume ~60% of the horizontal canvas. | When the status selector is set to a single status, collapse non-matching lanes into 48px header-only rails showing only the count and allow click-to-expand; when the selector is 'All', expand all four. Alternatively, auto-switch the status selector to 'All' the first time the kanban is rendered and let column-level counts carry the filtering story. | Keeps the status dropdown and the four-lane kanban from `InventoryManagementSurface` intact — nothing is removed, only the default interaction between filter and board is reconciled. |
| `inventory-UX-2` | **P1** | **Rightmost 'Quarantined' column is clipped at 1440px viewport** — At the default viewport the Quarantined column header is cut off mid-word with no visible horizontal scroll affordance. The user has no cue that more content exists to the right. | Set column min-width to ~280px with `overflow-x: auto` on the board container and render a persistent right-edge fade + scroll shadow. Additionally, show a sticky column-count rail above the board (e.g., 'Awaiting 0 · Live 100 · On Hold 0 · Quarantined N') so counts are readable even when a column is scrolled out. | Preserves the four-column lane layout from `InventoryManagementSurface`; only the container's overflow behavior and a summary rail are added. |
| `inventory-UX-3` | **P1** | **Batch cards omit the data that drives wholesale decisions** — Each card shows SKU, product name, a single supplier/origin line, Qty, and price. There is no THCA%, no weight, no room/location, no intake date or batch age, no COA/test status, no photography status, and no hold/sample reservations. | Add a 2-line metadata region under the product name: line 1 = THCA% · weight (lb/kg) · age in days; line 2 = location/room · COA badge (Pass/Pending/Fail) · photo badge · hold/reserved badge. Keep Qty and price pinned to the bottom-right as today. Allow the 'Default' saved view to toggle a 'Compact' density that hides line 2. | No new data sources required — every field surfaces existing attributes already rendered in the deep-linked `batchId` row sheet of `InventoryManagementSurface`; nothing is removed. |

Keep the Sales items available under OPERATIONS→Sales, not in the top rail. | Every existing Sales Quick Action item remains reachable; this is a rename + per-route item swap inside the existing rail component, no router or tRPC endpoints change. |
| `inventory-UX-5` | **P2** | **KPI chips (303 batches · 38,185.26 units · $34,215,625.44 value) are dead text** — The three portfolio KPIs sit in chip-shaped containers but are not clickable, cannot be filtered to, and do not update when filters or status selector are applied — they always reflect the unfiltered portfolio. | Keep the chips visually identical but make each one: (a) recompute against active filters with the unfiltered total shown as subdued 'of 303' suffix, and (b) clickable to toggle 'show only batches contributing to this metric' (e.g., clicking '$value' sorts by value desc). | `InventoryManagementSurface` already exposes batches/units/value aggregates; this only adds click handlers and a filter-aware recompute, preserving the original totals as secondary text. |
| `inventory-UX-6` | **P2** | **'Inventory' appears three times within 120px of vertical space** — The breadcrumb says Inventory, the H1 says Inventory, the active tab says Inventory, and the KPI strip header says Inventory — four repetitions stacked in the top pane. | Drop the KPI strip's duplicate 'Inventory' subheader (keep the chips and the 'INVENTORY OPERATIONS' eyebrow). Replace the H1 'Inventory' with a contextual title that includes the active view, e.g., 'Inventory — Live view' that updates with the status selector. Keep the tab label as-is. | Pure copy/label change inside the H1 region of `InventoryWorkspacePage`; tabs, KPIs, and routing are untouched. |
| `inventory-UX-7` | **P2** | **'Save View' button is disabled by default with no affordance explaining why** — Next to the 'Default (available now)' view selector, 'Save View' renders in a disabled state on page load with no tooltip, hint, or muted helper text. | Keep the button disabled until a filter/sort/status change is applied, and replace the static label with 'Save changes to view' + a tooltip on hover: 'Change a filter, search, or status to save a new view.' | `inventory-UX-8` | **P3** | **Active tab visual treatment is almost invisible** — The active 'Inventory' tab is distinguished only by a faint outline/underline; it reads nearly identical to inactive tabs like 'Direct Intake' and 'Shipping'. | Give the active tab a 2px bottom border in the brand accent, bold the label (500→600), and darken the label color one step. Keep hover/focus rings as-is. | Styling-only change to the existing tab component in `INVENTORY_WORKSPACE`; no routing or tab logic changes. |

**Redesign sketch.** Top pane: breadcrumb → H1 'Inventory — {active status} view' → six tabs with a stronger active underline. Below tabs, a single-row command strip: left = search input, status selector ('All' by default so the board carries filtering), Filters, saved-view selector + contextual 'Save changes to view' button; right = density toggle (Compact/Standard) and Export CSV. Below the strip, three clickable KPI chips (batches · units · value) that recompute against active filters and show 'of {unfiltered}' subtext. Main surface: four-lane kanban with min-width 280px lanes, horizontal scroll with edge shadows, and a sticky summary rail above the board showing all four lane counts even when a lane is scrolled off. Each card: row 1 = SKU chip + status dot; row 2 = product name; row 3 = supplier / origin; row 4 = THCA% · weight · age-in-days; row 5 = location · COA badge · photo badge · hold/reserved badge; footer = Qty left, price right. Left rail renamed 'Quick Actions' with context-aware items for /inventory (New Intake, Create Adjustment, Photography Queue, Pending Samples, Today's Shipments). Everything documented in the baseline — tabs, sheet-native surfaces, deep-link `batchId`, status lanes, KPIs, saved views, Export CSV — stays intact; the redesign only rewires defaults, density, and card information architecture.

#### InventoryWorkspacePage.shipping — `/inventory?tab=shipping` (full)

![InventoryWorkspacePage.shipping](screenshots_all/inventory_shipping.png)

*The Shipping queue shows the right raw ingredients — status counts, a sortable list, per-shipment progress bars — but the workflow is broken in two decisive ways. First, selecting the highlighted shipment S-1773368587219 leaves the entire right two-thirds of the viewport blank; there's no detail pane, no pick list, no empty state. The page is a dead-end the moment a user tries to act. Second, the defaults are inverted for the actual job: 381 Pending shipments drown the 2 Ready ones that are the only ones a packer can actually work on right now, and there's no way to pivot except through a generic 'All statuses' dropdown. The four stat cards tease filtering affordance (colored, clickable-looking) but are decorative. The 'Spreadsheet View / Standard View' toggle top-right and the floating 'Standard' pill bottom-right appear to be doing overlapping jobs and neither is labeled in a way a new packer would understand.*

**Keep.** Stat cards give an immediate, honest read on queue health (Pending/Partial/Ready/Shipped) with sensible color coding.; Each shipment row surfaces packing progress (2/2 items packed, bag count, progress bar) without requiring a drill-down.; Status chip on each row (Ready, Pending) is high-contrast and scannable at list speed.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `inventory_shipping-UX-1` | **P0** | **Selected shipment renders a blank right pane** — S-1773368587219 is clearly selected (blue border, 'Ready' chip, 2/2 items packed) but the entire area to the right of the list is empty white space. There is no detail, no pick list, no pack action, and no empty-state copy. | Always render the FulfillmentPilotSurface detail pane in the right column. When nothing is selected show an explicit empty state ('Select a shipment to start packing'); when a row is selected, mount the pick list, bag breakdown, and primary 'Start Packing'/'Mark Ready'/'Mark Shipped' action there. If the blank pane is an unhandled loading state, show a skeleton with the row header echoed so the user knows the click registered. | FulfillmentPilotSurface (and the PickPackWorkSurface classic fallback behind SheetModeToggle) continues to own the detail UI; the fix only guarantees it mounts and has a defined empty state, leaving all pick/pack mutations and tRPC calls untouched. |
| `inventory_shipping-UX-2` | **P1** | **Default sort buries the 2 Ready shipments under 381 Pending** — The list is sorted 'Newest' with 'All statuses' selected. Ready: 2, Pending: 381 — yet the queue leads with the one Ready shipment only because it happens to be newest. The next three rows are all Pending, and the user must scroll or change the filter to find shipments they can actually act on. | Change the default sort to 'Action needed': Ready first, then Partial, then Pending, then Shipped (within each group, Newest). Keep 'Newest' selectable in the existing sort dropdown. Alternatively, default the status filter to 'Ready + Partial' and show a persistent 'Show all (381 Pending)' link above the list. | The existing 'All statuses' dropdown and 'Newest' sort control remain and can still be selected; only the initial default values change, and the underlying shipment query (status counts of 381/0/2/127) is untouched. |
| `inventory_shipping-UX-3` | **P1** | **Stat cards look clickable but are not filters** — The four numbered cards (381 Pending, 0 Partial, 2 Ready, 127 Shipped) are styled like interactive pills with colored backgrounds and bold numbers, but they sit alongside a separate 'All statuses' dropdown and do nothing when clicked. This is wasted real estate and a misleading affordance. | Promote the four stat cards into the primary status filter control: clicking 'Ready' filters the list to Ready, shows an active-state border, and keeps the count live. The existing 'All statuses' dropdown becomes 'All' as a fifth reset chip, or is removed from the filter row in favor of the cards. Zero-count cards (0 Partial) render disabled rather than hidden so the layout stays stable. | The 'All statuses' filter control and its underlying query parameter are retained — the cards simply drive the same filter state. The stat counts already come from the same shipment-by-status aggregation; we just wire their click handlers. |
| `inventory_shipping-UX-4` | **P1** | **Two view toggles with overlapping meaning** — Top-right has a 'Spreadsheet View / Standard View' segmented control. Bottom-right has a floating pill showing 'Standard' with a list icon. Both appear to toggle between sheet-native and classic surfaces (the SheetModeToggle documented in the baseline command strip), but they are visually unrelated and the floating one has no label explaining its purpose. | Keep one SheetModeToggle in a single location — the top-right header row next to 'Refresh Queue' — and style it consistently (Spreadsheet \| Standard with a clear selected state). Remove the floating duplicate or repurpose the FAB for the shipping-specific 'New Shipment' / 'Manage MCP & Webhooks' action it already surfaces in the button list, with a proper label. | SheetModeToggle behavior (switching between FulfillmentPilotSurface and PickPackWorkSurface) and the 'Manage MCP & Webhooks' entry point are both retained — the fix consolidates their placement so only one control owns view mode. |
| `inventory_shipping-UX-5` | **P2** | **Page heading hierarchy duplicates itself** — Breadcrumb says 'Inventory', H1 says 'Inventory', the active tab is 'Shipping', and the section header below the tabs also says 'Shipping' with a 'Saved' badge. The user gets told they are on Inventory twice before finding out they are actually on Shipping. | Collapse the H1 to reflect the active tab: 'Inventory › Shipping' in the breadcrumb, H1 'Shipping', and drop the second 'Shipping' section header. Replace the 'Saved' badge with a specific label like 'Filters saved' or move it onto the filter row where it belongs; keep it only when the user has actually saved a custom filter state. | The tab set from INVENTORY_WORKSPACE, the `tab=shipping` URL parameter, and the saved-filter state remain — only the typographic hierarchy and badge placement change. |
| `inventory_shipping-UX-6` | **P2** | **Shipment cards omit customer, destination, and due date** — Rows show only: shipment ID, a free-text line (e.g. 'wer werwe', 'San Jose Supply', 'Mendocino Supply'), packed count, bag count, and status. There is no carrier, no ship-by date, no order value, no origin/destination pair. The 'wer werwe' entry on the Ready row is particularly damning — clearly a test note, but indistinguishable from a real customer name with current formatting. | Standardize each card to three lines: (1) shipment ID + status chip + ship-by date on the right; (2) customer name + destination city/state; (3) items-packed progress + bag count + progress bar. Label the customer line explicitly so free-text reference notes don't masquerade as customer names. | The underlying shipment record (customer, destination, ship date, items, bags) already drives the existing card; this fix only renders more of those fields. No baseline field is removed. |
| `inventory_shipping-UX-7` | **P3** | **Pluralization bug: '1 bags'** — The Ready row reads '1 bags' in the right corner. All other rows show '0 bags' which is correct, but the singular case is not handled. | Use a pluralization helper (`${n} ${n === 1 ? 'bag' : 'bags'}`) wherever the bag count is rendered on shipment rows. Apply the same treatment to 'items packed' if the same bug exists there. | The bag count value from the shipment model is unchanged; only the rendered string is corrected. |
| `inventory_shipping-UX-8` | **P2** | **No bulk actions or keyboard affordances for a 381-row queue** — With 381 Pending shipments and 127 Shipped, the list offers no multi-select, no keyboard arrow-navigation cue, no 'J/K' hint, and no bulk 'Mark Ready' / 'Assign to picker' action. The command palette (CTRL K) exists at app level but there is no per-row quick action or right-click menu visible. | Add (a) arrow-key navigation between rows with the detail pane updating live, (b) a checkbox column and a sticky bulk-action bar ('Assign picker', 'Mark Ready', 'Print labels') that appears when ≥1 row is selected, and (c) a subtle 'J/K to navigate, Enter to open' hint in the list header. | Existing per-shipment actions remain on the detail pane (FulfillmentPilotSurface); bulk actions call the same shipment status mutations in a loop, so no new business rule is introduced. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: breadcrumb 'Inventory › Shipping', H1 'Shipping', inline subtitle 'Pick, pack, and ship customer orders.' Right-aligned in the header: SheetModeToggle (Spreadsheet | Standard) + 'Refresh Queue' + overflow menu (Saved filters, Manage MCP & Webhooks). Remove the duplicate bottom-right floating toggle.

Primary filter row = the four stat cards, now interactive: [Ready 2] [Partial 0] [Pending 381] [Shipped 127] [All 510]. Active card gets a filled border. Below them: search input, secondary 'Sort: Action needed ▾' (default), ship-by-date range picker, customer filter, and 'Reset'.

Body is a two-column split: left 360px shipment list, right flex detail pane.

List rows (default sorted Ready → Partial → Pending → Shipped, newest within): checkbox · ID + status chip · ship-by date (right) // customer name + destination // progress bar + '2/2 items · 1 bag'. Arrow keys navigate, Enter opens, Space selects for bulk. When ≥1 checkbox is selected, a sticky action bar slides in: 'Assign picker · Mark Ready · Print labels · Cancel'.

Detail pane (always mounted) shows the selected shipment's header (customer, destination, ship-by, carrier), a pick list table (SKU, lot, required, picked, location), bag breakdown, and a sticky footer action strip whose primary button changes by status: Pending → 'Start Picking', Partial → 'Continue Picking', Ready → 'Mark Shipped', Shipped → 'View BOL'. Empty state when nothing is selected: centered icon + 'Select a shipment to start packing' + 'or press N to create a new shipment'.

Microcopy: '1 bag' / 'n bags' pluralized; '0/1 items packed' becomes 'Not started'; 'wer werwe'-style free-text is relabeled 'Reference' and rendered smaller beneath the real customer name.

#### InventoryWorkspacePage.intake — `/inventory?tab=intake` (lightweight)

![InventoryWorkspacePage.intake](screenshots_all/inventory_intake.png)

*The Direct Intake tab packs a real workflow — supplier/product/qty/COGS entry, bulk row controls, and a live grid — into one screen, but hierarchy is broken in ways that will confuse any new receiver. The top form and the row grid look like two disconnected objects, the Location field literally renders 'Main Warehouse' five times concatenated, and the grid's column headers are truncated to single letters ('C…', 'S.') which makes the spreadsheet unreadable. The sub-tab row (Intake / Pending 5 / Submitted 0 / Errors 0 / Qty 0 / $0.00) mixes navigation pills with KPI counters using identical styling, so a user can't tell what's clickable. The Standard/Spreadsheet view toggle and the Submit controls are well placed, but the page needs a hierarchy pass before a real receiver could move fast on it.*

**Keep.** Saved indicator + Edit Selected Details give clear autosave feedback and a path to bulk edit — must survive any redesign.; Action grouping at the row level (Add Row, +5 Rows, Submit Selected, Fill Down, Duplicate, Remove, Submit All) covers every bulk operation a receiver needs in one strip.; Sub-counts (Pending 5, Submitted 0, Errors 0) expose draft health at a glance, which is the right ambient signal for a batch-entry workflow.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `inventory_intake-UX-1` | **P0** | **Location field renders duplicated 'Main Warehouse' string** — The Location select shows the value as 'Main WarehouseMain WarehouseMain WarehouseMain WarehouseMain Warehouse' — the same label concatenated five times inside one input — while every grid row below correctly shows a single 'Main Warehouse'. | Render the top-level Location control as a single selected value with a count chip only if multi-location is intentional (e.g., 'Main Warehouse · 5 selected'). Fix the join/format bug in the trigger so it displays one location label, matching the per-row cell below. | Keeps the `IntakePilotSurface` location selector and its binding to the location field on each grid row — this is purely a display/format fix to the select's trigger label. |
| `inventory_intake-UX-2` | **P1** | **Grid column headers are truncated to unreadable single letters** — In the row grid, four consecutive columns show headers 'C…', 'C…', 'C…', 'C…' and the last column is 'S.' — only Supplier, Product/Strain, and Location are legible. The columns are each ~80px wide with filter/menu chevrons eating the remaining space. | Set a minimum header width that fits the label before the filter icon (e.g., 120px for COGS/Qty, 140px for COGS Mode), move the column-menu kebab to a hover affordance, and allow the Supplier/Product/Location columns to flex so numeric columns keep their labels. Show full header text with a tooltip fallback only when genuinely space-constrained. | Preserves the `IntakePilotSurface` sheet-native column set (Supplier, Product/Strain, COGS Mode, COGS, Qty, Location, Status) and per-column filter/menu handlers; only column sizing and header rendering change. |
| `inventory_intake-UX-3` | **P2** | **Sub-tab row conflates navigation pills with KPI counters** — The strip 'Intake \| Pending 5 \| Submitted 0 \| Errors 0 \| Qty 0 \| $0.00' uses identical pill styling for all six items, but 'Intake' is the active view while 'Qty 0' and '$0.00' are totals, and 'Pending/Submitted/Errors' are filter counts. Nothing distinguishes the three roles. | Split the strip into two zones: left = segmented control for 'Intake / Pending (5) / Submitted (0) / Errors (0)' with a clear selected state; right = read-only summary chips 'Qty: 0' and 'Total: $0.00' rendered as metric tiles, not buttons. Align the summary chips with the 'Saved' and 'Edit Selected Details' cluster on the right. | Keeps every existing count and filter behavior in `IntakePilotSurface`'s status filter strip — the fix is a visual grouping and styling change, not a removal of any filter or metric. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row unchanged: H1 'Inventory' + tab bar + right-aligned Spreadsheet/Standard view toggle. Directly under the tab bar, a single command strip split into three zones: (left) segmented filter 'Intake · Pending 5 · Submitted 0 · Errors 0' with one selected state; (center) small metric tiles 'Qty 0' and 'Total $0.00' in muted type; (right) 'Saved ✓' + 'Edit Selected Details'. Below, a titled 'New intake row' card containing Supplier, Product/Strain, Qty, COGS Mode, COGS on row 1 and Location on row 2 — Location shows a single selected value, not a concatenated string. Then a bulk-actions toolbar ('Add Row', '+5 Rows', 'Fill Down', 'Duplicate Selected', 'Remove Selected', with 'Submit Selected (1)' and 'Submit All Product Intake' right-aligned in primary brown). The grid underneath uses full-width legible headers (SUPPLIER, PRODUCT/STRAIN, COGS MODE, COGS, QTY, LOCATION, STATUS), column menus hidden until hover, and a sticky first column for supplier so the receiver can scan rows while entering numerics.

#### PhotographyPage — `/inventory?tab=photography` (lightweight)

![PhotographyPage](screenshots_all/inventory_photography.png)

*The page surfaces the right data — four pipeline counters, a batch table with status chips, and an Open Shoot Desk action per row — but the hierarchy is flat and the primary workflow is buried. With 'Ready to Review' at 0 and 'Queued' at 2 but 100 'Total Batches' showing as Pending, the counters and the table tell conflicting stories. The 'Select All Ready to Review' button is the de facto primary action yet it sits top-right with no visual weight, and the per-row Open Shoot Desk buttons repeat identically in every row with no bulk equivalent. There is also no indication which of these Pending batches the current user should start on first.*

**Keep.** Four-up KPI strip (Queued / Ready to Review / Shot Today / Total Batches) cleanly frames the pipeline state at a glance.; Per-row status chip + explicit 'Open Shoot Desk' CTA makes the next step unambiguous on each batch.; Batch filter dropdown + product search are positioned together above the table, matching standard queue-tool conventions.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `inventory_photography-UX-1` | **P1** | **Primary bulk action is visually demoted** — 'Select All Ready to Review' is the only bulk action on the page but renders as a plain outlined button in the top-right of the table toolbar, while each row repeats a visually identical 'Open Shoot Desk' button. With 100 pending batches, the selection checkbox column also has no corresponding bulk action bar when rows are checked. | Promote 'Select All Ready to Review' to a primary (filled) button and pair it with a contextual bulk action bar that appears above the table when any row checkbox is ticked, showing count + 'Open Shoot Desk for N batches' and 'Mark Complete'. Keep per-row buttons unchanged. | Preserves the PhotographyModule multi-select, status chips, and mark-complete features from the baseline — the fix only restyles the existing control and surfaces the existing bulk capability. |
| `inventory_photography-UX-2` | **P2** | **KPI counters contradict the visible queue without explanation** — Header shows Queued: 2, Ready to Review: 0, Shot Today: 0, Total Batches: 100 — yet every visible row has a 'Pending' status chip. There is no legend mapping 'Pending' chip → which counter bucket, and the counters are not clickable filters. | Make each KPI card a toggleable filter that scopes the table to its PENDING/IN_PROGRESS/COMPLETED bucket, add a one-line caption under each label (e.g., 'Pending intake', 'Awaiting QA', 'Completed today'), and align the chip labels in the Status column to the same vocabulary. | Preserves the baseline filterable queue on PENDING/IN_PROGRESS/COMPLETED and the existing status chips — the fix wires the counters into the same filter state already driven by the `All batches` dropdown and `photography.*` router. |
| `inventory_photography-UX-3` | **P2** | **Strain column is dead weight and Batch ID is under-emphasized** — Every visible row shows '-' in the Strain column, while Product names are truncated-looking strings like 'Qa Swarm Intake Product 1774741644218' and Batch IDs (564, 563, 562…) are the actual identifier photographers call out, yet Batch ID is rendered in the same weight as everything else. | Render Batch ID as a monospace, bolded lead token (e.g., '#564') as the first visible column after the checkbox, and collapse Strain into a secondary line under Product (or hide the column when >80% of rows are empty, with a column-picker toggle to bring it back). | Preserves all columns documented in the baseline filterable queue — Strain data remains in the DOM/row model and can be revealed via the column toggle, so no field is removed. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep H1 'Inventory' and the tab strip unchanged. Below tabs: a tighter 4-up KPI row where each card is a filter chip (Queued · Ready to Review · Shot Today · Total) with a selected state that scopes the table; sub-caption under each number clarifies the bucket. Toolbar row: left = product search + 'All batches' dropdown + status multi-select; right = primary filled 'Select All Ready to Review' button plus a secondary 'Upload' entry into PhotographyModule. Table: checkbox | #BatchID (mono, bold) | Product (with Strain as dim subtitle when present) | Status chip | Added | Open Shoot Desk. When any checkbox is active, a sticky bulk action bar slides in above the table: 'N selected — Open Shoot Desk · Mark Complete · Clear'. Empty 'Ready to Review' state gets a one-line nudge: 'Nothing to review. 2 batches queued for shooting.'

#### InventoryWorkspacePage.receiving — `/inventory?tab=receiving` (lightweight)

![InventoryWorkspacePage.receiving](screenshots_all/inventory_receiving.png)

*This is the receiving queue, but the page never admits it. The H1 is 'Inventory', the tab reads 'Product Intake', and the H2 reads 'Purchase Orders' — nothing on screen tells a receiver 'these are the POs waiting for you to receive'. The table itself is clean and the supplier chip row with counts is genuinely useful for triage, but the primary workflow (click a row to auto-launch the receiving draft per `autoLaunchReceivingOnRowClick`) is completely invisible — there is no 'Receive' action, no hover affordance, and the helper text 'Select a row to see details and actions' is tucked in the far right corner in muted type. The Est. Delivery column is 'Not set' on every confirmed row, which is the single most important field for a receiving queue and there is no call-to-action to fix it.*

**Keep.** Supplier chip row with live counts (Sierra Nevada Farms 22, Trinity Alps 2, …) gives fast, one-click triage across the queue.; Status summary pills ('10 confirmed purchase orders', '2 receiving purchase orders') next to the H2 correctly frame the queue's two states.; Dense, scannable table with per-column filter + menu affordances matches the rest of the ERP and keeps muscle memory.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `inventory_receiving-UX-1` | **P1** | **Primary action (start receiving) has zero affordance** — Baseline says row click auto-launches the receiving draft via `autoLaunchReceivingOnRowClick`, but the rows render as plain text with no cursor change, no trailing 'Receive' button, and no hover row highlight visible. The only hint is the right-aligned, muted 'Select a row to see details and actions' sentence next to the filter bar. | Add a trailing actions column with a primary 'Receive' button on `CONFIRMED` rows and 'Resume' on `RECEIVING` rows. Keep the full-row click behavior, but give each row a visible hover state and a chevron. Promote the helper sentence into a one-line banner under the H2: 'Click a PO to open its receiving draft.' | Does not touch `autoLaunchReceivingOnRowClick` or the `ProductIntakeSlicePage` lazy route — the new button simply triggers the same handler, and draft/confirmed state split is already in the baseline. |
| `inventory_receiving-UX-2` | **P1** | **Est. Delivery is 'Not set' on every row with no way to fix it** — Every CONFIRMED row shows 'Not set' in EST. DELIVERY. The 'Expected Today (0)' quick filter therefore can never return anything, and there is no inline edit, no bulk set, and no visual flag that these POs are missing a required planning field. | Render 'Not set' as a muted button that opens an inline date popover writing back through the existing PO update router. Flag rows with no ETA with a small amber dot in the PO NUMBER cell, and add a 'Missing ETA (10)' chip next to 'Expected Today (0)' so the gap is first-class. | Uses the existing PurchaseOrderSurface mutation path for `estimatedDeliveryDate`; no schema or status-model change. `Expected Today` filter logic is untouched. |
| `inventory_receiving-UX-3` | **P2** | **Heading stack never says 'Receiving'** — H1 'Inventory' → active tab 'Product Intake' → H2 'Purchase Orders' → subtitle 'Unified purchase order queue…'. The word 'Receiving' only appears as a status on two rows, even though the route is `?tab=receiving` and the baseline calls the tab 'Product Intake / Receiving'. | Rename the H2 to 'Receiving Queue' and move the existing 'Purchase Orders' label into the subtitle ('Confirmed and in-progress purchase orders ready to receive'). Keep the tab label 'Product Intake' for nav consistency, but add 'Receiving' as a secondary word in the tab tooltip and breadcrumb so search and muscle memory both work. | Pure copy/hierarchy change inside `PurchaseOrderSurface` header slot; tab key `receiving`, `INVENTORY_WORKSPACE` registry, and `useWorkspaceHomeTelemetry('inventory', 'receiving')` are all untouched. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep the outer Inventory shell and tab bar. Inside the Receiving tab: H2 becomes 'Receiving Queue' with subtitle 'Confirmed and in-progress POs ready to receive — click a row to open its draft.' Status pills ('10 Confirmed', '2 Receiving', 'Missing ETA 10', 'Expected Today 0') sit on one row as the primary segment control; supplier chip row stays directly below as a secondary filter. Table gets: hover highlight, a leading status dot column (amber = missing ETA, blue = receiving in progress), the existing columns, and a trailing actions column with a solid 'Receive' / ghost 'Resume' button. Est. Delivery cells render 'Not set' as an inline date-picker button. 'New Purchase Order' and 'Export CSV' stay top-right; the 'Select a row…' helper moves into the subtitle so the right rail is free for a future bulk-selection toolbar.

#### SampleManagement — `/inventory?tab=samples` (lightweight)

![SampleManagement](screenshots_all/inventory_samples.png)

*The page gets the basics right — a clear New Sample CTA, a readable table, and an Expiring Samples callout — but it undermines itself by shipping the same operator-lane filter twice (once as compact chips next to search, once as prominent tab-like buttons above the table). The Product column crams two SKUs plus unlabeled parenthetical numbers into one line, which is the single most frequent read on this screen and the hardest to parse. Density is otherwise low: Due Date is universally 'Not set' and Location is universally 'Warehouse', so two full columns carry zero signal, while the Expiring widget occupies a large empty card that says nothing is expiring.*

**Keep.** Operator-lane counts (All 14 / Samples Out 12 / Samples Return 2) are surfaced directly on the filter controls so triage is a one-click action.; Status pills ('Samples Out', 'Samples Return') are color-coded and consistent with the lane filter vocabulary.; New Sample is a single, prominent primary-colored CTA that is never more than one click from any sub-tab.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `inventory_samples-UX-1` | **P1** | **Lane filter is duplicated — two controls, same function** — The 'All 14 / Samples Out 12 / Samples Return 2' chips appear to the right of the search field, and an identical 'All Samples / Samples Out 12 / Samples Return 2' segmented control appears directly above the table. Both drive the same ALL/OUT/RETURN lane filter. | Keep one control: the larger segmented button row above the table ('All Samples / Samples Out 12 / Samples Return 2') since it has the clearest affordance and counts. Remove the duplicate chip row next to the search input and move the search field onto that same row, left-aligned, with the segmented control right-aligned. | Preserves the `SampleList` operator-lane filter (`ALL`/`OUT`/`RETURN`) — the single remaining segmented control still exposes all three lanes with their live counts. |
| `inventory_samples-UX-2` | **P1** | **Product column is ambiguous: unlabeled parenthetical numbers** — Rows show 'Product #107 (4.9), Product #108 (1.9)' with a lorem-ipsum subtitle. The parenthetical numbers have no header, unit, or tooltip — they could be quantity, weight (lb/g), potency %, or price. | Render each line item as 'Product #107 — 4.9 lb' (or whatever the canonical unit is), one item per line within the cell, with the unit explicit. Drop the lorem subtitle or replace it with a strain/grade tag pulled from the product record. Add a column header note 'Qty per item' if multiple items are common. | Preserves the `samples.*` tRPC payload (product + qty pairs from `SampleForm`); the fix is purely display formatting of fields already returned. |
| `inventory_samples-UX-3` | **P2** | **Empty Expiring Samples widget consumes prime real estate** — The 'Expiring Samples' card on the right occupies roughly a third of the width above the table and contains only the line 'No samples expiring in the next 30 days.' when empty, which is the common case. | Collapse the widget to a single-line inline banner above the table when empty ('⏱ No samples expiring in the next 30 days'), and expand it back to a full card only when `ExpiringSamplesWidget` has ≥1 entry. Let the table take the full container width in the empty state. | Preserves `ExpiringSamplesWidget` — same data source and threshold, only the empty-state presentation changes; populated states still render the full card. |

**Redesign sketch.** Single H1 'Samples' with a right-aligned 'New Sample' primary button on the same row. Below it, one toolbar row: left = search input 'Search samples…', right = segmented control 'All Samples 14 | Samples Out 12 | Samples Return 2'. Empty-state Expiring Samples collapses to a thin inline banner above the toolbar; when populated, it becomes a full card docked to the right of the toolbar. Table columns: ID · Product (stacked line items, each 'Product #107 — 4.9 lb') · Client · Status pill · Requested · Due (muted 'Not set' italic when null) · Location · Actions. Row click opens the sample drawer; overflow menu exposes Return, Ship, and Update Location entry points tied to the existing dialogs.

#### WarehousePickPackPage — `/warehouse/pick-pack` (full)

![WarehousePickPackPage](screenshots_all/warehouse_pick_pack.png)

*The page is legible and the KPI strip + card list pattern is a reasonable starting point, but it badly under-delivers on its stated purpose: a mobile/tablet, touch-first fulfillment UI. Instead we get a full desktop chrome (286px sidebar, breadcrumbs, command palette) eating ~30% of a 1440 viewport, oversized cards that show only an order number and a supplier name, and no way to triage 381 pending orders — no age, priority, status badge, item preview, or ship date. The headline stat visually prioritises the backlog (381 Pending in blue) over the actionable bucket (2 Ready in green), the stat cards are not filters, 'Ready' is the smallest emphasis, and there is no scan-to-jump affordance on the list view despite the baseline calling out barcode entry as a core interaction. Grammar ('1 items') and an unlabeled FAB round out the polish debt.*

**Keep.** Four-bucket status KPI strip (Pending / Picking / Ready / Shipped) gives an at-a-glance fulfillment pipeline.; Order cards are large, low-density, and easy to tap — the right instinct for warehouse gloved/tablet use.; A single prominent search field above the list matches the 'find my order fast' mental model of a picker.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `warehouse_pick_pack-UX-1` | **P1** | **Desktop chrome swallows a page spec'd as touch-first** — The left sidebar (SALES QUICK ACTIONS, SELL, BUY, OPERATIONS, RELATIONSHIPS, FINANCE, ADMIN), breadcrumbs (Home / Warehouse / Shipping), and the 'CTRL K' command palette all render at full width on a page the baseline describes as 'Mobile/tablet-optimized, touch-first, ≥44 px tap targets'. On a tablet in landscape, the 286 px sidebar alone consumes roughly a third of the horizontal space before any order content. | Default the sidebar to collapsed on any `/warehouse/*` route (keep the collapse toggle visible), hide breadcrumbs and the CTRL-K pill below the `md` breakpoint, and promote the page to max-width:100% so the order list fills the viewport. Keep the sidebar icons reachable via the existing collapse chevron for admins who want it. | Does not touch `pickPack.getPickList` or remove any nav entry — only changes the default collapsed state of the app shell for this route, so every SALES QUICK ACTIONS / SELL / BUY item remains one tap away via the existing collapse toggle. |
| `warehouse_pick_pack-UX-2` | **P1** | **Stat tiles look like filters but aren't** — The four tiles (381 Pending, 0 Picking, 2 Ready, 127 Shipped) are bordered, equally weighted, and visually segmented the way a segmented filter would be — but tapping them appears to do nothing, and the list below mixes all statuses with no badge to show which bucket each card belongs to. | Make each tile a toggle filter backed by the existing `status` field on `pickPack.getPickList`. Default the page to `Ready + Picking` selected (the action-required buckets); allow multi-select; persist selection in URL. Add a small colored status dot + label (e.g. 'Ready', 'Picking') on each order row. | Uses the existing `pickPack.getPickList` router with the `PENDING`/`PARTIAL`/`READY`/`SHIPPED` statuses already in the baseline — no new endpoint, no behavior removed, all 381 pending orders remain reachable by tapping the Pending tile. |
| `warehouse_pick_pack-UX-3` | **P1** | **Order cards carry no triage information** — Each row shows only the S-number, customer ('San Jose Supply', 'Mendocino Supply', 'Sunset Dispensary'), and 'X items'. There is no status, no order age, no ship-by date, no SKU preview, no carrier, no priority — nothing that tells a picker which of 381 pending orders to pull next. | Reformat each card into a two-row layout: top row = status pill + S-number (truncated to last 6, e.g. 'S-…234441') + ship-by date in red if overdue; bottom row = customer · item count · first 2 SKU names truncated. Right-aligned meta: 'Created 2h ago'. Keep the chevron. | All fields are already available on the order records feeding `pickPack.getPickList` (status, createdAt, line items, customer); this is a presentation change only and the 'Select an order to start picking' tap target and navigation behavior are unchanged. |
| `warehouse_pick_pack-UX-4` | **P1** | **No scan-to-jump on the list view** — The baseline lists 'Scan (barcode input)' as a core interaction, but on the list screen there is only a text search field ('Search by order number or client…') and no scan affordance. The scan flow is apparently only available after the user has already manually selected an order. | Add a barcode icon button inside the search field (right-aligned) that opens the same scan input already used on the detail page. On successful scan of an order barcode, route directly to that order's pick list via the existing `pickPack.getPickList` detail flow. | Reuses the existing `pickPack.pick` scan handler and `pickPack.getPickList` detail route — no new router, no removal of the text search which remains the primary input. |
| `warehouse_pick_pack-UX-5` | **P2** | **Visual hierarchy celebrates the backlog, not the action** — '381 Pending' renders in the largest blue numeral; '2 Ready' — the bucket the picker should act on next — is the same size but in a muted green that reads as less urgent. '0 Picking' is given equal real estate despite being empty. | Reverse the emphasis: color 'Ready' in the primary accent and add a subtle pulse/badge when >0; render 'Pending' and 'Shipped' in neutral grey text with a colored accent bar. Collapse empty buckets (e.g. 'Picking: 0') to a smaller tile. | All four status counts remain visible and tappable; only weight and color change. The underlying `pickPack.getPickList` count query is untouched. |
| `warehouse_pick_pack-UX-6` | **P2** | **Unlabeled floating action button in bottom-right** — A circular icon button sits in the bottom-right corner of the content area with no label, no tooltip rendered in the DOM, and no accompanying text. Its meaning is unguessable from the screenshot. | Either give the FAB a persistent label ('Scan' or 'Quick pick') with an icon on the left, or move its function into the header as a labeled button. Add an `aria-label` regardless. | The FAB's current action (whatever it invokes) remains; only its label and ARIA annotation are added. |
| `warehouse_pick_pack-UX-7` | **P2** | **No refresh control and no visible last-updated timestamp** — The baseline explicitly lists 'refresh' as a feature, but there is no refresh button or pull-to-refresh indicator on the screen, and no 'Updated 30s ago' stamp near the stat strip. | Add a small 'Updated 14s ago · Refresh' control aligned to the right of the H1. Auto-refresh the list every 30s via the existing query. On tablet, also wire pull-to-refresh. | Uses the existing `pickPack.getPickList` query; adds a manual re-fetch trigger and a timestamp, no new endpoints. |
| `warehouse_pick_pack-UX-8` | **P3** | **'1 items' grammar and unreadable 13-digit order IDs** — Every card with a single line says '1 items' (see 'S-1773179234441 · 1 items' and 'S-1773179163763 · 1 items'). The S-number itself is a 13-digit timestamp that is visually impossible to distinguish between rows — the first 10 digits are identical. | Pluralize correctly ('1 item' / '2 items'). Render order IDs as 'S-…234441' with a monospace suffix and the full ID available on hover/long-press; the last 6 digits are unique enough for visual scanning. | The full `orderNumber` is preserved in the underlying data and in search; only the rendered form is truncated. |

**Redesign sketch.** On /warehouse/pick-pack the app shell collapses its sidebar by default and hides breadcrumbs/CTRL-K under md. Header is a single row: H1 'Pick & Pack' with a right-aligned 'Updated 14s ago · Refresh' and a labeled 'Scan order' button. Below, a compact segmented filter bar built from the existing four status buckets — Ready (2) highlighted in primary green and selected by default alongside Picking (0); Pending (381) and Shipped (127) selectable but muted. Full-width search with an inline barcode icon on the right that opens scan mode. The order list becomes denser two-line rows: line 1 = colored status pill + 'S-…234441' (monospace) + ship-by chip ('Ship by Today' in amber when <24h); line 2 = customer name · '2 items' (pluralized) · preview of first SKUs ('Blue Dream 1g ×4, Gelato 3.5g ×2'). Right-side meta: '2h ago' and chevron. An unlabeled FAB is replaced with a labeled 'Scan' pill pinned to the bottom-right on mobile. Empty states per filter: 'No orders ready to pack — nice work.'

#### PricingProfilesPage — `/pricing/profiles` (lightweight)

![PricingProfilesPage](screenshots_all/pricing_profiles.png)

*The page cleanly surfaces the CRUD primitives (name, description, rules count, edit/delete) and the Create Profile affordance is well-placed. But the table is informationally thin — 'Rules Count' showing '1 rule(s)' tells me nothing about what the profile actually does, there is no column for client assignments (the stated purpose of bundling rules for clients), and the profile names here are timestamp-stamped QA garbage with no way to tell which is active or in use. The page reads as a list rather than a working management surface.*

**Keep.** Clear page header with purpose subtitle ('Manage collections of pricing rules for easy application to clients') anchors the task.; Create Profile CTA is prominent, top-right, with the conventional + icon.; Search input and table columns are scannable; edit/delete iconography matches the rest of the app.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `pricing_profiles-UX-1` | **P1** | **Rules Count column is dead weight — show what's in the bundle** — The 'Rules Count' column renders a badge that says '1 rule(s)' with no indication of which rules (volume discount? tier pricing? client-specific markup?) are in the profile. Users must click Edit on every row to learn what a profile does. | Replace the 'Rules Count' badge with a 'Rules' column that renders the count + a comma-separated preview of rule types (e.g., '3 · Volume discount, Tier pricing, +1'). Keep the numeric badge on hover/tooltip. Column remains sortable by count. | Baseline 'checkbox list of rules + priority ordering' form stays intact; this is a read-only projection of the same rule relationship already loaded for the profile row. |
| `pricing_profiles-UX-2` | **P1** | **No visibility into which clients use each profile** — The page purpose explicitly states profiles are 'assignable to clients', but the table has no 'Assigned Clients' or usage column. Deleting a profile via the trash icon gives no warning about downstream client impact. | Add an 'Assigned Clients' column showing a count badge (e.g., '12 clients') that opens a popover listing the clients. Gate the delete icon: if count > 0, disable with tooltip 'Reassign 12 clients before deleting' or force a confirmation modal listing affected clients. | The CRUD delete action and pricing profile router remain unchanged; this is an additive read column and a confirmation guard around the existing delete mutation — no behavior removed. |
| `pricing_profiles-UX-3` | **P2** | **No empty/zero-profile guidance and timestamp-named rows read as debug data** — The only two rows shown — 'Codex QA Pricing Profile 2026-03-12T23-51-30-199Z' and 'QA Pricing Proof 2026-03-12 Profile' — are ISO-stamped test artifacts, and the description column exposes internal ticket references ('TER-696'). There's also no status chip (Active/Draft/Archived) to distinguish real profiles from staging noise. | Add a Status column with Active/Draft/Archived chips, a default sort by 'Last updated' descending, and a filter chip row above the table ('All \| Active \| Draft \| Archived'). Truncate long names at ~48 chars with a tooltip on hover. | No baseline field is removed; status is derived from existing profile records (or defaults to 'Active' if the field doesn't yet exist), and the existing Search input and table columns remain. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep the current header block ('Pricing Profiles' H1 + subtitle, Create Profile CTA top-right). Below the search input, add a filter chip row: All · Active · Draft · Archived. Replace the current 4-column table with: Name (with status chip inline) · Rules (count + preview of top 2 rule names, '+N' overflow) · Assigned Clients (count badge, clickable popover) · Last Updated · Actions. Default sort: Last Updated desc. Delete icon shows a confirm modal listing affected clients when count > 0; otherwise deletes immediately. Empty state (zero profiles) shows an illustrated card: 'No pricing profiles yet — bundle your rules into reusable profiles to assign to clients in one click' with a primary Create Profile button.

#### PricingRulesPage — `/pricing/rules` (lightweight)

![PricingRulesPage](screenshots_all/pricing_rules.png)

*The page is functional and legible: a clean searchable table with clear columns, prominent Create Rule CTA, and per-row edit/delete actions. But it wastes the table's evidentiary power — every rule shows the same '+50.00%' pill and '1 condition(s)' placeholder, so at a glance you cannot tell what any rule actually does, who it applies to, or whether the top-priority rule is the one you think it is. The scope dimension (global / category / client / profile) from the baseline is entirely invisible, and the 'Back to Dashboard' link above the card competes with the page title for the primary wayfinding slot.*

**Keep.** Single prominent 'Create Rule' CTA and inline per-row edit/delete keep CRUD obvious.; Dedicated search field above the table matches the baseline's 'searchable table' contract.; Priority and Status columns are present and readable, supporting the rule-ordering mental model.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `pricing_rules-UX-1` | **P1** | **Conditions column is an opaque '1 condition(s)' placeholder** — Every row in the Conditions column shows the literal string '1 condition(s)' with no hint of what the condition is (category? client? SKU?). Combined with identical '+50.00%' adjustments and an 'AND' logic chip with nothing to AND, three rules look indistinguishable. | Render a human-readable summary chip per condition, e.g. 'Category: Flower', 'Client: Acme', 'Profile: Wholesale'. If >1 condition, show the first plus '+N more' with a tooltip listing the rest. Drop the parenthetical '(s)' and only show the AND/OR chip when conditions.length > 1. | Uses the same `pricing.*` rule payload already fetched for the table; edit dialog and condition storage are untouched — only the cell renderer changes. |
| `pricing_rules-UX-2` | **P2** | **Rule scope (global / category / client / profile) is not surfaced** — The baseline documents scope as a first-class feature, but the table has no Scope column. A global +50% markup and a client-specific +50% markup render identically. | Insert a 'Scope' column between Name and Adjustment with a colored tag: Global (neutral), Category (blue), Client (purple), Profile (amber). Sort/filter by scope via column header. | Reads existing scope field exposed by `pricing.list` (create/edit dialogs already write it per baseline 'rule scope' feature); no schema or router change. |
| `pricing_rules-UX-3` | **P2** | **Status is display-only; baseline promises active/inactive toggles** — The Status column shows a static red 'Active' badge on every row. Baseline explicitly lists 'active/inactive toggles', but there is no toggle affordance in the row — the only way to deactivate is presumably inside the edit dialog. The red color also miscodes Active as a warning state. | Replace the badge with a switch component that calls `pricing.setActive` inline, with an optimistic update and toast. Use green for Active, neutral gray for Inactive. Keep the label next to the switch for scannability. | The baseline 'active/inactive toggles' feature and `pricing.*` mutation are the mechanism; this fix exposes the existing toggle in the row instead of burying it in the edit dialog. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep the card layout but promote the H1 'Pricing Rules' to the top of the card and demote 'Back to Dashboard' to a small breadcrumb-adjacent link (the breadcrumb already carries it). Below the title, a subtitle plus a compact filter row: search input, Scope dropdown (All / Global / Category / Client / Profile), Status dropdown (All / Active / Inactive), and a right-aligned 'Create Rule' button. Table columns, left to right: Name, Scope (colored tag), Adjustment (+/- % pill, green for markdown / red for markup so direction is legible), Conditions (human-readable chips, first + '+N more'), Logic (hidden when ≤1 condition), Priority (right-aligned numeric, with an ↑↓ reorder affordance on hover), Status (inline switch), Actions (edit / delete icons). Empty-state microcopy: 'No pricing rules yet. Create one to apply markups or markdowns by category, client, or profile.' Default sort: Priority desc, so the highest-priority rule is row 1.

#### ProductsPage — `/products` (lightweight)

![ProductsPage](screenshots_all/products.png)

*This is a functional but under-designed reference catalogue. The table renders strain name, a color-coded type badge, and description in a clear 3-column layout with an obvious search and a single prominent 'Create Strain' CTA. But for an ERP 'Products & Strains' screen, this page shockingly under-delivers: there is no column for product count, SKU count, stock/availability, last-updated, or any numeric context; descriptions are lorem-ipsum filler eating 50% of the horizontal space; there is no filter by Type (Indica/Sativa/Hybrid) despite the badge being the second column; and each row has no affordance for the 'edit strain' action promised by the baseline. Users browsing to pick a strain for an order get zero operational signal from this page.*

**Keep.** Clear H2 + subtitle pattern ('Products & Strains' / 'Manage strains and product varieties') with a single, unambiguous primary action.; Color-coded Type badges (Hybrid/Indica/Sativa) give instant visual categorization while scanning.; Search input is large, prominent, and sits directly above the table — matches `useTableUrlState` URL-state behavior.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `products-UX-1` | **P1** | **Row has no visible edit affordance or row action** — The baseline lists 'edit strain' as a feature, but rows (Apple Fritter, Biscotti, Blue Dream, etc.) show no pencil icon, kebab menu, hover action, or clickable name. There's no way to discover how to edit a strain from this table. | Add a trailing Actions column with a kebab menu per row ('Edit strain', 'View products', 'Archive') and make the strain name a clickable link that opens the same edit dialog. Show the kebab at low opacity by default, full opacity on row hover. | Uses the existing `strains.update` tRPC mutation and the edit strain dialog from the baseline — this is purely surfacing an existing feature, no behavior change. |
| `products-UX-2` | **P1** | **No Type filter despite Type being a first-class column** — Type (Indica/Sativa/Hybrid) is rendered as a badge column but the toolbar offers only a free-text search. There is no chip filter, segmented control, or dropdown to narrow by category. | Add a segmented filter to the right of the search input: 'All \| Indica \| Sativa \| Hybrid', persisted to URL state alongside the existing search param. | Extends the existing `useTableUrlState`-driven search by adding a `type` query param consumed by `strains.list`; the search input and its URL-state behavior are untouched. |
| `products-UX-3` | **P2** | **Table carries no operational signal — just name, badge, and filler description** — Three columns: Strain Name, Type, Description. Description is the widest column and is pure lorem-ipsum on staging. There is no product/SKU count, no 'last updated', no indicator of whether the strain is in active use. | Replace the Description column width with two new numeric columns from `productCatalogue.*`: '# Products' (right-aligned) and 'Last updated' (relative time). Truncate Description to a single line at ~40ch with a tooltip for the full text. | Description remains visible (truncated with tooltip) and the new columns are read-only projections over existing `products.*` / `productCatalogue.*` routers — no schema or mutation changes. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: H1 'Products & Strains' with subtitle unchanged, 'Create Strain' stays top-right. Toolbar row: left — search input (unchanged width); right — segmented Type filter [All | Indica | Sativa | Hybrid], then a small 'Refresh' icon button. Table columns: Strain Name (clickable, opens edit dialog) | Type (badge) | Products (right-aligned count, links to filtered products view) | Description (single-line truncate, tooltip on hover) | Last updated (relative) | ⋯ kebab (Edit, View products, Archive). Row hover reveals kebab at full opacity and highlights the row. Empty state inside the table when search returns nothing: 'No strains match "{query}" — Clear search or Create strain.' All URL state continues flowing through `useTableUrlState`.

#### CogsSettingsPage — `/settings/cogs` (lightweight)

![CogsSettingsPage](screenshots_all/cogs_settings.png)

*The page has a clean, scannable structure with a clear tab split between Global Settings and Client Adjustments, and the three channel rows (Sales Catalogue, Live Shopping, VIP Shopping) make the surface immediately intelligible. However, the page feels underbuilt: each row duplicates its own state twice (the 'Mid' dropdown and the 'Middle of range' pill say the same thing), there is no visible save affordance or autosave confirmation so users cannot tell whether changing the selector actually commits, and the settings are abstract — staff see LOW/MID/HIGH without any concrete dollar example of what selecting one does to a customer-facing price. The helpful info callout is good but is the only thing orienting the user to what they're configuring.*

**Keep.** Clear two-tab split (Global Settings vs Client Adjustments) matches the documented mental model in the baseline.; The inline info banner explaining staff vs customer visibility of vendor ranges is exactly the right microcopy for a pricing-integrity setting.; Per-channel row layout (Sales Catalogue / Live Shopping / VIP Shopping) is scannable and leaves room for future channels.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `cogs_settings-UX-1` | **P1** | **No save affordance — users can't tell if selection persisted** — The three channel dropdowns ('Mid' for Sales Catalogue, Live Shopping, VIP Shopping) have no adjacent Save button, no toast, no 'Saved' timestamp, and no dirty-state indicator. A user changing a dropdown has no confirmation that the change committed to the CogsGlobalSettings store. | Add an inline 'Saved [timestamp]' microcopy to the right of each selector that updates on successful mutation, plus a transient toast ('Default basis updated for Live Shopping'). If the existing behavior is manual-save, add a sticky footer bar with 'Save changes' / 'Discard' that appears only when the form is dirty. | Touches only feedback and footer chrome around the existing CogsGlobalSettings tab mutation — the dropdown values and their LOW/MID/HIGH options are untouched. |
| `cogs_settings-UX-2` | **P2** | **Each row duplicates its own state** — Every channel row renders both a 'Mid' dropdown on the right and a 'Middle of range' badge next to the 'Default effective basis:' label on the left. These two elements encode identical information and always move together. | Keep the dropdown as the single source of truth. Replace the redundant 'Middle of range' pill with either (a) a small helper line under the channel name describing what that channel is used for (e.g. 'Prices published to the public B2B catalogue'), or (b) the current resolved dollar range for a sample SKU (e.g. '$1,240 – $1,380, selected: $1,310'). Both options reuse the row's existing left column. | The CogsGlobalSettings selector (LOW/MID/HIGH) and the underlying vendor-range model remain the authoritative control; the pill is purely presentational and its removal does not alter any tRPC call. |
| `cogs_settings-UX-3` | **P2** | **No page H1 and weak visual hierarchy between page and card** — The DOM capture reports H1: []. 'COGS Settings' is rendered as styled text inside the card, not as a semantic page heading, and it competes visually with the 'Range-Based COGS Defaults' card title directly below it. | Promote 'COGS Settings' to a true <h1> in the page header region (above the card, aligned with 'Back to Dashboard'), and demote the in-card title to a smaller section label. Keep the subtitle 'Configure cost of goods sold calculations and client-specific adjustments' attached to the H1. | Pure typographic/semantic change — does not alter the Global Settings / Client Adjustments tab components or their routing. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header band outside the card: back link, then H1 'COGS Settings' with one-line subtitle. Directly below, the existing two-tab control (Global Settings | Client Adjustments) as the primary navigation. Under Global Settings, a single section 'Range-Based COGS Defaults' with the info callout kept verbatim. Below that, a 3-row table-style layout, one row per channel, with columns: (1) Channel name + one-line purpose description ('Public B2B catalogue', 'Live shopping sessions', 'VIP-only pricing'), (2) resolved preview like '$1,240 – $1,380 · selected $1,310' computed from a representative SKU, (3) single LOW/MID/HIGH segmented control (replacing the dropdown+pill pair), (4) small 'Saved 2s ago' microcopy that appears after a successful mutation. Sticky footer with 'Save changes' / 'Discard' surfaces only when the form is dirty, so autosave vs explicit-save behavior is unambiguous either way.

#### ShrinkageReportPage — `/reports/shrinkage` (lightweight)

![ShrinkageReportPage](screenshots_all/shrinkage.png)

*The page establishes a reasonable shrinkage overview — date/category/reason filters, three KPI cards, two breakdown charts, and CSV export — but the execution wastes vertical space and strips meaning from the visuals. The title 'Shrinkage Report' is rendered twice within 60px of itself (once beside the back button, once as the H1), and the 'Shrinkage by Reason' pie chart has no legend, no labels, and no percentages, so a user literally cannot tell which reason the dominant blue slice represents. The KPI trio is clean and the bar chart is legible, but 'Suspicious Events: 0' has no definition or drill-through affordance, so it reads as a dead metric.*

**Keep.** Filter row (Start/End/Category/Reason/Min Quantity) is laid out in a single scannable line with sensible 30-day default range.; Three KPI cards (Total Events, Total Qty Lost, Suspicious Events) give an immediate at-a-glance summary before the charts.; Export CSV is persistently visible in the top-right, matching the pattern used on other reports.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `shrinkage-UX-1` | **P2** | **Title 'Shrinkage Report' is rendered twice in the header** — The back-button row shows '← Back to Inventory  📉 Shrinkage Report' and then immediately below, the H1 repeats '📉 Shrinkage Report' with the subtitle 'Track and analyze inventory losses and discrepancies'. The page label and the H1 are identical strings stacked ~40px apart. | Collapse to a single header row: '← Back to Inventory' on the left, then the page title 'Shrinkage Report' with the subtitle directly beneath, and 'Export CSV' right-aligned on the same row. Drop the redundant title chip next to the back button — the breadcrumb ('Reports › Shrinkage') already labels the page. | Preserves the `ShrinkageReport` component's back-to-`/inventory` link and the Export CSV action documented in the baseline; only the duplicated text node is removed, no behavior changes. |
| `shrinkage-UX-2` | **P1** | **Shrinkage-by-Reason pie chart has no legend, labels, or values** — The left chart card titled 'Shrinkage by Reason' renders a blue circle with a thin white sliver — no legend, no slice labels, no tooltip hint, no percentages. In contrast the 'Shrinkage by Category' bar chart on the right labels Flower and Tincture with a numeric axis. | Add a right-side legend listing each reason with its color swatch, event count, and percentage (e.g. 'Damaged — 5 events · 83%'). Render slice labels on segments ≥8%, and fall back to a horizontal stacked bar when there are ≤2 reasons so a single dominant slice doesn't read as a solid disc. | Uses the same reason breakdown data the `ShrinkageReport` variant='full' component already aggregates; this is a presentation layer change to the existing chart, not a data or router change. |
| `shrinkage-UX-3` | **P2** | **'Suspicious Events' KPI is undefined and non-interactive** — The third KPI card shows 'Suspicious Events: 0' with an alert icon, but there is no tooltip, no definition of what makes an event suspicious, and clicking the card does nothing — while 'Total Events: 6' sits next to it with no way to filter the table below to just those 6 either. | Add an info tooltip on 'Suspicious Events' stating the exact rule (e.g. 'Events where qty lost > X% of batch or flagged by reviewer'). Make all three KPI cards clickable: Total Events scrolls to and filters the Shrinkage Events table to the current filter set; Suspicious Events additionally applies a `suspicious=true` filter; Total Qty Lost sorts the table descending by quantity. | Preserves the `ShrinkageReport` component's by-batch table and existing filter params (date range, category, reason, min quantity); the KPIs become shortcut filters over the same dataset rather than new endpoints. |

**Redesign sketch.** Single-row header: back chevron + breadcrumb on left, 'Shrinkage Report' H1 with 'Track and analyze inventory losses and discrepancies' subtitle centered-left, 'Export CSV' right-aligned. Second row: compact filter bar (Start/End preset chips '7d · 30d · 90d · Custom', Category, Reason, Min Qty) with an 'Apply / Reset' pair. Third row: 3 clickable KPI cards — Total Events (click = scroll+filter table), Total Qty Lost (click = sort table desc by qty), Suspicious Events (click = filter suspicious=true, with hover tooltip defining the rule). Fourth row: two equal-width chart cards; the pie becomes a donut with right-side legend showing 'Reason — count · %' rows, and the bar chart gains value labels at bar ends. Below, the existing 'Shrinkage Events' table anchors with a sticky filter summary chip row so users always see which slice/reason the table is scoped to.

### Procurement & Slice V1 Lab

#### ProcurementWorkspacePage — `/purchase-orders` (full)

![ProcurementWorkspacePage](screenshots_all/procurement.png)

*The page delivers the essentials — a dense PO queue, supplier pivots with counts, and clear primary actions (New Purchase Order, Export CSV) — but it wastes a full screen of hierarchy before the user reaches the data. 'Buying' as H1 sits above an almost-empty card whose only payload is an 'Expected Today' button; then 'Purchase Orders' appears again as H2 with three count chips; then 'Purchase Orders Queue' appears a third time with those same counts re-written as prose. Meanwhile the Expected Today control is duplicated (once in the command strip, once in the filter bar as 'Expected Today (0)'), the EST. DELI… column is 100% 'Not set' for every visible row, two column headers are truncated, statuses are rendered as plain text with no color cue, and the critical instruction 'Select a row to see details and actions' is floated as 12px grey copy in dead space to the right of the filters. This is a functional tool undermined by redundant chrome and weak scanability.*

**Keep.** Supplier pivot chips with inline counts (Sierra Nevada Farms 22, Trinity Alps 2, …) make it trivial to scope the queue to a vendor.; Status summary chips next to the 'Purchase Orders' title give an at-a-glance split of draft / confirmed / receiving without a click.; Primary workflow entry points (New Purchase Order, Export CSV, Expected Today) are all visible above the fold and never collapse behind a menu.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `procurement-UX-1` | **P1** | **Expected Today control is duplicated and the top copy is misleading** — There are two Expected Today affordances: a solo 'Expected Today' button in the 'Buying' card at the very top, and 'Expected Today (0)' in the filter row beside 'All statuses'. They both toggle the same `expectedToday=1` query param / `initialShowExpectedToday` filter. The top one shows no count; the bottom one correctly shows (0). | Remove the duplicate button slot in the 'Buying' card and keep only the filter-row pill 'Expected Today (0)', which already displays the live count. Reclaim the empty card space for a compact KPI row (draft / confirmed / receiving / expected today) that clicking filters the queue. | The 'Expected Today' command strip behavior in the baseline (toggles `expectedToday=1` + `initialShowExpectedToday`) is preserved on the filter-row pill, which already fires the same action; only the redundant twin is removed. |
| `procurement-UX-2` | **P1** | **Three duplicate summaries of the same counts stacked above the table** — The counts '1 draft · 10 confirmed · 2 receiving' appear (a) as chips next to the 'Purchase Orders' H2, and then (b) again in prose under 'Purchase Orders Queue': '30 visible purchase orders · 1 draft purchase orders · 10 confirmed purchase orders · 2 receiving purchase orders.' The descriptive sentence 'Unified purchase order queue with status, supplier, dates, total, and payment terms at a glance.' is also pure boilerplate. | Collapse to a single title block: keep the 'Purchase Orders' H2 with its count chips, delete the 'Purchase Orders Queue' header + description + restated counts, and let the table sit directly under the filter row. | PurchaseOrderSurface's queue table and all filters stay untouched — this is a pure layout deletion of a decorative section, not a functional one. |
| `procurement-UX-3` | **P1** | **EST. DELIVERY column is 100% 'Not set' but still consumes a prime column slot** — Every one of the 13 visible rows shows 'Not set' under 'EST. DELI…' (the header itself is truncated). The column adds no information and pushes TOTAL ($) and PAYMENT TERMS further right. | Keep the column but (a) inline-edit the cell with a muted '+ Set date' button rather than dead 'Not set' text, and (b) when 100% of the visible page is unset, collapse the column to a narrow icon column with a tooltip prompt. Unhide automatically once any row has a date. | The `estimatedDeliveryDate` field on the PurchaseOrderSurface row stays writable and the `expectedToday` business rule (delivery date ≤ end-of-day today) continues to read the same field; only the empty-state rendering changes. |
| `procurement-UX-4` | **P1** | **Status values are unstyled text, killing scanability** — The STATUS column renders 'Received', 'Confirmed', 'Sent' as plain grey prose identical in weight to the supplier name next to it. There is no color, badge, or icon differentiating draft/confirmed/sent/received. | Render status as a colored pill: amber for Draft, blue for Sent, violet for Confirmed, green for Received, grey for Cancelled. Keep the text label; only add background + 12px dot. Apply the same style inside the count chips at the top so the palette stays consistent. | The underlying status enum from PurchaseOrderSurface and its status-switch action are unchanged; this is a cell renderer change only. |
| `procurement-UX-5` | **P2** | **'Select a row to see details and actions' is hidden as 12px grey copy next to filters** — The critical instruction telling users that the queue is row-selection-driven is floated to the far right of the filter row, in light grey, at body-small size. At first glance it looks like a secondary filter label, not guidance. | Move this hint into an empty-state panel on the right side of the page (below the filter row) that says 'Select a PO to edit, confirm, split, or receive' with inline icons for each action. When a row is selected, the panel populates with actions; when none is selected, it shows the hint at readable size. | The row-selection-driven detail panel and the underlying action set (edit, confirm, split, receive, cancel/archive, notes, docs, status switch) remain identical; only the idle-state copy becomes visible and persistent. |
| `procurement-UX-6` | **P2** | **Column headers are truncated to ellipses instead of wrapping or resizing** — 'ORDER D…' and 'EST. DELI…' both render with a trailing ellipsis in the header row. Every header also carries a filter icon plus a kebab menu, so the text column gets squeezed first. | Allow header text to wrap to two lines (min-height 40px) before truncating; move the kebab into the filter popover instead of rendering two icons per header; shorten labels to 'Order date' / 'Est. delivery' in sentence case rather than ALL CAPS to recover width. | Column filter and per-column menu actions on PurchaseOrderSurface stay reachable — they are just consolidated into one icon per header instead of two. |
| `procurement-UX-7` | **P2** | **Count chips have broken singular/plural grammar** — The chips beside 'Purchase Orders' read '1 draft purchase orders', '10 confirmed purchase orders', '2 receiving purchase orders'. The queue description repeats '1 draft purchase orders'. | Pluralize via `count === 1 ? 'order' : 'orders'`. Also drop the word 'purchase' inside chips that already sit next to a 'Purchase Orders' H2 — '1 draft', '10 confirmed', '2 receiving' is cleaner and saves horizontal space. | Counts still bind to the same aggregate from PurchaseOrderSurface; only the label template changes. |
| `procurement-UX-8` | **P2** | **'QUEUE FIRST, THEN RECEIVING HANDOFF' tagline is jargon with no call to action** — Directly under the 'Purchase Orders' title sits the all-caps micro-line 'QUEUE FIRST, THEN RECEIVING HANDOFF'. It describes the page's mental model to the engineer who built it, not the user who is about to click 'New Purchase Order'. | Replace with a one-line, lower-case helper: 'Queue draft and confirmed POs here. Click Receive on any row to open receiving.' Remove the all-caps styling so it reads as a subtitle, not a section flag. | The receiving auto-route business rule (`/inventory?tab=receiving&draftId=…`) is unchanged; copy merely describes it accurately. |

**Redesign sketch.** Single-column workspace. Top band: breadcrumb + 'Buying' H1 removed in favor of a single H1 'Purchase orders' with a subtitle helper 'Queue draft and confirmed POs. Click Receive on any row to hand off.' Immediately under the H1, a KPI strip of four clickable tiles — Draft (1), Confirmed (10), Receiving (2), Expected today (0) — replacing both the old top 'Expected Today' button AND the duplicate filter pill; clicking a tile applies the filter. Right side of that row: 'New Purchase Order' (primary) and 'Export CSV' (secondary). Second band: supplier pivot chips (unchanged) on one wrap row. Third band: filter row — search, status dropdown, date range; the 'Select a PO to edit, confirm, split, or receive' hint moves OUT of this row and INTO a persistent right-rail detail panel. Main body: full-width queue table, columns in order — PO #, Supplier, Status (colored pill), Order date, Est. delivery (inline '+ Set date' instead of 'Not set'), Total, Payment terms, with wrapping sentence-case headers and a single combined filter/menu icon per header. Right rail (320px, collapsible): when no row selected, shows action legend (Edit, Confirm, Split, Receive, Cancel, Notes, Attach); when a row is selected, shows that PO's meta + the same actions as buttons. All existing PurchaseOrderSurface behaviors (create, edit, confirm, split, receive-routes-to-inventory, cancel, notes, docs, status switch, Expected Today filter) remain wired to the same trpc calls — only chrome, hierarchy, and cell rendering change.
