#### ProductIntakeSlicePage — `/slice-v1-lab/product-intake` (lightweight)

![ProductIntakeSlicePage](screenshots_all/slice_v1_intake.png)

*The page lands in a hollow empty state: an H1 'Receiving', a dead 'Select receiving draft' dropdown, an action toolbar whose primary button ('Receive') is styled active but cannot do anything, and a data table with headers but zero rows. The user is told twice to go 'Back to Receiving Queue' but the page still spends most of its real estate on a non-functional table and disabled-looking affordances. There is no inline way to pick a PO from here, so the screen is effectively a redirect page dressed up as a workspace. The breadcrumb 'Purchase Order → Receiving → Received' in the header is the clearest signal of where you are, but it is visually buried next to an environment label.*

**Keep.** The three-step breadcrumb 'Purchase Order → Receiving → Received' establishes the intake pipeline clearly and should be preserved.; The action rail (Review / Receive / Activity Log / Attachments / SKU Gallery) is a coherent task vocabulary for a receiving draft and maps to the documented QA-gated flow.; The empty-state copy 'Open a purchase order from the Receiving queue to continue' correctly names the next step rather than showing a blank grid.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `slice_v1_intake-UX-1` | **P1** | **Empty state shows a full toolbar and table that cannot be used** — With 'No active receiving draft' the page still renders the column selector, density toggle, action rail (Review, Receive, Activity Log, Attachments, SKU Gallery), the '0 selected / Clear' bulk bar, and a full column header row. The 'Receive' button is rendered in the active/filled style even though there is nothing to receive. | When `activeDraft` is null, collapse the toolbar and table into a single centered empty-state card containing the existing 'Back to Receiving Queue' button as the primary CTA plus a secondary 'Select receiving draft' dropdown. Keep the action rail mounted but visually disabled (reduced opacity, `aria-disabled`) so its presence is still discoverable. | Preserves the Review/Receive/Activity Log/Attachments/SKU Gallery action rail and the `Select receiving draft` picker — none are removed, only gated on draft presence so they light up the moment a draft is loaded. |
| `slice_v1_intake-UX-2` | **P2** | **Two identical 'Back to Receiving Queue' buttons compete for the same action** — There is a 'Back to Receiving Queue' button in the top filter row and a second, visually different one in the center empty state. Both do the same thing. | Remove the header-row instance only while the draft is null (render it in the centered empty state as the sole primary CTA). When a draft is active, move it back to the header row as a secondary action next to 'Columns'. | The navigation target (Receiving queue route) is retained in both states; only one instance renders at a time, so no handler or route is removed. |
| `slice_v1_intake-UX-3` | **P2** | **H1 'Receiving' duplicates the nav tab and ignores draft context** — The page H1 is a generic 'Receiving' identical to the active top-nav tab label, with a subtitle describing the feature rather than the current object. Once a draft is loaded there is no place for the PO reference or vendor to surface at title level. | Make the H1 dynamic: 'Receiving — {PO reference} · {Brand/Farmer}' when a draft is active, and 'Receiving · No active draft' when empty. Demote the current 'Review to Receive with inline QA gating…' sentence to a one-line helper under the empty-state card only. | Uses the same PO_REFERENCE and BRAND/FARMER fields already exposed in the table columns; no router or data contract changes, purely a title-binding. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row unchanged: brand + breadcrumb 'Purchase Order → Receiving → Received' on the left, top-nav tabs centered, environment tag right. Below it, a context bar whose H1 becomes 'Receiving · No active draft' (or 'Receiving — PO-1042 · Green Ridge Farms' when loaded), with the 'Select receiving draft' dropdown and a compact action rail (Review, Receive, Activity Log, Attachments, SKU Gallery) pinned to the right — all in a disabled state until a draft loads. When empty, replace the entire table region with a single centered card: icon, heading 'No receiving draft selected', body 'Pick a PO from the Receiving queue to start inline QA and receipt.', primary button 'Back to Receiving Queue', secondary inline 'Select receiving draft ▾'. When a draft is active, the card is swapped for the existing columned table (PO Reference, Brand/Farmer, Strain, Category, Packaging, Qty, Cost, Grade, Location, SKU) with the density toggle and Columns picker restored in the header row and the action rail lit up.

#### InventoryBrowseSlicePage — `/slice-v1-lab/inventory` (lightweight)

![InventoryBrowseSlicePage](screenshots_all/slice_v1_inventory.png)

*The page delivers on the 'grid-first browse' promise with a clean table, readable monospace SKUs, a density toggle, and a Columns control — the bones of a competent inventory grid. But the table is doing almost nothing to help an operator actually work inventory: Status is rendered as raw enum tokens (AWAITING_INTAKE, LIVE), Supplier is mostly a bare dash with no explanation of why, numeric columns are right-aligned but the headers drift with them making scan-alignment fuzzy, and every row has a redundant 'Gallery' button instead of the row itself being the click target. The density dropdown and Columns trigger have no visible state (no count of hidden columns, no current view name), so discoverability of the view-mode/drawer features called out in the subtitle is low.*

**Keep.** Monospace SKU column with consistent prefixing makes scanning and copy/paste reliable.; Density control ('Comfortable') + Columns control + search in a single toolbar row is the correct Linear/Ramp-style pattern.; Breadcrumb 'Purchase Order → Receiving → Received' in the header anchors this slice inside the broader PO flow.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `slice_v1_inventory-UX-1` | **P1** | **Status column shows raw enum tokens instead of human labels** — The Status cells render 'AWAITING_INTAKE' and 'LIVE' as uppercase SCREAMING_SNAKE strings with no color semantics — 'LIVE' and 'AWAITING_INTAKE' use the same muted pill treatment, so an operator cannot distinguish sellable inventory from not-yet-received inventory at a glance. | Map the existing status values to title-cased labels ('Awaiting intake', 'Live') and apply a two-tone badge: neutral/amber for awaiting_intake, green for live. Keep the enum value as a `data-status` attribute and in the tooltip so filtering and tests continue to key off the raw token. | The underlying status enum from the inventory query stays identical; this is a presentational mapping in the Status cell renderer, so any column-filter or Columns-toggle behavior keyed on the status field is untouched. |
| `slice_v1_inventory-UX-2` | **P2** | **Per-row 'Gallery' button is redundant and crowds the row** — Every row ends in an identical 'Gallery' pill button — the runtime captured 25 of them in sequence. The row itself is not a click target, so the only way into SKU detail is this one repeated control, and it steals horizontal space from the Supplier column (which is already showing '-' for most rows). | Make the entire row the primary click target that opens the SKU gallery drawer, and demote the per-row affordance to a small icon-only image button that appears on row hover/focus with an aria-label of 'Open gallery for {sku}'. Keep the button in the DOM on focus so keyboard access is preserved. | The SKU gallery drawer trigger referenced in the page subtitle ('SKU gallery drawer') remains reachable via both row click and the hover icon, so no capability is removed — only the default invocation surface changes. |
| `slice_v1_inventory-UX-3` | **P2** | **Toolbar controls have no state and no result count** — The toolbar shows a search input, a 'Comfortable' dropdown, and a 'Columns' button, but nothing tells the user how many rows matched, how many columns are currently hidden, or what view mode is active beyond density. The subtitle advertises 'column controls, view modes, and SKU gallery drawer' but view modes are not visible anywhere on the page. | Add a left-aligned result counter ('13 SKUs') next to the search, badge the Columns button with the hidden-column count ('Columns · 2 hidden' when applicable), and surface the view-mode switch as a segmented control ('Table / Gallery') immediately to the right of density. Keep 'Comfortable' as the density label but render it as a segmented Compact/Comfortable/Spacious toggle so current state is visible without opening the menu. | All three controls (density selector, Columns popover, and the view-modes/gallery drawer referenced in the subtitle) remain intact; the change is purely surfacing their current state inline. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row unchanged (H1 'Inventory Browse' with subtitle). Toolbar becomes: [Search ........] [13 SKUs] · [Table | Gallery segmented] · [Compact | Comfortable | Spacious density] · [Columns · 2 hidden] · overflow menu. Grid columns: SKU (mono) · Product · Status (title-case colored badge: green=Live, amber=Awaiting intake) · On Hand (right-aligned, right-aligned header) · Cost (right-aligned) · Supplier (with an em-dash and muted 'No supplier' tooltip when null) · trailing hover-only icon column for gallery. Row click opens the SKU gallery drawer; Cmd/Ctrl-click opens in a side panel. Empty supplier state uses muted '—' with a tooltip rather than a bare '-'. Keyboard: arrow keys move row focus, Enter opens drawer, G opens gallery — documented in a small '?' affordance next to Columns.

#### PurchaseOrdersSlicePage — `/slice-v1-lab/purchase-orders` (lightweight)

![PurchaseOrdersSlicePage](screenshots_all/slice_v1_po.png)

*The page presents a clear, readable list of POs with a sensible column set (PO / Supplier / Status / Order Date / Expected / Total), but the action bar is a flat row of six disabled-looking buttons that carry equal visual weight regardless of selection state, and the 'Start Receiving' CTA — arguably the point of this queue — is rendered in the same muted style as Activity Log. The EXPECTED column is 100% dashes, Total lacks alignment discipline at the thousands place (e.g. $6054.00 vs $1000.00 formatting inconsistency), and Status sorting is nonexistent so RECEIVED POs dominate the top of a queue whose stated purpose is to 'start receiving.' The helper text 'Select a purchase order row to inspect detail context and start receiving' is doing work that the UI itself should do via hierarchy.*

**Keep.** Clear breadcrumb-style subtitle (Purchase Order → Receiving → Received) orients users to the three-tab workflow.; Status pills are color-coded and legible (RECEIVED green, CONFIRMED darker green, SENT blue).; Density toggle ('Comfortable') and 'Columns' control are surfaced prominently for power users.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `slice_v1_po-UX-1` | **P1** | **Primary action 'Start Receiving' is visually indistinguishable from secondary actions and gives no feedback about selection** — The action row renders Create PO, Place Order, Place Order (Bulk), Start Receiving, and Activity Log at identical weight. 'Start Receiving' appears faintly highlighted but reads as disabled, and the '0 selected / Clear' counter sits far right, disconnected from the button that consumes the selection. Supporting copy 'Select a purchase order row to inspect detail context and start receiving' is required to explain the state. | Promote 'Start Receiving' to a filled primary button (same brown as Create PO or a distinct accent), and make it explicitly disabled with a tooltip ('Select one or more SENT/CONFIRMED POs') when 0 selected. Move the '0 selected' counter directly adjacent to it (e.g. 'Start Receiving (3)'). Group Create PO / Place Order / Place Order (Bulk) as a left cluster, and right-align Activity Log / Columns as utilities. | Retains the Create PO, Place Order, Place Order (Bulk), Start Receiving, Activity Log, and Clear buttons from the runtime button list — only their styling, grouping, and disabled-state copy change; all click handlers and tRPC calls remain wired. |
| `slice_v1_po-UX-2` | **P1** | **Default sort buries actionable POs under completed ones** — The list is sorted newest-first by PO number, so the viewport is dominated by RECEIVED rows (11 of 16 visible). The single SENT row (PO-2026-0019) and four CONFIRMED rows — the only ones that can actually be received — are scattered between finished work. | Default-sort by status priority (SENT → CONFIRMED → RECEIVED), then by order date desc within each group. Keep the current 'All Statuses' filter dropdown; additionally default it to 'Actionable' (SENT + CONFIRMED) with a one-click 'Show received' toggle. Status column should be sortable on click. | The 'All Statuses' filter button in the runtime button list is retained and its options unchanged; only the default value and row ordering heuristic change. Data source and status taxonomy are untouched. |
| `slice_v1_po-UX-3` | **P2** | **EXPECTED column is entirely empty and TOTAL formatting is inconsistent** — Every row in EXPECTED shows '-'. TOTAL mixes $50.00, $500.00, $1000.00, $6054.00 with no thousands separators, so $6054.00 and $1000.00 don't visually align with $500.00 at the decimal — scanning for large orders is harder than necessary. | If 'Expected' (expected delivery date) is genuinely empty across suppliers, hide the column by default and expose it via the existing 'Columns' chooser. Format TOTAL as '$6,054.00' with thousands separators and a tabular-figure font so decimals stack. | The 'Columns' button already exists in the runtime button list; this fix routes the Expected column through that existing chooser rather than removing it. TOTAL values and underlying tRPC fields are unchanged — only the client-side Intl.NumberFormat call changes. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep the H1 'Purchase Orders' and the three-step subtitle. Collapse the toolbar into two rows: row 1 = search (wider) + status filter (default 'Actionable: SENT + CONFIRMED') + density + columns; row 2 = left cluster [Create PO (primary brown), Place Order, Place Order (Bulk)] · right cluster [Activity Log], with a contextual action bar that slides in above the table when rows are selected showing 'N selected · Start Receiving (primary) · Clear'. Table default-sorts SENT first, then CONFIRMED, then RECEIVED; Status column header shows a sort caret. Hide the empty EXPECTED column behind Columns; right-align TOTAL with tabular figures and comma separators. Replace the 'Select a purchase order row…' helper line with an empty-contextual-bar state that only appears when Start Receiving is the relevant next step.

### Relationships & Clients

#### RelationshipsWorkspacePage.clients — `/relationships?tab=clients` (full)

![RelationshipsWorkspacePage.clients](screenshots_all/relationships_clients.png)

*The page has the right bones — tab switcher, KPI strip, search + filter + Quick Add, and a sortable table — but it's drowning in low-signal repetition. Every one of the 40 rows shows the same Seller+Supplier badge stack, the same 'Watch' status, and the same $0.00 / 0 metrics, so the table reads as broken or unseeded even when it isn't. Copy is inconsistent ('Reachable Handles' is engineer jargon, 'Saved' badge has no referent, Quick Add doesn't say what it adds) and the SUPV-prefixed codes in the Clients tab imply suppliers. The heading hierarchy also double-stamps an H1. Underneath all that, the core directory + profile drill-in flow is intact and fast.*

**Keep.** Clear tab model (Clients / Suppliers) matching the baseline's two work surfaces, with Clients selected and visually distinct.; KPI strip (Total, With Debt, LTV) sits next to the tab header so operators get portfolio context before they scan rows.; Every column that should be sortable (Code Name, LTV, Debt, Orders) exposes a sort affordance, and the row chevron plus keyboard-selected row border make the drill-in to ClientProfilePage obvious.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `relationships_clients-UX-1` | **P1** | **Relationship column is pure noise — every row stacks the same Seller + Supplier pair** — All eight visible rows (Sierra Nevada Farms through Humboldt Harvest Co) show an identical 'Seller' / 'Supplier' badge stack in the Relationship column. Move the full role list into the profile page and the All Types filter (which already exists and is empty today). | The VendorsWorkSurface contract (suppliers = clients with isSeller=true) is untouched; we still render both flags, just in a denser chip, and the Suppliers tab continues to filter by isSeller=true. |

Stack email (regular weight) over phone (muted) in the cell, each with its own copy-on-click affordance. Keep the handle-join logic server-side. | No change to the tRPC query returning the email/phone fields — only the column header copy and cell layout are updated. |
| `relationships_clients-UX-5` | **P2** | **Local search placeholder advertises Cmd+K, which is already the global command palette** — The table search input reads 'Search clients… (Cmd+K)' but the top-bar command palette button is also labelled 'CTRL K' and the runtime exposes an H2 'Command Palette'. Leave Cmd/Ctrl+K wired exclusively to the global Command Palette. | The existing client-filter search handler keeps its input binding; only the placeholder string and an added slash-key focus listener change. | `relationships_clients-UX-6` | **P2** | **'Quick Add' button doesn't say what it adds** — The orange primary CTA in the table header says only 'Quick Add' with a plus icon. Keep the plus icon and the orange fill. | Same quick-create modal the button already opens; only the button label is tab-aware. |
| `relationships_clients-UX-7` | **P2** | **'Saved' pill has no referent next to the KPIs** — Between the subtitle and the KPI counters sits a green 'Saved' badge with a check icon. Toolbar row: left = search input with '/' hint, type filter, and a new 'With debt' toggle chip; right = primary 'Add client' button (renamed from Quick Add). Zero metrics render as '—' not '$0.00'. When all rows have null metrics, a dismissible banner explains why: 'Metrics populate after the first invoiced shipment.' Row selection keeps the existing orange focus border and chevron drill-in to ClientProfilePage.

#### RelationshipsWorkspacePage.suppliers — `/relationships?tab=suppliers` (lightweight)

![RelationshipsWorkspacePage.suppliers](screenshots_all/relationships_suppliers.png)

*The Suppliers tab presents a clean, scannable directory with a consistent row pattern, but the page squanders most of its horizontal real estate on near-empty columns. Every supplier shows identical 'Seller / Supplier' chips, $0.00 value, and 0 orders, so the table reads as data-less noise rather than a useful directory. The header stats ('Total: 18, Active: 18, Value: $0.00') echo the same emptiness, and there is no filter, sort control, or segmentation to help an operator find who actually matters. Search and Add Supplier placement are fine; the problem is hierarchy and signal density.*

**Keep.** Clear Clients/Suppliers tab toggle with the active state visible and a persistent Add Supplier CTA in the upper right.; Row layout cleanly pairs display name with SUPV#### ID, making lookup by ID or name both viable.; Header summary band (Total/Active/Value) is a good pattern to keep — it just needs better metrics.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|

Table columns become: Supplier (name + SUPV####, with a tiny 'Seller+Supplier' chip inline), Contact (email + phone), Tags/Region, Last PO (date), Open POs (#), PO spend (scoped by header timeframe), with a chevron to the profile. Empty-state microcopy for zero-activity suppliers: 'No POs yet — Create PO'.

#### ClientProfilePage — `/clients/1` (full)

![ClientProfilePage](screenshots_all/client_profile.png)

*This is effectively a dead-end. The entire 360° profile — Overview, Sales & Pricing, Money, Supply & Inventory, Activity — has been replaced by a single terse sentence ("This relationship profile could not be loaded.") because one tRPC call (presumably `relationshipProfile.*`) failed. The rest of the page has no skeleton, no client identity, no recovery action, no diagnostic. The breadcrumb reads "#1" and the document has no H1, so a user who landed here from search or a deep link has zero context about which client this is or what to do next. Everything the baseline promises for this page is hidden behind a single error dependency.*

**Keep.** The left Sales Quick Actions rail remains available, so the user isn't trapped — they can still jump to New Order, Active Orders, or Recent Customers.; Global chrome (command palette, breadcrumb, notifications, FAB) is preserved, so keyboard shortcuts and navigation still function around the broken panel.; The error is at least contained in a bordered card rather than a raw stack trace or a white screen.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `client_profile-UX-1` | **P0** | **One failed dependency nukes the entire client profile** — A single error string "This relationship profile could not be loaded." replaces every documented section (Overview metrics, Sales & Pricing, Money, Supply & Inventory, Activity). There is no partial render, no client name, no fallback from `clients.getById` or `client360.*` which are independent calls. | Scope the error boundary to only the Overview relationship header. Render the full `LinearWorkspaceShell` with its five tabs regardless; let each section render its own loading/error state from its own router. The relationship card shows the error inline with a Retry button; Money, Activity, etc. continue to load from their independent tRPC calls. | Preserves `relationshipProfile.*` as the source for the relationship header while allowing `clients.getById`, `clientLedger.*`, `credits.*`, `client360.*`, `clientCommunications.*` to drive their own sections per the baseline's section list. |
| `client_profile-UX-2` | **P0** | **No client identity anywhere on a client page** — There is no H1, no page title beyond "TERP [STAGING]", and the breadcrumb reads only "Clients › #1". The user cannot tell which client they are viewing. | Always render an H1 page header with `{client.businessName}` plus a `RelationshipRoleBadge` row beneath it, fed by `clients.getById` (which does not depend on the relationship profile). Replace the breadcrumb token "#1" with the business name, falling back to "Client #1" only if the name is still loading. | Keeps `RelationshipRoleBadge` and `clients.getById` exactly as specified in the baseline; only adds a header region above the shell. |
| `client_profile-UX-3` | **P1** | **Error message gives no cause, no recovery, no next step** — The error card contains a single sentence with no error code, no timestamp, no Retry, no "Back to Clients", no "Report to support", and no hint about whether the problem is permissions, a missing relationship profile record, or a network failure. | Replace the bare string with a structured empty state: icon, title "Couldn't load relationship profile", subtext "Client record loaded, but relationship roles failed to fetch. (code: RP-404 · 12:03:14)", and three actions — "Retry", "Create relationship profile" (if the cause is absence), and "Back to Clients". There are zero tabs in the runtime DOM. | Render the section tab bar (Overview / Sales & Pricing / Money / Supply & Inventory / Activity) unconditionally inside `LinearWorkspaceShell`. Each tab lazy-loads its own data; Overview is the only tab that surfaces the relationship-profile error inline. | Matches the baseline's explicit "Shell: LinearWorkspaceShell with five sections" contract; sections continue to call their baseline tRPC routers independently. |
| `client_profile-UX-5` | **P2** | **Error card floats in a sea of unused canvas** — The error occupies a thin card at the top of a ~900px empty workspace. The proportions read as "page loaded fine, just empty" rather than "dependency failed" — and the floating action button in the bottom right is still clickable with no context about what it does when the page is errored. | Once UX-4 lands, the shell fills the canvas and this is resolved for the normal state. For the isolated relationship-card error, constrain the card to the Overview column width (e.g. 720px) and left-align it under the new H1. Hide or disable the FAB when the primary content region is in an error state, with a tooltip "Unavailable while profile is loading". | FAB behavior (quick actions) is unchanged when the page renders normally; we're only gating it on the error branch of the same component. |
| `client_profile-UX-6` | **P2** | **Quick-actions rail is Sales-only on a dual-role client page** — The left rail is titled "SALES QUICK ACTIONS" with New Order, Active Orders, Sales Catalogue, Recent Customers, Today's Shipments — all customer-side. The baseline explicitly supports suppliers and dual-role clients via `SupplierProfileSection`, yet there are no supplier quick actions (New PO, Open POs, Supplier Catalogue) exposed at the same level. | Make the quick-actions rail role-aware: when `relationshipProfile` resolves as supplier-only show Buy actions; when dual-role show a segmented header (Sales \| Supply) that swaps the five items. Keep the same slot positions and icon language. | Uses the already-loaded relationship role from `relationshipProfile.*`; navigation targets already exist under the Buy menu items — no new routes. |
| `client_profile-UX-7` | **P2** | **No H1/title means poor keyboard and screen-reader orientation** — Playwright capture shows `H1: []`, only "Command Palette" as H2. Tab count is 0. Users default to browser back, which breaks in-app state. | Promote the Back button into the error empty-state action row (next to Retry) with the label "Back to Clients", and ensure it sits inside the visible viewport alongside the H1 breadcrumb trail. | Same Back handler; only its placement and label change. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header band: breadcrumb "Clients › Acme Hemp Co." then H1 "Acme Hemp Co." with `RelationshipRoleBadge` chips (Customer · Supplier), a right-aligned action cluster (Edit Client, Log Activity, Book Appointment, More ⋯). Section tabs pinned below: Overview | Sales & Pricing | Money | Supply & Inventory | Activity. Each tab renders independently; a failure in one section shows an inline empty state (icon + cause + Retry + secondary action) without taking down its siblings. Overview is two-column: left shows relationship summary, quick stats, `FreeformNoteWidget`; right shows `CommentWidget` and recent communications preview with "View all in Activity". Left rail becomes role-aware Quick Actions (Sales set for customers, Supply set for suppliers, segmented control for dual-role). Error microcopy pattern: "Couldn't load {section}. {reason} · {timestamp}" with Retry + contextual secondary (e.g. "Create relationship profile"). FAB remains for logging activity but is disabled with tooltip when the page is in a global error fallback. Title bar: "{Client} · Clients · TERP" so browser tabs and screen readers have context.

#### ClientLedgerPage — `/client-ledger` (lightweight)

![ClientLedgerPage](screenshots_all/client_ledger.png)

*The embedded InvoicesSurface gives this page real substance — AR totals, status filters, bulk actions, and a dense invoice grid all land above the fold. But three things undermine it: the Status column is literally rendering raw HTML (`<span cla...`) instead of a badge, the page has no H1 so the browsing context reduces to the tiny 'Client Ledger' breadcrumb, and the Amount Due / Paid % columns bury the only signal that matters on a ledger (who still owes money) behind visually identical $0.00 / 100% rows. For a page whose entire job is surfacing receivables, the hierarchy treats fully-paid and delinquent invoices with equal weight.*

**Keep.** Header KPIs ($963,104 AR, 0 overdue, 520 total) and the AR Aging shortcut give immediate financial context.; Status-filter chips (All/Draft/Sent/Viewed/Partial/Paid/Overdue/Void) plus contextual bulk actions (Mark Sent, Record Payment, Void, PDF, Print) keep core AR workflows one click away.; Keyboard/selection legend (Click, Shift+Click, Ctrl+Click, Ctrl+C, Escape) is a power-user affordance worth keeping.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `client_ledger-UX-1` | **P0** | **Status column renders raw HTML instead of a badge** — Every row in the STATUS column shows the literal string `<span cla…` (truncated markup) rather than a rendered Paid/Partial/Sent pill. The column is unreadable for all 10 visible invoices. | Render the status cell through the existing badge component (the same one powering the filter chips above) instead of injecting an HTML string into the cell's text node. Map each invoice status to its established color token (Paid=green, Partial=amber, Overdue=red, Sent/Viewed=neutral, Draft=grey, Void=strikethrough). | Leaves the InvoicesSurface grid schema and the underlying invoice status field untouched; only the cell renderer changes from text to badge component. |
| `client_ledger-UX-2` | **P1** | **Delinquent invoices are not visually prioritized** — INV-000116 (Mendocino Naturals, $5,885.76 due, 69% paid) and INV-000111 (Chula Vista, 102% paid — a likely overpayment) sit in identical typography and weight as nine fully-paid rows. The default sort appears to be invoice number descending, so the one row that actually needs action is buried mid-table. | Default-sort by Amount Due desc (or add a secondary sort that floats non-zero Amount Due to the top), bold any non-zero Amount Due value, and color the 102% Paid % cell amber to flag overpayment. Keep the existing column sort affordances so users can re-sort by Invoice # or Due Date. | InvoicesSurface column definitions, filter chips, and the tRPC invoice list query remain intact; this is a default-sort and conditional-formatting change inside the existing grid. |
| `client_ledger-UX-3` | **P2** | **No page heading; 'Invoices' subtitle duplicates the table caption** — The page has no H1 (Playwright confirms `H1: []`). Identity is carried only by the breadcrumb 'Client Ledger', while the card header reads 'Invoices' and the table caption below also reads 'Invoices · 50 visible · 520 total'. A user landing here from the command palette sees two 'Invoices' labels and no explicit 'Client Ledger' title in the content area. | Add an H1 'Client Ledger' above the KPI strip, demote the card header to 'Open Invoices' (or remove it, since the grid caption already labels the table), and keep the KPI chips ($963,104 AR / 0 overdue / 520 total) immediately under the H1. | Per baseline, ClientLedgerPage renders InvoicesSurface — no surface is removed; this only adds a heading wrapper and relabels the duplicated inner card title. |

**Redesign sketch.** Top of content area: H1 'Client Ledger' with a right-aligned 'Search invoice # or client' input. Directly below the H1, a single row of three KPI chips — AR Outstanding $963,104, Overdue 0, Total Invoices 520 — with 'AR Aging' as a secondary link button on the right. Status filter chips (All/Draft/Sent/Viewed/Partial/Paid/Overdue/Void) as a segmented control; bulk-action bar (Create Invoice primary; Mark Sent, Record Payment, Void, PDF, Print secondary) pinned to the right of the chip row. Grid: Invoice # · Client · Invoice Date · Due Date · Total · Amount Due (bold when >0) · Paid % · Status (rendered badge). Default sort: Amount Due desc, then Due Date asc. Row microcopy: overpaid rows show a small amber 'Overpaid' tag next to Paid %. Footer legend and selection counter remain as-is.

#### CreditsWorkspacePage — `/credits` (lightweight)

![CreditsWorkspacePage](screenshots_all/credits.png)

*The dashboard explains the policy-vs-adjustments distinction clearly in prose, but it is almost pure navigation chrome wrapped around four $0.00 tiles. The same three destinations are exposed three times (tabs, header 'Open ...' buttons, and the two large cards with 'Open Capacity Settings' / 'Review Issued Adjustments' CTAs), which creates decision noise without adding capability. The KPI row (Adjustment balance, Adjustments used, Expiring soon) is the most valuable piece of information on the page and it is buried below two explanatory cards, with no timeframe filter, no drill-in, and no empty-state guidance explaining whether $0.00 means 'nothing issued yet' or 'nothing loaded'.*

**Keep.** The 'Keep the concepts separate' footer and the two intro cards do real teaching work — capacity vs. issued adjustments is a genuinely confusing distinction and the copy lands it.; Tab set (Dashboard / Issued Adjustments / Capacity Settings) maps cleanly to the two operator jobs plus an overview.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `credits-UX-1` | **P1** | **Triple-exposed navigation for the same three destinations** — The tab row ('Dashboard', 'Issued Adjustments', 'Capacity Settings'), the top-right button cluster ('Open Dashboard', 'Open Issued Adjustments', 'Open Capacity Settings'), and the two primary cards ('Open Capacity Settings', 'Review Issued Adjustments') all route to the same three places. 'Open Dashboard' from the Dashboard tab is a no-op. | Keep the Dashboard/Issued Adjustments/Capacity Settings tabs as the single navigation surface. Delete the top-right 'Open Dashboard / Open Issued Adjustments / Open Capacity Settings' button group. Keep the contextual CTAs inside the two explanatory cards ('Open Capacity Settings', 'Review Issued Adjustments') since they carry teaching context. | No routes are removed — every destination remains reachable via the tab bar and the two in-card CTAs, so the Capacity Settings page and Issued Adjustments page stay fully discoverable. |
| `credits-UX-2` | **P1** | **KPI tiles are inert, unscoped, and buried** — 'Adjustment balance', 'Adjustments used', and 'Expiring soon' all render $0.00 with no timeframe selector, no click-through, and no indication of whether the zero is real data or an empty state. 'Expiring soon' hardcodes '0 open adjustments in the next 30 days' with no way to change the window. | Promote the KPI row above the two explanatory cards. Make each tile a link into Issued Adjustments pre-filtered by state (open / applied / expiring≤30d). Add a small period selector ('Last 30d ▾') on the row header and surface it on the Expiring tile. When all values are zero, replace the $0.00 with an inline empty-state line ('No adjustments issued yet — Issue your first'). | The underlying Issued Adjustments list/router is unchanged; tiles become pre-filtered entry points into that same view, and no metric is removed. |
| `credits-UX-3` | **P2** | **No primary action for the most common operator task** — The Issued credit adjustments card describes issuing returns/refunds/pricing/goodwill adjustments, but the only CTA is 'Review Issued Adjustments'. There is no 'Issue adjustment' / 'New adjustment' entry point on a page whose own copy frames issuing as a core decision. | Add a secondary 'Issue adjustment' button next to 'Review Issued Adjustments' on the Issued credit adjustments card, wired to the same create flow the Issued Adjustments tab exposes. Mirror with 'Adjust capacity' on the capacity card if that create route exists. | Reuses the existing Issued Adjustments creation route/mutation — no new business logic, just a shortcut entry point on the dashboard. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: H1 'Client Credit' with a single tab row (Dashboard | Issued Adjustments | Capacity Settings) and no duplicate 'Open ...' buttons. Row 1 (KPI strip, full width, 4 columns): Adjustment balance · Adjustments used · Expiring soon (30d ▾) · Issued this period — each tile clickable, routing into Issued Adjustments pre-filtered, with inline empty-state copy when zero. Row 2 (two teaching cards, 50/50): 'Client credit capacity' with CTAs [Open Capacity Settings] [Adjust capacity]; 'Issued credit adjustments' with CTAs [Review Issued Adjustments] [Issue adjustment]. Row 3 (full-width footer callout): 'Keep the concepts separate' explainer, unchanged. Microcopy for empty KPIs: 'No adjustments issued yet' with a subtle link rather than a hard $0.00.

### Accounting

#### AccountingDashboard — `/accounting?tab=dashboard` (full)

![AccountingDashboard](screenshots_all/accounting_dashboard.png)

*The page opens with a clear narrative — three cash KPIs, then a reconciliation block, then an alert — and the numbers are large, readable, and color-coded sensibly. But the dashboard is asymmetric in action: it gives only one primary CTA (Pay Supplier) while $963K / 371 overdue invoices sits to the left with no equivalent receivables action. The sidebar shows 'SALES QUICK ACTIONS' even though the user is inside Finance, so the quick-action rail is wasted space. Several tiles (Queue Pressure 15, Last Reconciled Never, the duplicate 'items need attention' banner) describe state but give no way to act on it, so the above-the-fold area reads more like a status poster than a control center. Tightening CTAs onto the KPI cards, contextualising the sidebar, and reworking the two meta-metrics would recover most of the control-center promise the subhead already makes.*

**Keep.** Opinionated subhead ('Start with the cash-moving work…') frames the dashboard's intent instead of listing widgets.; Three-KPI top row (Receivables / Payables / Queue Pressure) with semantic green/red amounts gives an at-a-glance cash posture.; Reconciliation Summary cleanly separates outstanding vs. unrecorded vs. last-reconciled, which is the right mental model for AR/AP close.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `accounting_dashboard-UX-1` | **P1** | **Sidebar shows 'Sales Quick Actions' while user is in Accounting** — The left rail's pinned block is labelled 'SALES QUICK ACTIONS' with New Order / Active Orders / Sales Catalogue / Recent Customers / Today's Shipments, and the FINANCE group is collapsed — yet the user is deep inside /accounting?tab=dashboard. | Make the quick-actions block context-aware: when the active route starts with /accounting, swap to a 'FINANCE QUICK ACTIONS' set (New Invoice, Record Payment, New Bill, Pay Supplier, Reconcile) and auto-expand the FINANCE nav group. Keep the Sales block as the default for /sales/* routes. | Only the contents of the Quick Actions panel change; the SELL/BUY/OPERATIONS/RELATIONSHIPS/FINANCE/ADMIN nav tree and every link it exposes remain intact, so navigation coverage is unchanged. |

When a date exists, show the date plus a 'Reconcile again' secondary button. | The `ReconciliationSummary` component keeps its existing data shape and tRPC calls; the fix adds a button that deep-links into Bank Accounts → reconcile flow that already exists. |
| `accounting_dashboard-UX-5` | **P2** | **'4 items need attention' banner duplicates the Unrecorded Payments card** — The yellow 'UNRECORDED PAYMENTS: 4 / AR: 2 ($83,543.00) / AP: 2 ($5,800.00)' card already conveys the full breakdown. Immediately below it, a separate warning box repeats '4 items need attention / 2 AR payments without matching invoices / 2 AP payments without matching bills.' | Merge the warning copy into the card itself: keep the yellow tile, and directly under the AR/AP split add two inline action links — 'Match 2 AR payments →' and 'Match 2 AP payments →'. Delete the separate banner panel. | The underlying `ReconciliationSummary` data and its AR/AP split remain; the merged card still routes into the same match-payments flow, just via one panel instead of two. |
| `accounting_dashboard-UX-6` | **P2** | **KPI cards are not clickable and have no data freshness stamp** — The Receivables, Payables and Queue Pressure cards look like tiles but have no hover affordance, no chevron, and no 'as of HH:MM' timestamp. The only way to drill in is to move up to the tab bar and pick 'Invoices' or 'Bills'. | Make the entire KPI card a link target to the corresponding tab with the overdue filter pre-applied, add a right-aligned chevron, and show 'Updated 2 min ago · Refresh' in the card footer driven by the `accounting.*` query's `dataUpdatedAt`. | The cards still consume the same `invoices.*` / `bills.*` / `accounting.*` data; the fix only adds an href and a timestamp reading from the existing query metadata. |

#### AccountingWorkspace.invoices — `/accounting?tab=invoices` (full)

![AccountingWorkspace.invoices](screenshots_all/accounting_invoices.png)

*This is a dense, data-first invoice register with a lot of the right pieces: a clear tab spine, status filter pills, a contextual action bar, summary chips ($963,104 AR / 0 overdue / 520 total), and a column-filter-capable table. But the execution has one flat-out rendering bug (the Status column is leaking raw `<spar...` markup in every row) and several workflow flaws: bulk actions are clickable with zero selection, multiple column headers are truncated, and the 'overdue' chip contradicts the table (Mendocino Naturals has $5,885.56 outstanding against a Sep 28 due date). The shortcut legend dominates the bottom of the screen while the '0 selected · All · 520 total' context is orphaned below the table. This page will feel both broken and confusing to an AR clerk running a daily collections pass.*

**Keep.** Summary chips ($963,104 AR, 0 overdue, 520 total) plus the AR Aging shortcut give an at-a-glance financial posture before the user touches the table.; Status filter pills (All / Draft / Sent / Viewed / Partial / Paid / Overdue / Void) cover the `BillStatusActions`-style state machine and are the right primary slicer for an AR workflow.; Per-column filter affordances and the keyboard shortcut legend (Click / Shift+Click / Ctrl+Click / Ctrl+C / Esc) signal a real power-user grid, not a generic table.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `accounting_invoices-UX-1` | **P0** | **Status column renders raw `<spar...` markup in every row** — The STATUS column shows `<spar...` in every visible row (INV-000120 through INV-000111). A template is leaking the literal opening of a `<span>` tag instead of rendering the status badge. | Restore the status cell renderer: render a color-coded pill (Draft gray, Sent blue, Viewed indigo, Partial amber, Paid green, Overdue red, Void slate). While fixing, widen the column to a minimum of 110px so the longest label ('Overdue') fits without truncation, and escape any user-supplied content rather than injecting HTML strings. | Touches only the cell renderer inside `InvoicesSurface`'s table column definition; the underlying invoice status field and the Draft/Sent/Viewed/Partial/Paid/Overdue/Void state machine remain intact. |
| `accounting_invoices-UX-2` | **P1** | **Bulk action buttons are enabled with zero rows selected** — 'Mark Sent', 'Record Payment', 'Void', 'PDF', and 'Print' all sit in the action bar at full opacity while the footer reads '0 selected · All · 520 total'. None of them can do useful work without a selection. | Disable Mark Sent / Record Payment / Void / PDF / Print when `selectedInvoiceIds.length === 0`, with a tooltip 'Select one or more invoices'. Keep 'Create Invoice' always enabled as the non-selection primary action. | The `InvoicesSurface` lazy sheet's mark-sent, record-payment, void, PDF, and print handlers are untouched — only their enablement predicate and container change. |
| `accounting_invoices-UX-3` | **P1** | **'0 overdue' chip contradicts the data in the table** — The summary chip reads `0 overdue`, but INV-000116 (Mendocino Naturals) shows a due date of Sep 28 2025 with $5,885.56 still outstanding rendered in red, and INV-000111 is at 102% paid (apparent overpayment). The chip is out of sync with the row-level state. | Compute the overdue count from the same query that drives the row-level 'Overdue' status (due_date < today AND amount_due > 0). Make the chip clickable so it filters the table to Overdue (equivalent to the Overdue pill). Add a second chip for overpayments ('1 overpaid' → filters to paid_ratio > 100%) so INV-000111 doesn't vanish into 'Paid'. | Keeps the existing `InvoicesSurface` chip slots and the Overdue status filter pill; only the aggregation query and a new click handler are added. |
| `accounting_invoices-UX-4` | **P1** | **Four column headers are truncated at default width** — INVOICE DATE renders as 'INVOICE ...', AMOUNT DUE as 'AMOUNT D...', PAID % as 'PA...', and STATUS as 'STATU...'. The grid is not allocating minimum widths, and the filter/overflow icons inside each header eat the remaining space. | Set min-widths per column (Invoice Date 120px, Due Date 120px, Total 120px, Amount Due 130px, Paid % 90px, Status 110px). Move the three-dot column menu behind a hover reveal so the label owns the header at rest. Abbreviate 'Paid %' rather than truncating the header. | No change to `InvoicesSurface` column definitions, sort, or filter behaviour — only CSS widths and hover state on the header affordances. |
| `accounting_invoices-UX-5` | **P2** | **Toolbar hierarchy dilutes the primary action and hides AR Aging** — 'Create Invoice' is the only true primary action, yet it shares visual weight with Mark Sent, Record Payment, Void, PDF, and Print on the same row. Separately, 'AR Aging' is isolated on the right of the chip row, far from the other report-style controls, and reads ambiguously — is it a filter, a link, or a drawer? | Promote 'Create Invoice' to a solid-accent button anchored to the top-right of the Invoices panel next to the search. Group Mark Sent / Record Payment / Void / PDF / Print into a contextual selection bar (see UX-2). Relocate 'AR Aging' into a secondary 'Reports ▾' menu beside Create Invoice, with a subtitle 'Open aging buckets report' on hover. | All six existing buttons and the AR Aging route remain reachable; only grouping and visual weight change. `InvoicesSurface`'s handler bindings are untouched. |
| `accounting_invoices-UX-6` | **P2** | **Search input placeholder is clipped** — The search field placeholder renders as 'Search invoice # or clie…' because the input is too narrow for its own hint. Also the search has no visible scope indicator (is it just invoice # / client, or also PO/line items?). | Widen the input to ~320px, rewrite the placeholder to 'Search invoice #, client, PO, or amount', and add a scope hint on focus ('Press / to focus · Ctrl+K for global'). Anchor it to the right of the panel next to the refresh button already present. | No change to the invoice search tRPC call or its fuzzy-match fields; only input width and placeholder copy. |
| `accounting_invoices-UX-7` | **P2** | **Shortcut legend dominates screen while selection state is orphaned** — A five-chip keyboard-shortcut legend (Click / Shift+Click / Ctrl+Click / Ctrl+C / Escape) sits in a large floating panel at the bottom-right, permanently. | `accounting_invoices-UX-8` | **P3** | **Over-payment (102%) on INV-000111 is not flagged** — INV-000111 (Chula Vista Cannabis) shows `102%` in the Paid % column — the customer paid more than invoiced — but the cell is styled identically to the 100% and 69% rows. Amount Due reads $0.00, masking the overpayment. | When paid_ratio > 100%, render the cell in a warning tone with a small 'Overpaid' chip and a tooltip showing the credit amount. A second row holds the status filter pills (All / Draft / Sent / Viewed / Partial / Paid / Overdue / Void) left-aligned, with a small row-count '50 visible · All statuses' at right. The grid has fixed min-widths per column so no header truncates, Status renders as a colored pill, Paid % >100% renders in warning tone with an 'Overpaid' chip, and overdue rows get a red due-date tint computed from due_date < today. A sticky footer under the grid shows '0 selected · All · 520 total · Clear' on the left and a '?' shortcut popover on the right (collapsed by default). When ≥1 row is selected, the top toolbar's Create Invoice area is replaced by a contextual bar 'N selected · Mark Sent · Record Payment · Void · PDF · Print · Clear', so bulk actions only appear when they apply. The AR Aging link, GL reversal viewer, and all existing invoice-sheet drill-downs remain reachable from row click and the Reports menu.

#### BankAccounts — `/accounting?tab=bank-accounts` (lightweight)

![BankAccounts](screenshots_all/accounting_bank_accts.png)

*The page delivers the documented features — a type-segmented table of accounts with the total cash card ($2,075,000.00), an Add Row action, and per-column filter/sort affordances — but the information hierarchy is inverted. The most important number (total cash balance) is a tiny green pill beside the title instead of a headline KPI, the Balance column is truncated to '$1,250,00…' so users cannot read the numbers the page exists to show, and the 'active' state is rendered as a raw checkbox with no label. For a four-row reference table, the dense grid chrome (per-column filter icons, kebab menus, column resizers) is overkill and competes with the data itself.*

**Keep.** Type filter chips (All Types / Checking / Savings / Credit Card / Money Market) give fast segmentation over the four-account list.; Account numbers are masked to last-4 (****6789), which is the correct default for a wholesale ERP.; Total cash, account count, and active count are all surfaced in the header strip rather than hidden in a footer.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `accounting_bank_accts-UX-1` | **P1** | **Balance column truncates the page's headline numbers** — The Balance column renders '$1,250,00…', '$350,000.…', '$500,000.…', '-$25,000.…' — every row is clipped with an ellipsis despite roughly 300px of empty space to the right of the Active checkbox column. | Right-align the Balance column, widen it to fit '$9,999,999.99' at the default zoom, and drop the per-column filter/kebab icons from Balance and Type so the header isn't eating horizontal space. Format negatives as red '-$25,000.00' rather than monospace text. | Baseline 'current balance' column in the accounts table — the fix only changes width, alignment, and formatting, not the data source or tRPC shape. |
| `accounting_bank_accts-UX-2` | **P1** | **Total cash balance is buried as a header pill, not a KPI** — The documented 'total cash balance card' renders as a small green chip ($2,075,000.00) tucked next to the 'Bank Accounts' label, the same visual weight as the '4 accounts' / '4 active' counters. | Promote it to a proper KPI card above the type filter row: large numeric ($2,075,000.00), label 'Total Cash Balance', sublabel '4 accounts · 4 active', right-aligned mini-breakdown by type (Checking $1.6M, Savings $500K, Credit -$25K). Keep the existing tRPC aggregation. | Baseline 'total cash balance card' — fix restores the card treatment the baseline already calls for without changing the underlying sum. |
| `accounting_bank_accts-UX-3` | **P2** | **Active column is a bare checkbox with no label or meaning** — The rightmost column header reads 'BALA…' (the Balance header bleeding) and the cells show only a blue checkbox with no column title visible and no indication whether clicking toggles state or is read-only. | Rename the column 'Status', render values as pill badges ('Active' green / 'Inactive' gray) rather than a checkbox, and move toggling into the row's kebab menu with a confirm step. Fix the TYPE cell values by title-casing ('Credit Card' instead of 'CREDIT_C…'). | Baseline 'active' boolean field — still displayed and still editable, just via an explicit action instead of an ambiguous inline checkbox. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: H1 'Accounting' with the existing tab strip unchanged. Below the 'Bank Accounts' tab, a single full-width KPI card: 'Total Cash Balance — $2,075,000.00', with a right-side mini-breakdown (Checking $1.6M · Savings $500K · Credit Card -$25K · 4 active of 4 accounts). Below that, a single toolbar row: type chips on the left (All Types / Checking / Savings / Credit Card / Money Market), search and refresh in the middle, primary '+ New Bank Account' button on the right (replacing the generic '+ Add Row'). Table columns, left to right: Account Name · Bank · Last 4 · Type (title-cased badge) · Balance (right-aligned, full currency, negatives in red) · Status (Active/Inactive pill) · row kebab (Edit, Deactivate, View transactions). Remove per-column filter/kebab icons from Type, Balance, and Status; keep them only on Account Name and Bank where search is useful. Empty-cell space below the four rows becomes a thin footer 'Showing 4 of 4 accounts'.

#### BankTransactions — `/accounting?tab=bank-transactions` (lightweight)

![BankTransactions](screenshots_all/accounting_bank_txns.png)

*The Bank Transactions tab is a spreadsheet-style ledger but in its empty state it reads as broken: three summary chips show $0.00/0 with no context, the filter bar is duplicated (type chips + status chips) without labels, and the table area is a blank card with no column headers so users can't tell what they're supposed to see. The keyboard-hint cluster floating at the bottom right is helpful but misplaced below the empty card, making it look like a footer rather than table help. Nothing tells a first-time user whether they need to connect a bank account, import a CSV, or manually add rows.*

**Keep.** Two-axis filtering (type: All/Deposit/Withdrawal/Transfer/Fee and status: All/Reconciled/Unreconciled) is the right mental model for reconciliation work.; Summary chips for deposits, withdrawals, and unreconciled count are the correct KPIs to surface at the top.; Inline spreadsheet affordances (Add Row, Toggle Reconciled, Export CSV, click/double-click/ctrl+c legend) match the power-user reconciliation workflow.

A new user cannot tell what fields a transaction has or how to populate the first row. | Always render the column header row (Date, Type, Description, Reference, Amount, Reconciled) even when empty, and replace the generic icon with two primary actions inline: 'Add first transaction' (triggers the existing Add Row) and 'Clear filters' (only when a non-'All' chip is active). Keep the 'No transactions match your filters' copy as secondary text. | Uses the existing '+ Add Row' control and the existing type/status filter chips — no new router or mutation; just renders headers and wires buttons to existing handlers. |
| `accounting_bank_txns-UX-2` | **P2** | **Summary chips and filter chips are visually indistinguishable** — The header row has three pill badges ('$0.00 deposits', '$0.00 withdrawals', '0 unreconciled') immediately above two rows of filter pills ('All/Deposit/Withdrawal/Transfer/Fee' and 'All Status/Reconciled/Unreconciled'). Below KPIs, a single toolbar row: left side two labeled filter groups ('Type:' All·Deposit·Withdrawal·Transfer·Fee / 'Status:' All·Reconciled·Unreconciled); right side action cluster (+ Add Row, Toggle Reconciled, Export CSV, ? shortcuts). The table card always shows column headers (Date · Type · Description · Reference · Amount · Reconciled) with a sticky header row. #### Bills — `/accounting?tab=bills` (lightweight)

![Bills](screenshots_all/accounting_bills.png)

*The Bills table has a strong scaffold — clear sub-tab nav, a useful header strip (AP total, overdue count, total count), status filter pills, and bulk action buttons (Pay Vendor, Mark Received, Void) with a keyboard-shortcut inspector. But two columns — DUE AMT and STATUS — are literally rendering raw HTML strings (`<span class="…">`) instead of values and badges, which torches the table's usefulness and looks broken. On top of that, the Bill # column is truncated to unreadable stubs (`BILL-GF002-LIF…`) and the documented 'create bill dialog' has no visible entry point anywhere on this page, despite Bills being an AP workflow where creation matters.*

**Keep.** Header chip row ($1,088,665 AP / 27 overdue / 27 total) plus AP Aging button gives a strong at-a-glance AP posture before the user touches the table.; Status filter pills (All/Draft/Pending/Approved/Partial/Paid/Overdue/Void) sit right above bulk actions (Pay Vendor, Mark Received, Void), which maps cleanly to the BillStatusActions state machine.; Persistent keyboard-shortcut inspector (Click/Shift+Click/Ctrl+Click/Ctrl+C/Escape) teaches power-user selection behavior without stealing screen space from the table.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `accounting_bills-UX-1` | **P0** | **DUE AMT and STATUS columns render raw HTML instead of values** — Every row in the DUE AMT and STATUS columns shows the literal string `<span class="…">` instead of a dollar amount or a status badge. The two most decision-critical columns on an AP page are unreadable. | Render the cell as the computed value, not the HTML template string: DUE AMT should be a right-aligned currency (e.g. `$500.00`, dimmed when $0, red when > 0 and past due); STATUS should be a colored pill matching the filter chip palette (Draft grey, Pending amber, Approved blue, Partial violet, Paid green, Overdue red, Void slate). Fix the cell renderer so the span's text content is passed, not its markup. | Leaves the existing column definitions, sortable/filterable table, and BillStatusTimeline/BillStatusActions state machine untouched — only the cell renderer changes so the already-computed due amount and status string are displayed instead of escaped HTML. |
| `accounting_bills-UX-2` | **P1** | **Bill # column truncates the only unique identifier** — Every Bill # is cut to ~14 chars with an ellipsis (`BILL-GF002-LIF…`, `BILL-GF002-177…`, `BILL-20260219-…`), so six consecutive rows look identical and the user cannot distinguish bills without clicking each one. | Widen the Bill # column to fit the longest ID (~22 chars) and shrink the over-wide empty space in DUE AMT/STATUS once they render properly. If space is tight, keep truncation but add a tooltip on hover showing the full ID, and make the ID itself a monospace link to the detail sheet. | Does not change the table schema, sort, or the `?billId=` deep-link — only column width and hover affordance. Detail sheet opening behavior is unaffected. |
| `accounting_bills-UX-3` | **P1** | **No visible entry point for the Create Bill dialog** — The baseline documents a 'create bill dialog,' but the Bills header shows only a search box and a refresh icon. Keep the Ctrl+K route as a power-user path. | Wires the existing create bill dialog to a visible trigger; no router, mutation, or BillStatusActions behavior changes. The dialog component itself is unchanged. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep the Accounting H1 and the sub-tab row. Bills sub-header becomes two rows: (row 1) title `Bills` + chip strip `$1,088,665 AP · 27 overdue · 27 total` on the left, and on the right `AP Aging`, search, refresh, and a primary `+ New Bill`; (row 2) status filter pills on the left, bulk action buttons on the right, with a live `N selected` counter that replaces the '0 selected' footer when rows are checked. #### Expenses — `/accounting?tab=expenses` (lightweight)

![Expenses](screenshots_all/accounting_expenses.png)

*The Expenses tab loads into a spreadsheet grid that is entirely empty with no obvious path to create the first expense beyond a small '+ Add Row' button aligned right. The summary chips ($0.00 total · 0 entries · 0 pending reimbursement) are useful but visually compete with the page title. Category CRUD and category-breakdown cards promised by the baseline are nowhere visible on the empty state, so the user has no way to set up categories before adding expenses. Keyboard hints are helpful but occupy disproportionate screen real estate relative to the one action (Add Row) a new user actually needs.*

**Keep.** Summary chips surface total, entry count, and pending reimbursement inline with the section title — fast scan for finance users.; Keyboard hint panel teaches spreadsheet interactions explicitly, which matches the grid paradigm.; Filter controls (All Categories, Reimbursable only) are placed directly above the grid where expected.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `accounting_expenses-UX-1` | **P1** | **Empty state doesn't guide first expense creation** — The grid shows a generic file icon with 'No expenses — No expenses match your filters' even when there are zero expenses total (0 entries, 0 total). The only CTA is a small '+ Add Row' button in the toolbar corner; there's no primary action inside the empty canvas. | Conditional empty state: when total entries = 0, show 'No expenses yet. Add your first expense to start tracking reimbursables and category spend.' with a prominent 'Add Expense' button (same handler as + Add Row) and a secondary 'Manage Categories' link. Keep the current 'No expenses match your filters' copy only when a filter is active. | Reuses the existing + Add Row action and category CRUD entry points from the baseline — only the empty-state copy and CTA placement change. |
| `accounting_expenses-UX-2` | **P2** | **Category-breakdown cards and category CRUD are not discoverable** — Baseline lists 'category-breakdown cards' and 'category CRUD' as features, but the rendered page shows only a flat 'All Categories' dropdown filter and no way to create/edit categories or view spend-by-category. | Add a collapsible 'Categories' strip above the grid with breakdown cards (category name, total, count, reimbursable badge) and an overflow menu on each card for Rename/Archive. Add a 'Manage categories' button next to the 'All Categories' filter dropdown that opens the existing category CRUD. | Surfaces the baseline's category CRUD and category-breakdown-cards features without altering their data model or tRPC contracts. |
| `accounting_expenses-UX-3` | **P3** | **Keyboard hint panel dominates the empty viewport** — The six keyboard shortcuts (Click, Double-click, Ctrl+C, Ctrl+V, Ctrl+Z, Escape) render as a large pill cluster bottom-right, taking more visual weight than the primary Add Row CTA. | Collapse the hints into a single '?' icon (or 'Shortcuts' link) that reveals the panel on hover/click, and suppress it entirely when the grid is empty. Preserve all six shortcut labels inside the expanded popover. | No shortcut is removed; behaviors (select, edit, copy, paste, undo, cancel) remain globally bound — only the hint chrome is collapsed. |

**Redesign sketch.** Heading row: 'Expenses' H2 with inline muted meta chips ($0.00 total · 0 entries · 0 pending reimbursement) and a right-aligned primary 'Add Expense' button plus secondary 'Export CSV' and overflow menu containing 'Manage Categories'. Below the heading, a horizontally scrollable strip of category breakdown cards (name, total, count) — hidden when no categories exist, replaced by a 'Create your first category' inline prompt. Filter bar below: 'All Categories' dropdown, 'Reimbursable only' toggle, search on the right. Grid fills remaining space; when empty and unfiltered, show a centered empty state with icon, 'No expenses yet' headline, subcopy explaining reimbursable tracking, and an 'Add Expense' primary button. Keyboard hints collapse to a '?' chip bottom-right that expands to the current six-shortcut popover. Status footer ('0 selected | All Categories | 0 total') stays as-is beneath the grid.

#### FiscalPeriods — `/accounting?tab=fiscal-periods` (lightweight)

![FiscalPeriods](screenshots_all/accounting_fiscal.png)

*The Fiscal Periods tab has the right scaffolding (status filter pills, + Add Row, Close/Lock actions, a spreadsheet-style empty state with keyboard hints) but fails the zero-state moment badly. The empty table shows a generic 'No fiscal periods' message with no onboarding toward the primary action, and the Close Period / Lock Period buttons sit enabled in the toolbar despite there being nothing to close or lock. The 'Fiscal Periods' label also duplicates itself twice within 80px of vertical space (section header and card header), which makes the page feel unfinished. For an accounting surface where period setup is a prerequisite for closing the books, first-run guidance is the critical missing piece.*

**Keep.** Status filter pills (All / Open / Closed / Locked) map directly to the documented period lifecycle and are immediately scannable.; Keyboard shortcut legend (Click, Double-click, Ctrl+C, Ctrl+V, Ctrl+Z, Escape) teaches the spreadsheet interaction model without a modal.; Tab navigation keeps Fiscal Periods adjacent to Bank Transactions and General Ledger, which is the correct month-end mental model.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `accounting_fiscal-UX-1` | **P1** | **Empty state dead-ends the first-run user** — With zero periods, the table body shows only a file icon, 'No fiscal periods', and the misleading subline 'No fiscal periods match your filters' — but no filter is actually applied (All is selected). There is no CTA pointing at the '+ Add Row' button in the toolbar. | When the underlying period count is 0 (not just the filtered count), swap the empty state to: heading 'Set up your first fiscal period', body 'Define a date range so invoices and journal entries can post to a book', and a primary button 'Create fiscal period' that triggers the same handler as '+ Add Row'. Reserve the current 'No periods match your filters' copy for the case where totalCount > 0 but filteredCount === 0. | Reuses the existing '+ Add Row' / date-range calendar popover from the Features list; only swaps empty-state copy and adds a second entry point to the same create action. |
| `accounting_fiscal-UX-2` | **P2** | **Close Period and Lock Period are enabled with nothing selected** — The toolbar status bar reads '0 selected \| All Statuses \| 0 total' yet the 'Close Period' and 'Lock Period' buttons are fully enabled with no visual affordance that they require a selected row. | Disable both buttons when selectedCount === 0, with tooltip 'Select a period to close' / 'Select a closed period to lock'. Keep '+ Add Row' always enabled. When a row is selected, also show the selected period's label next to the buttons (e.g., 'Close Period — Q3 2025'). | Preserves the documented open/close period action and the journal-entry-exists warning; disabling is conditional on selection state, not removal of capability. |
| `accounting_fiscal-UX-3` | **P3** | **Duplicate 'Fiscal Periods' headings stack vertically** — The card header shows 'Fiscal Periods  [0 periods]' at the top, and then a second bold 'Fiscal Periods' label sits directly above the empty table body with no distinguishing information. | Remove the inner 'Fiscal Periods' label above the table body; the outer card header already provides the count and identity. If the inner label is serving as a column-group header, replace it with the actual column headers the grid will render (Period Name, Start Date, End Date, Status, Journal Entries). | Pure typographic dedup; no router, data, or interaction behavior is touched. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep tab strip and the single card. Card header: 'Fiscal Periods' on the left with the [0 periods] badge; search and refresh on the right (as today). Second row: segmented status pills (All/Open/Closed/Locked) on the left, and a right-aligned action cluster where '+ New Period' is the primary filled button and 'Close Period' / 'Lock Period' are secondary, disabled until a row is selected with tooltips explaining the rule. Body: when totalPeriods === 0, render a centered empty state — ledger icon, 'Set up your first fiscal period', one-line rationale about posting and close, and a primary 'Create fiscal period' button that opens the existing date-range calendar popover. When periods exist, render the spreadsheet grid with columns Period | Start | End | Status (colored chip) | Journal Entries (count) | Last Modified, and keep the keyboard shortcut legend docked in the footer next to the '{n} selected | {status} | {total}' summary.

#### GeneralLedger — `/accounting?tab=general-ledger` (lightweight)

![GeneralLedger](screenshots_all/accounting_gl.png)

*The ledger has the right ingredients — account filter, fiscal period, date range, status tabs, running balance, Trial Balance, Post/Reverse/Export actions, and keyboard power-user hints — but it loads into a dead empty state because nothing is defaulted. Worse, the toolbar mixes three different concerns (status filters, a balance readout styled like a filter, and primary actions) on one line, and the keyboard-shortcut inspector takes up a quarter of the viewport while there is literally nothing to inspect. A trained bookkeeper will still get work done, but the first 10 seconds on this page communicate 'empty and confusing' rather than 'pick an account to begin'.*

**Keep.** Full filter surface (account, fiscal period, date range, status, search) is present without being hidden in a drawer.; Primary ledger actions (Post Journal Entry, Reverse Entry, Export CSV, Trial Balance) are all one click away.; Keyboard shortcut inspector (Click, Shift+Click, Ctrl+Click, Ctrl+C, Escape) is a nice power-user affordance for a spreadsheet-style grid.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `accounting_gl-UX-1` | **P1** | **Page loads empty because no filters are defaulted** — Both 'Select account…' and 'Select fiscal period…' are unset on mount, the date inputs read mm/dd/yyyy, and the grid shows 'No ledger entries — Adjust filters or post a new journal entry.' A user who just wants to see this month's activity has to make 2–3 picks before anything appears. | Default fiscal period to the current open period (from the Fiscal Periods tab data) and default account to 'All accounts' so the grid renders on load. Leave the selects fully editable; show the defaulted values as chips the user can clear. | Uses the same fiscal-period and account filter inputs already wired to the ledger query; we only change initial state, so the 'Filter/sort ledger entries' feature from the baseline is untouched. |
| `accounting_gl-UX-2` | **P2** | **'Balance: $0.00' chip is styled like a status filter** — In the toolbar row, 'All / Posted / Draft' are segmented filter pills and immediately to their right sits a pill labeled 'Balance: $0.00' in the same pill shape and color family. It reads as a fourth clickable filter. | Move the balance out of the filter pill group and render it as a right-aligned, label+value readout ('Filtered balance: $0.00') with a different weight/treatment than the segmented control. Keep it in the same toolbar row so it still updates with filters. | The balance is still displayed and still reactive to the same filter state; only typography and grouping change, so the baseline detail dialog and filter behavior are unaffected. |
| `accounting_gl-UX-3` | **P2** | **Keyboard-shortcut inspector dominates the empty state and Reverse Entry looks enabled with no selection** — When the grid is empty, a large cluster of shortcut hints (Click select row, Shift+Click extend range, Ctrl+Click add to selection, Ctrl+C copy cells, Escape close inspector) anchors the bottom of the content area, competing with the 'No ledger entries' illustration. Meanwhile 'Reverse Entry' in the action row does not visibly differ from Post Journal Entry / Export CSV even though '0 selected' is shown in the footer. | Collapse the shortcut hints into a small '? Shortcuts' popover anchored bottom-right when the grid is empty or unfocused, and expand them inline only once ≥1 row exists. Disable the Reverse Entry button (reduced opacity + tooltip 'Select a posted entry to reverse') whenever selection count is 0. | All shortcut affordances and the Reverse Entry action remain available and wired to the same handlers; we only gate their visibility/enabled state on grid content and selection, preserving the 'Filter/sort ledger entries' and reverse-entry behaviors from the baseline. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row: 'General Ledger' H2 with a right-aligned summary strip ('Filtered balance $X · N entries · Period: 2025-Q1'). Row 2 (filters): Account select (defaulted to All accounts), Fiscal Period select (defaulted to current open period), From/To dates with visible labels, and Search on the far right. Row 3 (view + actions): segmented control 'All / Posted / Draft' on the left; on the right a grouped action cluster 'Post Journal Entry (primary) · Reverse Entry (disabled until selection) · Trial Balance · Export CSV'. Main area: ledger grid with sticky header, running-balance column, and inline row-expand for line items (reusing the baseline detail dialog on double-click). Empty state centered: icon, 'No entries for this filter', one-line helper, and a single 'Post Journal Entry' CTA — no shortcut wall. A small '? Shortcuts' pill bottom-right opens the full inspector on demand once rows exist.

#### Payments — `/accounting?tab=payments` (lightweight)

![Payments](screenshots_all/accounting_payments.png)

*The Payments tab gives a clean ledger with useful top-line totals (283, $4.97M received, $5,800 sent) and filter chips for Received/Sent. But the TYPE column is rendering raw HTML markup ('<span clas...') instead of a styled badge, which is an embarrassing P0 data-integrity-looking bug. The Reference column leaks internal IDs like 'No reference' and raw hashes where a method-specific label would read better, and the 4 unrecorded payments surfaced on the dashboard ('2 AR without matching invoices, 2 AP without matching bills') have no visible affordance here to triage them. The keyboard hint footer is a nice touch and the action split (Record Payment vs Void) is clear.*

**Keep.** Header totals ($4,973,788 received / $5,800 sent / 283 total) give immediate financial context before the table loads.; Keyboard affordance footer (Click/Shift+Click/Ctrl+Click/Ctrl+C/Escape) is discoverable and power-user friendly.; Received/Sent/All segmented filter is the right primary cut for a payment ledger.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `accounting_payments-UX-1` | **P0** | **TYPE column renders raw HTML instead of a badge** — Every row in the TYPE column shows the truncated literal string '<span clas…' rather than a rendered Received/Sent status pill. The actual payment type (ACH, CASH, CHECK, etc.) is shown in the METHOD column, so TYPE is both broken and duplicative-looking. | Escape/render the status badge HTML properly so TYPE displays a colored pill ('Received' green, 'Sent' amber, 'Void' grey). If the column is meant to show direction, rename the header to 'DIRECTION' to disambiguate from METHOD. | Touches only the cell renderer for the `paymentType` column documented in the baseline's filterable-table spec; filtering/sorting on `paymentType` is unchanged. |
| `accounting_payments-UX-2` | **P1** | **No path from 'Unrecorded Payments' alert to this registry** — The dashboard flags '4 unrecorded payments · 2 AR without matching invoices · 2 AP without matching bills', but on the Payments tab there is no chip, filter, or banner to isolate those 4 rows among 283. The 'Sent $5,800' total in the header matches the AP figure but is not clickable. | Make the '$4,973,788 received' and '$5,800 sent' totals clickable filters, and add a fourth chip 'Unmatched (4)' next to All/Received/Sent that filters to payments with no linked invoice/bill. Add a subtle amber row indicator for unmatched rows. | Uses the existing `paymentType` filter plumbing and the `?invoiceId=`/`?orderId=` deep-link schema; no new router surface, just a preset filter state. |
| `accounting_payments-UX-3` | **P2** | **Void action is ambiguous with no row selected** — The 'Void' button sits in the top-right next to 'Record Payment' with no selection state shown. It is unclear whether clicking it opens a void-by-ID dialog, voids the highlighted row, or is disabled until selection — and there is no selection checkbox column visible. | Disable 'Void' until a row is selected, and when enabled, change its label to 'Void PAY-000060' (the selected payment #). Move 'Void' into the detail drawer as the primary destructive action rather than a top-bar button so it is always scoped to a specific payment. | Void action and the row→drawer selection flow from the baseline ('Select a row to see details and take actions') are retained; only the button's enabled-state and label binding change. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep the 'Accounting' H1 and tab bar untouched. Under the tab strip, render a compact header row: 'Payments' title on the left; on the right, three clickable KPI tiles — Total (283) · Received ($4,973,788) · Sent ($5,800) — each acting as a filter preset. Below that, a single control bar: segmented [All · Received · Sent · Unmatched (4)] on the left, search on the right, and a meatball menu for column visibility. Move 'Record Payment' to a primary button top-right; remove the standalone 'Void' and make it a destructive action inside the row drawer. Table columns: PAYMENT # · DATE · DIRECTION (rendered badge, green/amber) · METHOD · AMOUNT (right-aligned, signed) · INVOICE/BILL · REFERENCE. Unmatched rows get a left-edge amber bar and a 'Link…' inline action. Keep the keyboard-hint footer pinned.
