### Analytics

#### AnalyticsPage — `/analytics` (full)

![AnalyticsPage](screenshots_all/analytics.png)

*The page has a clean header, a reasonable KPI grid, and the right tab scaffolding (Overview/Sales/Inventory/Clients) to support deeper drill-downs, but the content currently undermines its own premise. With 'Last 30 days' selected, Period Revenue reads $761.32 with '1 this period' order — yet the tile next to it shows Avg Order Value $63,840.06 and Total Revenue $36M, and the Revenue Trends table below renders six months of data (2025-04 through 2025-09). The user literally cannot tell which tiles obey the period selector and which are all-time, which is a trust-killer for an analytics surface. There is also no actual visualization on a page called Analytics — just a flat table — and only one of the eight KPI tiles carries a delta, leaving the rest without a baseline to judge against.*

**Keep.** Tabbed structure (Overview/Sales/Inventory/Clients) pre-segments the analytics workload into recognizable buckets instead of one infinite scroll.; KPI tiles are readable: large numeric weight, consistent tile footprint, one-line subtext under each number.; Global period selector and Export live in the top-right where an operator expects them, adjacent to the H1.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `analytics-UX-1` | **P0** | **KPI tiles mix period-scoped and all-time values with no visual distinction** — With 'Last 30 days' active, Period Revenue shows $761.32 (-99.7%) while Total Revenue shows $36,261,153.77, Outstanding Balance shows $31,281,565.32, Payments Received shows $4,979,588.45, and Avg Order Value shows $63,840.06. The subtexts ('Total from all orders' vs 'Average per order' vs 'Unpaid invoices') are inconsistent about scope, so the user cannot tell which tiles respect the selector and which ignore it. | Segment the 8 tiles into two clearly labeled bands: a top row 'This period · Last 30 days' (Period Revenue, Orders in Period, New Clients, Period Avg Order Value) and a second row 'All time' (Total Revenue, Outstanding Balance, Payments Received, Active Batches). Add a small muted pill 'Period' or 'All time' to each tile's header so scope is never ambiguous even when the user scrolls. Keep identical tile chrome and icons. | Uses the same `analytics.getExtendedSummary` payload and the same MetricCard components — only the tile grouping, header pill, and subtext copy change; no KPI is removed. |
| `analytics-UX-2` | **P0** | **Revenue Trends table ignores the selected period** — The period selector reads 'Last 30 days', but the Revenue Trends table lists 2025-04, 2025-05, 2025-06, 2025-07, 2025-08, 2025-09 — six monthly rows. The baseline states the page 'fetches granularity-aware trends (day for short periods, month otherwise)', so 30 days should render ~30 daily rows, not 6 monthly ones. | Bind RevenueTrendsTable to the same period state as the KPI band and honor the granularity rule from the baseline: ≤31 days → daily rows, 32–180 days → weekly, >180 days → monthly. Label the Period column header with the granularity in use ('Day', 'Week', 'Month'). Add a one-line caption under 'Revenue Trends' reading 'Daily revenue over the last 30 days' that updates with the selector. | Calls the same `analytics.getRevenueTrends` router that already supports granularity per the baseline; the fix just wires the selector through and surfaces the current granularity in the caption. |
| `analytics-UX-3` | **P1** | **No chart on a page called Analytics** — The Revenue Trends section is a pure 4-column table (Period, Revenue, Orders, Avg Order). There is no line, bar, or sparkline anywhere on the page, including the KPI tiles. | Add a Revenue Trends line chart above the existing table, sharing the same data source. Keep the table intact beneath it as the tabular drill-down. Add 30-day sparklines inside the Period Revenue, Total Orders, Active Clients, and Payments Received tiles using the same trend data. | Uses the existing `analytics.getRevenueTrends` payload; RevenueTrendsTable stays exactly as documented in the baseline — the chart is additive. |
| `analytics-UX-4` | **P1** | **Export button hides its four datasets and two formats behind a single label** — The top-right control reads 'Export' with a download icon but no caret or hint that it's a dropdown. The baseline specifies four distinct datasets (summary/revenue/clients/inventory) × two formats (CSV/JSON). | Render as a split-menu button: primary action 'Export summary (CSV)' with a caret on the right that opens a menu grouped by dataset (Summary, Revenue, Clients, Inventory) with a CSV/JSON toggle at the top of the menu. Persist the last-used dataset+format as the default primary action via a per-user preference. | Hits the same `analytics.exportData` router with the same four datasets and two formats from the baseline; only the control pattern and default selection change. |
| `analytics-UX-5` | **P1** | **Only one tile shows a delta; the rest lack a comparison baseline** — Period Revenue shows '-99.7% vs previous period' in red. The other seven tiles — Total Revenue, Avg Order Value, Outstanding Balance, Total Orders, Active Clients, Batches, Payments Received — carry no comparison, only a static subtext. | On every period-scoped tile, render a delta row under the number in the same pattern as Period Revenue: arrow + %Δ + 'vs previous period', with green/red semantic color. For all-time tiles (Outstanding Balance, Total Revenue, Batches), replace the delta row with a muted 'as of today' timestamp so the absence is intentional rather than omitted. | `analytics.getExtendedSummary` already returns the previous-period comparison used by Period Revenue; the fix fans the same pattern out to the other fields the router exposes, touching only MetricCard composition. |
| `analytics-UX-6` | **P2** | **KPI tile icons are decorative and in one case wrong** — Outstanding Balance carries a percent-sign icon (%), which signals a rate, not a dollar balance. Total Revenue, Avg Order Value, and Payments Received all carry a generic '$' icon, giving no visual differentiation between the four money tiles. | Replace the percent on Outstanding Balance with a clock/hourglass 'aging' glyph. Differentiate money tiles by semantic glyph: Total Revenue → stacked-bars, Avg Order Value → receipt, Payments Received → check-circle, Outstanding Balance → clock. Keep glyph position and size identical so layout is unchanged. | Pure icon swap inside MetricCard; no data, router, or layout change. |
| `analytics-UX-7` | **P2** | **Tile subtext copy is inconsistent and often ambiguous** — Subtexts read 'Total from all orders', 'Average per order', 'Unpaid invoices', '1 this period', '6 new this period', 'Active batches in inventory', 'Total collected'. The grammar oscillates between scope descriptors, counts, and raw labels, and 'Average per order' never says over what window. | Standardize to the pattern '<Count/Scope> · <Window>': 'All orders · all time', 'Per order · last 30 days', '1 order · last 30 days', '6 new · last 30 days', 'Active batches · now', 'Collected · all time'. Use a dot separator and Sentence case. Replace ambiguous '1 this period' with explicit 'orders' or 'new'. | Copy-only change inside MetricCard instances; no router or data contract impact. |
| `analytics-UX-8` | **P3** | **'Back to Dashboard' link is redundant with the active sidebar state** — The left sidebar already shows Analytics as the active nav item (green bar + highlight), and the top breadcrumb shows Home › Analytics. Yet a third 'Back to Dashboard' link with left arrow sits above the H1. | Remove the 'Back to Dashboard' row and rely on the existing breadcrumb (Home › Analytics) for upward navigation. Lift the H1 and subtitle to the first row. The recovered vertical space lets the KPI band and the new trend chart sit above the fold. | Navigation intent is preserved by the existing breadcrumb row visible in the DOM; no routes are removed. |

**Redesign sketch.** Top bar (unchanged): breadcrumb, search, notifications, user. Page header row: H1 'Analytics' + subtitle on the left; on the right a period selector ('Last 30 days ▾') and a split-menu Export ('Export summary (CSV) ▾'). Immediately below the header, the four tabs (Overview / Sales / Inventory / Clients) remain as the primary pivot. Overview body is then organized in three bands, each with a small uppercase eyebrow label: (1) 'This period · Last 30 days' — 4 KPI tiles (Period Revenue, Orders, New Clients, Avg Order Value) each with a sparkline and a green/red %Δ row. (2) 'All time' — 4 KPI tiles (Total Revenue, Payments Received, Outstanding Balance, Active Batches) each with an 'as of today' timestamp in place of the delta. (3) 'Revenue trends · Daily over last 30 days' — a line chart with Revenue (primary axis) and Orders (secondary), followed by the existing RevenueTrendsTable underneath acting as the numeric drill-down with a granularity column header that reflects the current binning. Below that, a 'Top clients · Last 30 days' section housing TopClientsTable with client name, revenue, order count, and trend arrow. Iconography is semantic (bar-chart, receipt, check-circle, clock) and every tile carries both a scope pill ('Period' or 'All time') and a one-line subtext in the pattern '<scope> · <window>'. The Sales / Inventory / Clients tabs reuse the same three-band pattern scoped to their domain.

### VIP Portal

#### VIPDashboard — `/vip-portal/dashboard` (full)

![VIPDashboard](screenshots_all/vip_dashboard.png)

*The dashboard route itself could not be evaluated because `/vip-portal/dashboard` redirects unauthenticated sessions to `/vip-portal/login`, which is what actually rendered. The visible login gate is functional but minimal: a centered card with email, password, Sign In, and a forgot-password link on a bare cream canvas. It works, but it reads as a generic Tailwind starter — there is zero TERP branding, no indication which client's portal this is, no show/password affordance, no support path if login fails, and an internal-looking 'Command Palette' FAB is leaking onto a client-facing surface. For a B2B hemp/THCA wholesale portal where buyers handle invoices and live-buy inventory, the first-touch screen needs to feel like a verified, account-specific front door, not a stock auth template.*

**Keep.** Form is short, vertically centered, and focus order (Email → Password → Sign In) is correct — no unnecessary friction on the critical path.; Primary action 'Sign In' is a full-width, high-contrast terracotta button that matches the TERP accent color, so the CTA is unambiguous.; Secondary action 'Forgot password?' is present and keeps the account-recovery path discoverable on the same screen.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `vip_dashboard-UX-1` | **P1** | **Internal Command Palette FAB is exposed on the client-facing login** — A black circular FAB (runtime H2 'Command Palette', with 'Manage MCP & Webhooks' buttons in its tree) renders in the bottom-right of the VIP login page. This is an operator/admin tool and has no business on an external client surface. | Gate the Command Palette mount on an authenticated admin/impersonation role (or on routes outside `/vip-portal/*`). On `/vip-portal/login` and VIP-portal routes without an admin session, do not render the FAB at all. | The Command Palette component and its 'Manage MCP & Webhooks' actions remain fully available in admin shells; this is a mount-condition change, not a feature removal. The `ImpersonationBanner` path still exposes admin context when a real admin is impersonating a VIP. |
| `vip_dashboard-UX-2` | **P1** | **Login header is generic 'VIP Client Portal' with no TERP brand or client context** — The card title reads 'VIP Client Portal' with subtitle 'Sign in to access your account'. There is no TERP wordmark, no logo, no account/company name, and nothing visually tying this screen to the hemp/THCA wholesale business. | Above the card, add the TERP wordmark + a one-line tagline ('Wholesale portal for approved buyers'). Change the card title to 'Sign in to TERP' with a subheading 'VIP Client Portal'. Keep the form unchanged. | The `VIPDashboard` auth flow, tRPC login mutation, and post-login routing to `/vip-portal/dashboard` are untouched; this is pure header/brand chrome above the existing form. |
| `vip_dashboard-UX-3` | **P2** | **Password field has no show/hide toggle** — The Password input renders as masked dots with no trailing eye icon or 'Show' control. Users who mistype on a laptop keyboard have no way to verify the value before submitting. | Add a trailing eye/eye-off icon button inside the Password input that toggles `type` between `password` and `text`. Announce state via `aria-pressed`. | The password field name, validation, and submit payload to the VIP auth endpoint stay identical — only the rendered input type is toggled client-side. |
| `vip_dashboard-UX-4` | **P2** | **No support path if a buyer cannot sign in** — The card offers only 'Sign In' and 'Forgot password?'. There is no 'Need help?', no rep contact, and no link back to a marketing/contact page. A buyer locked out (account disabled, not yet provisioned, wrong portal) has nowhere to go. | Below 'Forgot password?' add a muted second line: 'Need access? Contact your TERP rep or email sales@terp.[domain].' Do not introduce a signup flow — VIP accounts are provisioned by admins. | No baseline flow is altered; this is additive microcopy. The VIP account-provisioning rule (admin-created accounts only) is explicitly reinforced by 'Contact your TERP rep' rather than offering self-signup. |
| `vip_dashboard-UX-5` | **P2** | **Missing 'Remember me' / session persistence control** — There is no checkbox to keep the session alive between visits. The baseline notes logout clears local/session storage, which implies session state is stored — but the user has no control surface over it. | Add a 'Keep me signed in on this device' checkbox above the Sign In button, defaulted off. Bind it to an extended refresh-token TTL; leave the default session length unchanged for unchecked logins. | The existing logout behavior that clears local/session storage (per baseline Navigation note) continues to work; the checkbox only adjusts token TTL when opted in — it does not change the logout contract. |
| `vip_dashboard-UX-6` | **P2** | **Login card floats in a void with no value reinforcement** — Roughly 80% of the 1440×900 viewport is empty cream background. The single card is visually isolated, and there is no mention of what the portal provides (Live Catalog, AR invoices, Appointments, Documents) — things a returning buyer would recognize. | Convert the layout to a two-column pattern at ≥md breakpoint: left column keeps the existing card; right column shows a short bulleted 'Inside your portal: Live Catalog, Invoices & Payments, Appointments, Documents, Marketplace'. Stack vertically on mobile. | Every item named in the right column maps 1:1 to a baseline `VIPDashboard` module (`LiveCatalog`, `AccountsReceivable`, `AppointmentBooking`, `DocumentDownloads`, `MarketplaceNeeds`/`Supply`) — the page is strengthened, not reshaped, and per-client config still governs which modules actually render post-login. |
| `vip_dashboard-UX-7` | **P3** | **'Forgot password?' link is typographically indistinguishable from body text** — 'Forgot password?' is rendered in the same small gray weight as the 'Sign in to access your account' subtitle, with no underline, no color accent, and no hover affordance visible in the static. | Render 'Forgot password?' in the terracotta accent color (same hue as the Sign In button) with an underline on hover and `focus-visible` ring. Keep size and position. | The link target, handler, and password-reset route are unchanged; this is purely a style token swap. |
| `vip_dashboard-UX-8` | **P1** | **Dashboard-level assessment is blocked: no empty/loading state visible for `/vip-portal/dashboard`** — Requesting `/vip-portal/dashboard` without a VIP session hard-redirects straight to `/vip-portal/login` — there is no intermediate 'Session expired, please sign in again' messaging, and after login there is no indication the user was returning to a specific deep link. | On the login redirect, preserve the originally requested pathname in a `?next=` query param. After successful sign-in, route to `next` if present and if it resolves to a module enabled in the client's per-client config; otherwise fall back to `/vip-portal/dashboard`. On the login screen itself, when `next` is present, show a small banner: 'Sign in to continue.' | The per-client module gating documented in the baseline ('rendered modules depend on the per-client config') is honored by validating `next` against the enabled modules before redirect; the default `/vip-portal/dashboard` landing remains the fallback, so no existing flow regresses. |

**Redesign sketch.** Two-column auth layout at ≥md. Top-left: TERP wordmark + small tagline 'Wholesale portal for approved buyers'. Left column (420px, vertically centered): card titled 'Sign in to TERP' with subheading 'VIP Client Portal'. Fields: Email (autofocus), Password (with trailing show/hide eye icon), 'Keep me signed in on this device' checkbox (unchecked by default), full-width terracotta 'Sign In' button. Below button, two lines: accent-colored 'Forgot password?' and muted 'Need access? Contact your TERP rep.' If `?next=` is present, a subtle info strip above the form reads 'Sign in to continue to [module name].' Right column: heading 'Inside your portal', then a 4–5 row list with icon + label pairs (Live Catalog, Invoices & Payments, Appointments, Documents, Marketplace) sourced from enabled VIP modules — purely decorative on this screen. On mobile, the right column collapses below the card. The Command Palette FAB is not mounted on any `/vip-portal/*` route for non-admin sessions. Post-login, the actual `VIPDashboard` retains its existing module grid (balance, YTD spend, greeting, quick links) — this redesign only fixes the gate in front of it.

#### VIPLogin — `/vip-portal/login` (lightweight)

![VIPLogin](screenshots_all/vip_login.png)

*The login card is functional but generic and undifferentiated — it reads like a Tailwind starter template rather than a VIP wholesale portal. The card is vertically centered with heavy whitespace above, the 'VIP Client Portal' title carries no brand or context (no TERP logo, no hemp/THCA framing), and the password field offers no visibility toggle. 'Forgot password?' is styled as plain muted text under the button with no affordance hinting it's a link. The primary action works and the layout is clean, but the page misses an opportunity to signal legitimacy to external buyers landing here from an email.*

**Keep.** Single-column card with clear label → input → submit flow, no distracting navigation; Primary 'Sign In' button is high-contrast terracotta and spans the full form width, making the CTA unambiguous; Email and Password are the only fields — zero friction to authenticate

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `vip_login-UX-1` | **P2** | **No brand identity — page doesn't look like a legitimate TERP portal** — The card header just says 'VIP Client Portal' in black sans-serif with the subtitle 'Sign in to access your account'. There is no TERP logo, no wordmark, and no visual tie to the ERP brand. An external wholesale buyer arriving from a password-reset or invite email has no visual confirmation they're on the real TERP system. | Add the TERP wordmark/logo above the card (centered, ~40px tall) and rename the card H1 to 'TERP VIP Portal' with the existing subtitle kept underneath. Apply the same warm off-white background treatment but anchor the card with a subtle terracotta top border (4px) matching the Sign In button so the brand color appears twice. | Does not touch `vipPortal.auth.login` or the email/password/submit DOM — purely additive header chrome above the form. |
| `vip_login-UX-2` | **P2** | **Password field has no show/hide toggle** — The Password input renders as a masked field with no eye-icon affordance to reveal typed characters. | Add a right-aligned eye/eye-off icon button inside the password input that toggles `type` between `password` and `text`. Keep default state masked. No change to submit behavior. | `vipPortal.auth.login` still receives the same password string from the same input element; only the input's `type` attribute toggles client-side. |
| `vip_login-UX-3` | **P3** | **'Forgot password?' doesn't read as a link** — The 'Forgot password?' control sits below the Sign In button rendered in muted gray with no underline, no color differentiation, and no icon. It's a button per the DOM, but visually indistinguishable from the 'Sign in to access your account' subtitle above. | Style 'Forgot password?' as an underlined link in the terracotta accent color, and append helper microcopy: 'Forgot password? Contact your account manager.' so the outcome is set before the click. | Preserves the existing Forgot-password button handler that fires the support-contact toast — only the label text and CSS change. |

**Redesign sketch.** Centered card on warm off-white, ~420px wide. Above the card: TERP wordmark logo, 40px tall, centered. Card has a 4px terracotta top border. Inside card: H1 'TERP VIP Portal' (28px, semibold), subtitle 'Sign in to access your wholesale account' (14px, muted). Form: Email label + input (placeholder `you@company.com`), Password label + input with trailing eye-toggle icon. Full-width terracotta 'Sign In' button. Below button, a single line of microcopy: 'Forgot password? Contact your account manager.' where 'Forgot password?' is an underlined terracotta link. Footer line under the card (outside): '© TERP · Authorized wholesale buyers only'.

### Scheduling & Time

#### CalendarPage — `/calendar` (full)

![CalendarPage](screenshots_all/calendar.png)

*The calendar gets the basics right — a clean month grid, consistent tabbed navigation to Invitations/Requests/Time Off, a legible legend, and a clear primary CTA. But it's underpowered for an ERP that touches deliveries, payments, and appointments: event pills show raw order IDs that no human can parse at a glance, the tab row is missing the pending-count badges the baseline promises, the view switcher is four unlabeled icons, the Filters bar is a collapsed empty band eating prime vertical space, and the legend is decoration rather than a filter. The header also buries 'April 2026' between Next and the view switcher instead of making it the anchor of the page. Nothing on this page is broken, but almost every interaction takes one more click than it should.*

**Keep.** Color-coded legend (Intake Appointments / Order Deliveries / Payment Due) gives a domain-specific semantic layer most generic calendars don't have.; Tab structure (Calendar / Invitations / Requests / Time Off) correctly collapses four related inboxes behind one route.; Today (23rd) is clearly marked with a filled blue pill and the whole Thursday column is tinted, so the user never loses orientation.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `calendar-UX-1` | **P1** | **Tab labels are missing the pending-count badges** — The Invitations, Requests, and Time Off tabs render as plain text. The baseline explicitly states 'pending appointment requests and pending team time-off counts surface on tab labels', but no badge is visible next to any tab. | Render a small pill badge (e.g. neutral-100 bg, 11px, tabular) to the right of each tab label when the corresponding count > 0: 'Invitations 3', 'Requests 2', 'Time Off 1'. Hide the badge when zero. Color the Requests badge in the accent orange when count > 0 to match the page CTA so it reads as 'needs attention'. | Sourced from the same `appointmentRequests.*` and `timeOffRequests.*` counts already feeding `PendingInvitationsWidget` / `AppointmentRequestsList` / `TimeOffRequestsList`; we're only surfacing data that routers already return. |
| `calendar-UX-2` | **P1** | **Event pills show truncated order IDs, not customer/amount** — The five delivery events on Apr 13/14 all read 'Order S-1772839382419…' / 'Order S-1772839399561…' etc. The IDs are truncated at the same prefix so no pill is distinguishable from any other, and the pill never says who the delivery is for or how much it's worth. | Render each pill as `{CategoryDot} {Customer short name} · {Order short code}` — e.g. '● Greenwave · S-382419'. Keep the color dot mapped to the legend category. On hover, show a tooltip with full order ID, line total, and scheduled time. Order short code = last 6 digits of the ID to stay unique on screen. | The underlying event object from `calendar.*` already carries `orderId` and (via `calendarFinancials.*`) the linked customer/amount — this is a display-layer change to the month/week/day cell renderer; click-through to the event detail is unchanged. |
| `calendar-UX-3` | **P2** | **View switcher is four unlabeled icons** — The four buttons to the right of 'April 2026' (calendar icon, grid icon, clock icon, list icon) have no visible label and no text beside them indicating the current view is 'Month'. The active state (the calendar icon) is only marked by a thin border. | Convert to a segmented control with text labels: [Month \| Week \| Day \| Agenda], 120px wide, with the active segment filled. Keep icons as optional leading glyphs only if space allows. Move 'April 2026' to the left of the segmented control and render it at 18px semibold so the period label — not the switcher — is the visual anchor. | Drives the same `MonthView` / `WeekView` / `DayView` / `AgendaView` components and the same `calendarViews.*` persistence; only the control's visual treatment changes. |
| `calendar-UX-4` | **P2** | **'Filters' bar is a full-width empty band** — A 40px-tall horizontal container reading only 'Filters' with a funnel icon sits between the page header and the tabs. It is not expanded and shows no active chips, so it consumes vertical space without conveying any state. | Collapse the filter entry to a single 'Filters' button adjacent to 'Create Event'. When filters are active, show them as inline chips next to the button ('Calendar: Sales · Owner: Me'). Open the filter UI in a popover anchored to the button. Recover the vertical band for calendar grid height. | The `CalendarFilters` component and its calendar/owner/category inputs stay intact; only the entry point and layout change — filter state still reads/writes through the same hook. |
| `calendar-UX-5` | **P2** | **Legend is decorative, not interactive** — The three legend items (Intake Appointments, Order Deliveries, Payment Due) are displayed as static swatches with no affordance for clicking. Users cannot temporarily hide one category to de-clutter the grid. | Make each legend item a toggle chip: clicking 'Order Deliveries' dims all blue pills in the grid and its swatch goes outlined. Add a 'Reset' link that appears when any category is hidden. Keyboard: each chip focusable and toggles with Space. | Toggles write to the same category filter state consumed by `CalendarFilters`; this is a shortcut into an existing filter, not a new data path. |
| `calendar-UX-6` | **P2** | **Empty day cells have no visible click affordance for 'Create Event on this date'** — Clicking the '+Create Event' button opens `EventFormDialog` with an unspecified date. There is no inline hover state on empty cells (Apr 2, 3, 7, 8 etc.) to suggest 'click here to add an event on this date'. | On hover of any cell, show a ghost '+ Add' button in the top-right of the cell and change cursor to pointer. Clicking the cell (or the ghost button) opens `EventFormDialog` with `startDate` prefilled to that cell's date. Keep the global Create Event button for keyboard-first users. | Opens the existing `EventFormDialog` with the same `calendar.create` mutation — only the entry point and `startDate` default change; recurrence/participants/reminders fields remain the dialog's responsibility. |
| `calendar-UX-7` | **P2** | **Floating action button in bottom-right duplicates Create Event with no label** — A circular orange button in the bottom-right corner shows an icon only. There is already a full-width orange 'Create Event' button in the header, and the FAB's purpose is not self-evident. | If the FAB is the command/quick-action launcher, replace its icon with a distinct glyph and give it a tooltip ('Quick actions · ⌘K'). If it is Create Event, remove the FAB on this route and rely on the header CTA plus the per-cell affordance from UX-6. Decide and label. | No router behavior changes — this is a label/tooltip/routing decision. If the FAB is wired to `EventFormDialog`, the dialog and its tRPC calls are untouched. |
| `calendar-UX-8` | **P3** | **'Back to Dashboard' button is redundant with breadcrumb and sidebar** — Immediately left of the 'Calendar' H1 sits a 'Back to Dashboard' button. The top bar already shows the Home → Calendar breadcrumb, and the sidebar's Admin → Calendar highlights the current page. | Remove the explicit 'Back to Dashboard' button and rely on the existing breadcrumb. Move the Calendar H1 flush-left and place the Previous/Today/Next cluster, period label, and view switcher as a single right-aligned toolbar. | Navigation remains available through the top-bar breadcrumb (Home link) and the sidebar Dashboard item; no route is removed. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row, flush-left: H1 'Calendar' (24px semibold). Immediately below, a single toolbar row: left side shows '‹ Previous  Today  Next ›' and the active period 'April 2026' at 18px semibold; right side shows a segmented control [Month | Week | Day | Agenda] and a primary 'Create Event' button (with ⌘N hint). Remove the standalone Back to Dashboard button; breadcrumb handles that. Second row: tabs 'Calendar · Invitations 3 · Requests 2 · Time Off 1' with orange badge on any non-zero count. Third row (compact, 32px): left-aligned clickable legend chips for Intake Appointments / Order Deliveries / Payment Due that double as category toggles; right-aligned 'Filters' button with any active filters rendered as inline chips. Grid: seven columns Sun–Sat with slightly dimmed weekend columns, cells 110px tall minimum, today's cell with a blue left border and filled date badge. Event pills render as '● Customer · S-382419' with a hover tooltip containing full order code, amount, time, and owner. Empty cells show a ghost '+ Add' in the top-right on hover and open EventFormDialog with that date prefilled. Drop the ambiguous bottom-right FAB on this route, or relabel it as a scoped Quick Actions launcher with a tooltip.

#### SchedulingPage — `/scheduling` (lightweight)

![SchedulingPage](screenshots_all/scheduling.png)

*The page is a competent calendar shell: three tabs (Calendar/Shifts/Deliveries), Day/Week/Month toggle, Today + pager, a Rooms sidebar with color-coded groups, and context widgets (Today's Appointments, Live Queue) on the right. But the default Week view is a wasteland—eleven empty rows, 18:00+ cut off, and the only visible dimension is time. Resources (rooms) are listed in a sidebar rather than rendered as columns or lanes on the grid, so a user staring at the default view cannot tell which room is free when, which is the entire point of a room-booking tool. The right rail also duplicates 'today' context while the main grid shows a week, creating a mismatch. Book Room is prominent and the empty states are humane, which saves it from feeling broken.*

**Keep.** Clear tri-tab model (Calendar / Shifts / Deliveries) with Day/Week/Month + Today pager exactly where power users expect it.; Rooms sidebar groups by Meeting Rooms vs Loading Docks with colored dots and booking counts—fast mental model for resource type.; Primary 'Book Room' CTA is unambiguous, high-contrast, and anchored top-right next to the date controls.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `scheduling-UX-1` | **P1** | **Week grid shows time only, not rooms — can't see resource availability at a glance** — In Week view the grid columns are Mon 20…Sun 26 and rows are hours, but rooms are only selectable in the left sidebar as a filter. There is no per-room lane, so a dispatcher looking at 'Apr 20–Apr 26, 2026' cannot tell whether Loading Dock 1 vs Dock 2 vs Receiving Bay is booked at 10:00 Wednesday without re-filtering. | When 'All Rooms' is selected, render the Day view as resource columns (one column per room) and Week view as stacked per-room lanes within each day column (or a resource-first toggle next to Day/Week/Month). When a specific room is selected in the sidebar, fall back to the current time-only grid. Keep the sidebar as the filter control. | Preserves `RoomSidebar`, the Day/Week/Month views, and `scheduling.*` booking queries—only the grid's column/lane composition changes based on the sidebar selection. |
| `scheduling-UX-2` | **P2** | **Right rail shows 'Today' context while the calendar is on a week that may not include today** — The right column is 'Today's Appointments' and 'Live Queue' (today-scoped), but the main grid is showing Apr 20–26 with Thu 23 highlighted. If a user pages forward to next week with the chevron, the right rail still says 'Today' and stays empty, creating cognitive dissonance about what date the page is 'about'. | Rename the rail header to reflect the selected date ('Thu Apr 23 · Appointments', 'Thu Apr 23 · Queue') and have it follow the focused day in the grid. When the focused day is today, append a subtle 'Today' pill. Keep the refresh icon and empty-state copy unchanged. | Preserves the `TodaysAppointments` and `LiveQueue` panels and their tRPC data—only the header label and date-scope follow the calendar's current focus instead of hard-coding 'today'. |
| `scheduling-UX-3` | **P2** | **Default week view wastes vertical space on empty hours and hides end-of-day** — The visible grid starts at 8:00 and stops at 17:00 within the viewport, with every cell empty. There's no zero-state prompt inside the grid itself (e.g., 'Click a slot to book'), no 'jump to first booking', and evening hours (18:00–20:00) are below the fold even though loading docks frequently run late. | Auto-scroll to the earliest booking of the focused day (or 8:00 if none), show an inline hint in the first empty cell that reads 'Click any slot to book a room' that dismisses on first click, and add a compact 'Business hours / 24h' density toggle near the Day/Week/Month switcher. | Preserves `RoomBookingModal` triggering from slot clicks and the existing Day/Week/Month views; only scroll position, a dismissible hint, and a density toggle are added. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row unchanged: 'Scheduling' H1 + date range, tab group (Calendar/Shifts/Deliveries), view switcher (Day/Week/Month), pager + Today, Book Room CTA. Body becomes a 3-column layout: (1) narrow Rooms sidebar with 'All Rooms' default, Meeting Rooms group, Loading Docks group, gear for RoomManagementModal; (2) main grid that is resource-aware — when 'All Rooms' is selected, columns are rooms (Day view) or day-blocks subdivided into room lanes (Week view); when a specific room is selected, it collapses to the current time-only grid. Grid auto-scrolls to earliest booking and shows a one-time 'Click any slot to book' hint; business-hours/24h density toggle sits next to Day/Week/Month; (3) right rail retitled to follow the focused day — 'Thu Apr 23 · Appointments' and 'Thu Apr 23 · Queue' with a 'Today' pill when applicable, same empty states. Shifts and Deliveries tabs reuse the same header chrome so mental model stays consistent.

#### TimeClockPage — `/time-clock` (lightweight)

![TimeClockPage](screenshots_all/time_clock.png)

*The page is functional but over-uses vertical space for a user who hasn't clocked in yet. The hero 'Ready to start your day?' banner, the 'Not Clocked In' badge, and the Clock In button all repeat the same information, pushing the weekly timesheet and reports below the fold. The four KPI tiles render '0h 0m' with no contextual framing, which looks like a broken dashboard rather than a fresh week. The navigation pattern is solid (status badge, week stepper, Reports grouping), but the layout reads like a landing page instead of a working time tool.*

**Keep.** Clear status communication: the 'Not Clocked In' badge top-right and the green Clock In CTA give an unambiguous entry point.; Week navigation is well-formed — prev/next chevrons, a 'This Week' reset, and an explicit date range ('Apr 20 - Apr 26, 2026') remove ambiguity.; Reports section exposes the group-by control (Day/Week/Employee) inline rather than hiding it in a modal.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `time_clock-UX-1` | **P1** | **Hero 'Ready to start your day?' card triples up with the status badge and wastes the fold** — The full-width card containing 'Ready to start your day? / Click Clock In to begin tracking your hours / Clock In' occupies roughly 140px at the top of the content area, while the 'Not Clocked In' pill in the header and the green Clock In button inside the card communicate the same state. The KPI row, weekly timesheet, and reports all sit lower than necessary as a result. | Collapse the hero into a single compact status bar spanning the top of the content: left side shows status icon + 'Not Clocked In' / 'Clocked In since 8:14 AM' / 'On Break', right side shows the primary action button (Clock In / Clock Out / Start Break / End Break). Remove the separate 'Not Clocked In' header pill, or keep only one of the two. Height target ~64px. | All four state actions (Clock In, Clock Out, Start Break, End Break from `hourTracking.*`) remain as the primary button, swapping label/color based on live clock status — identical behavior to today's Clock In button, just in a denser container. |
| `time_clock-UX-2` | **P2** | **KPI tiles render four zeroes with no framing or comparison** — 'Regular Hours 0h 0m', 'Overtime Hours 0h 0m' (rendered in amber, implying a warning when the value is literally zero), 'Total Hours 0h 0m', 'Days Worked 0' all display simultaneously with no secondary context such as target hours, prior week, or week-to-date percentage. For a Monday-morning view this looks like a broken or unloaded dashboard. | Keep the four tiles but add a secondary line under each value: Regular shows '/ 40h target', Overtime shows 'vs last week 0h' and stays neutral gray when value is 0 (only turn amber >0), Total shows a tiny progress bar to 40h, Days Worked shows '/ 5 scheduled'. Keep '0h 0m' as the headline number. | Hours aggregation continues to come from `hourTracking.*` weekly totals bound to the 'Apr 20 - Apr 26, 2026' range — only the tile template changes, not the data source or calculation. |
| `time_clock-UX-3` | **P2** | **'Back' button on a top-level nav destination is a dead-end pattern** — A '← Back' control sits directly above the 'Time Clock' H1, but /time-clock is reached from the sidebar (ADMIN group) or command palette, not from a parent detail page. The button either no-ops, goes to an arbitrary referrer, or drops the user wherever they last were, which for a deep-linked or bookmarked landing is disorienting. | Replace the 'Back' button with a breadcrumb ('Admin › Time Clock') that mirrors the sidebar grouping, or remove it on this route and reserve the Back affordance for true detail pages (e.g., an employee timesheet drill-in). Keep the icon+title 'Time Clock' heading block unchanged. | No baseline action is attached to Back in the documented `hourTracking.*` surface; removing it affects chrome only. Sidebar, command palette, and browser back button continue to provide navigation out of the page. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row: breadcrumb 'Admin › Time Clock', H1 'Time Clock' with clock icon, subhead 'Track your work hours and manage timesheets'. Directly below, a single compact status strip: left = colored dot + 'Clocked In since 8:14 AM' or 'Not Clocked In'; right = context-aware primary button (Clock In / Clock Out) plus secondary Break toggle. Next, the 4 KPI tiles unchanged in layout but each gains a small secondary line (target, delta vs last week, or progress bar) and overtime color only activates when >0. Below KPIs, Weekly Timesheet card with the existing ‹ This Week › stepper and 'Apr 20 - Apr 26, 2026' range, empty state reading 'No punches yet this week — your first Clock In will appear here'. Reports card at the bottom retains the Group by (Day/Week/Employee) dropdown with microcopy 'Manager reports include all team members'. Net result: status + primary action visible in ~64px instead of ~200px, KPIs gain meaning, and the weekly timesheet clears the fold on a 1440×900 viewport.

### Productivity & Account

#### NotificationsPage — `/notifications` (full)

![NotificationsPage](screenshots_all/notifications.png)

*The page wires up the three required surfaces (system, alerts, todos) and exposes the core read/filter controls, but the System Notifications tab is doing almost nothing useful with its 118 items. The entire visible list is identical 'New Order Created' rows for Client #203, all timestamped '30 days ago', with no grouping, no priority, no client names, and no click-through to the underlying order. Worse, the word 'System Notifications' appears three times in the first 600px of viewport (tab, card title, list header) while the filter UI duplicates itself as both a dropdown and a chip row. The result is a hub that looks like an inbox but reads like a log file — you cannot triage from it.*

**Keep.** Tabbed structure cleanly separates System / Alerts / Todos per the baseline and keeps the URL stable at /notifications.; Unread indicator dot on the right edge of each row plus a 'Mark all read' affordance gives a clear read-state model.; The 118 count badge on the list header gives honest scale of the backlog without hiding it behind a 9+.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `notifications-UX-1` | **P1** | **Triple-stacked 'System Notifications' heading wastes the entire fold** — Within ~400px of vertical space the user reads 'System Notifications' as a tab label, then as an H2 card title with subtext 'Inbox items, reminders, and updates that need review.', then again as a bell-iconed list header with the 118 badge. The page H1 'Notifications' plus the subtitle 'Review system notifications and alerts in one hub.' is a fourth, nearly-identical line. | Collapse to a single heading pattern: keep the page H1 'Notifications' + one-line subtitle, drop the redundant card-level 'System Notifications' title and its duplicate subtext, and let the active tab itself act as the section label. Move the 118 badge onto the tab (e.g. 'System Notifications · 118') so count stays visible without a second header. | Preserves `InlineNotificationPanel` mount point and the `notifications.*` tRPC count query — only the chrome above the panel changes; the panel still renders the same list and mark-all-read action. |
| `notifications-UX-2` | **P1** | **Filter dropdown and filter chips duplicate each other** — Directly above the list there is a funnel-icon dropdown labelled 'All', and directly below it a chip row 'All / FYI / Needs Action'. Both controls filter the same list by notification category. | Keep the segmented chip row ('All / FYI / Needs Action') as the primary type filter — it is faster to scan and one click to switch. Repurpose the funnel dropdown for a secondary axis that the chips don't cover (date range: Today / 7d / 30d / All), or remove it if redundant. Right-align 'Mark all read' on the same row as the chips to reclaim vertical space. | Both controls hit the same `notifications.list` filter params; consolidating UI into one control per filter axis keeps every existing query combination reachable. |
| `notifications-UX-3` | **P1** | **Every row is '30 days ago' — there is no time hierarchy across 118 items** — All four visible rows show the relative timestamp '30 days ago' with no absolute date, no grouping header (Today / Yesterday / This week / Older), and no sort indicator. With 118 items this pattern continues for dozens of screens. | Group the list under sticky section headers ('Today', 'Yesterday', 'Earlier this week', 'Older') and switch each row's timestamp to a tooltip-on-hover exact datetime plus a short relative form ('2h', '3d'). Right-align timestamps in a fixed column so the eye can scan them. | Uses existing `createdAt` field already returned by `notifications.list`; grouping is a client-side render change inside `InlineNotificationPanel` and does not alter the router contract. |
| `notifications-UX-4` | **P1** | **Notification body is unclickable and hides the real identifiers** — Each row reads 'Order O-1774393232360 created for Client #203 - $129.72' but neither the order code nor the client is a link. The baseline names `normalizeNotificationLink` as the follow-through mechanism, yet nothing in the row signals affordance — no hover underline, no chevron, no 'Open order' action. | Make the entire row a clickable link routed through `normalizeNotificationLink`. Render 'O-1774393232360' as a monospace link-styled token and 'Client #203' as a secondary link to the customer record. Add a subtle right-edge chevron on hover to signal navigability. Keep 'Mark read' as a secondary action surfaced on row hover so click-to-navigate is the default. | `normalizeNotificationLink` already exists in the baseline; this fix just wires the row onClick to it. 'Mark read' button is preserved as a hover action, not removed. |
| `notifications-UX-5` | **P2** | **'Client #203' tells the user nothing** — Every visible notification references the customer as 'Client #203' — an internal numeric ID rather than the company name. | Replace 'Client #203' with the customer display name pulled from the same join the orders page already uses; keep the numeric ID available on hover/tooltip for support debugging. If the payload does not currently include name, add `customer.name` to the `notifications.list` return shape. | Enriches the existing `notifications.*` payload without removing the numeric ID; the underlying notification record and routing behaviour stay intact. |
| `notifications-UX-6` | **P2** | **No bulk selection on a 118-item backlog** — The only bulk action is 'Mark all read' (top right). There is no per-row checkbox and no way to mark a subset read — e.g. all 'FYI' order-created notices from last month. | Add a left-edge checkbox per row plus a 'Select all in view' checkbox in the header row. When ≥1 is selected, reveal a sticky action bar with 'Mark read (N)' and 'Dismiss (N)'. Keep the existing 'Mark all read' button unchanged as the nuclear option. | Adds a new multi-select mutation call against the same `notifications.markRead` router (batched); the single-row 'Mark read' buttons listed in the button inventory remain. |
| `notifications-UX-7` | **P2** | **Monotonous icon + type treatment makes priority invisible** — All four visible rows use the same amber circle-info icon and the same title color, despite the filter system distinguishing 'FYI' from 'Needs Action'. There is no way to scan down the list and find the 'Needs Action' items. | Assign a distinct leading icon + accent color per notification category: FYI (neutral info), Needs Action (amber/red with small badge 'Action'), Success/Completed (green check). Keep row layout identical; only the icon token and an inline category pill change. | Uses the `category`/`type` field already driving the chip filter; no router or data model change. |
| `notifications-UX-8` | **P3** | **Floating action button in bottom-right is unlabelled and unexplained** — A dark circular FAB sits fixed in the bottom-right of the viewport with no tooltip, no label, and no obvious relationship to the notifications list (it appears global across the app). | Add a hover tooltip naming the FAB's actual function (e.g. 'Quick add task' or whatever it invokes), and shift its position slightly so it does not overlap the right-edge unread dots / 'Mark read' column on this page. | Keeps the FAB and its target modal intact; only tooltip and offset change. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: single H1 'Notifications' with one-line subtitle. Directly below, a tab row 'System Notifications · 118 | Alerts · N | Todo Lists · N' — counts live on the tabs, so the redundant card title and bell-icon subheader are gone. Under the active tab: a single toolbar row containing [All | FYI | Needs Action] chip group on the left, a date-range dropdown (Today / 7d / 30d / All) in the middle, and 'Mark all read' right-aligned. Below the toolbar, the list is grouped under sticky date headers ('Today', 'Yesterday', 'Earlier this week', 'Older'). Each row: category icon (color-coded FYI vs Needs Action) + title ('New Order Created') + secondary line with linked order code ('O-1774393232360'), linked customer name ('Acme Hemp Co'), and amount; right side shows a monospace relative timestamp ('3d') with exact datetime on hover, plus unread dot. Entire row is clickable via normalizeNotificationLink; on hover a 'Mark read' ghost button and a right chevron appear. Left-edge checkbox enables multi-select; when ≥1 selected a sticky bottom bar offers 'Mark read (N)' / 'Dismiss (N)'. Empty, loading, error states continue to flow through EmptyState / LoadingState / ErrorState as the baseline specifies.

#### TodoListsPage — `/notifications?tab=todos` (lightweight)

![TodoListsPage](screenshots_all/todos.png)

*The Todo Lists tab is buried inside the Notifications hub, which conceptually conflates system-generated alerts with user-authored tasks. The tab itself is fine — tabs are labeled, the two primary CTAs (New List, New Todo) are discoverable, and the empty/loading state is explicit — but the page wastes the entire viewport on a single loading spinner with no skeleton, and the two primary actions sit above an empty canvas with no hint of what a 'list' vs a 'todo' is. The header micro-copy ('Review system notifications and alerts in one hub') also contradicts the Todo Lists subtitle directly beneath it.*

**Keep.** Two distinct CTAs (New List, New Todo) with clear visual hierarchy — primary filled for Todo, outlined for List — correctly signals the most common action.; Tab structure keeps Notifications/Alerts/Todos co-located, consistent with the Notifications hub pattern.; Explicit 'Loading your lists...' copy instead of a bare spinner tells the user the state is transient.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `todos-UX-1` | **P1** | **Header subtitle contradicts the active tab** — The page header reads 'Notifications — Review system notifications and alerts in one hub.' while the Todo Lists tab is active and the card subtitle says 'Organize your tasks with lists'. The two descriptions fight each other and the user has no cue this tab owns personal task data, not system alerts. | Make the subtitle tab-aware: when Todo Lists is active, swap the subtitle to 'Your personal and shared task lists'. Keep the H1 'Notifications' for hub consistency, but drive the subtitle from the active tab. | Preserves the Notifications hub H1 and the three-tab structure (System Notifications / Alerts / Todo Lists) from the baseline; only the subtitle string is tab-reactive. |
| `todos-UX-2` | **P2** | **Empty canvas below CTAs wastes ~600px and hides the loading state** — While lists load, the entire content area shows a single centered spinner with 'Loading your lists...' and nothing else. On a page whose baseline promises a 'card grid', there is no skeleton indicating shape, column count, or whether any list exists. | Replace the centered spinner with 3–4 skeleton list cards in the same grid the populated state will use, plus a persistent helper row under the CTAs: 'Lists group related todos. Todos can also live outside a list.' On load completion, if the result is truly empty, render an illustrated empty state with a 'Create your first list' primary action that reuses the New List handler. | Preserves the baseline card-grid layout and the create/quick-add/delete behavior; only swaps the loading visual and adds an empty-state variant that calls the same New List action. |
| `todos-UX-3` | **P2** | **New List vs New Todo distinction is unexplained at the point of decision** — Two same-sized buttons sit adjacent with no tooltip, helper text, or icon differentiation beyond the '+' glyph. A first-time user cannot predict whether 'New Todo' requires picking a list first, or whether 'New List' creates an empty container. | Add a one-line caption under each button in the header row: 'New List — group related todos' and 'New Todo — add a task (optionally to a list)'. Keep button labels identical; only add secondary caption text in 12px muted color beneath each. | Preserves the two baseline create affordances (New List and quick-add Todo) and their existing handlers — the change is purely copy/typography in the header. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep H1 'Notifications' and the three tabs. Make the subtitle tab-reactive: on Todo Lists, show 'Your personal and shared task lists'. Header row of the content card: left side 'Todo Lists' title with count pill (e.g., 'Todo Lists · 4'); right side New List (outline) and New Todo (filled), each with a 12px muted caption explaining scope. Body: responsive 3-column grid of list cards (title, todo count, last-updated, overflow menu with delete). While loading, render 4 skeleton cards in the same grid, not a centered spinner. True empty state: centered illustration + 'No lists yet' + primary 'Create your first list' button that invokes the existing New List handler. A persistent 'Unlisted todos' card anchors the grid so quick-added todos without a list are visible, not lost.

#### SearchResultsPage — `/search?q=batch` (lightweight)

![SearchResultsPage](screenshots_all/search_results.png)

*The page returns results and groups them correctly under 'Products (10)', but it squanders vertical space catastrophically. Each result card is ~130px tall to display four short fields (batch code, product line, qty, price), so only 4 hits fit above the fold on a 900px viewport. Worse, the page duplicates the global command palette input ('Search, jump, or run a command…' in the top bar) with a second in-page search box immediately below the H2 — two inputs, same purpose, no clear authority. The 'Product' pill repeated on every row is visual noise since we're already under a 'Products' heading, and there's no section for Quotes/Orders/Customers even though the baseline promises them. No filters, no sort, no result-type tabs.*

**Keep.** Clear result count in the heading ('Products (10)') sets expectations.; Each row shows the identifier, descriptive name, quantity, and price — enough to disambiguate without a click.; Results for "batch" subheading echoes the query, which helps orient after navigation.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `search_results-UX-1` | **P1** | **Result cards waste vertical space; density is ~4 rows per viewport** — Each of the ten BATCH-* cards occupies roughly 130px with generous padding and a full line for 'Qty:' and 'Price:' labels. On a standard laptop viewport only BATCH-00001 through BATCH-00004 are fully visible; scanning ten results requires scrolling, and any multi-section result set (Quotes, Orders, Customers, Products) will push non-product sections entirely below the fold. | Collapse each result to a single-line row: `[type badge] BATCH-20260222-00001  ·  Gorgeous Flower — hawk — OG Kush  ·  Qty 185.45  ·  $761.32`. Target row height ~44px so 12+ results fit above the fold. Keep the card border only around the section, not per row. | Preserves `search.global` row-click navigation — the entire row remains the click target to its surface, and all four fields continue to render; only layout density changes. |
| `search_results-UX-2` | **P1** | **Duplicate search inputs create ambiguity about authority** — The top bar shows the command palette input ('Search, jump, or run a command…' with CTRL-K chip), and the page body shows a second input prefilled with 'batch' plus a maroon 'Search' button. Both target the same `search.global` query param, but it's unclear which is canonical or whether editing one syncs the other. | Keep the in-page input (it's the one tied to the URL query param and visible on this route) and downgrade the top-bar palette trigger on this route to a button-style 'Jump to…' so the two don't read as twins. Alternatively, remove the redundant 'Search' submit button — input onChange already updates the query param per bug-042. | Preserves the `search.global` router binding and the bug-042 query-param sync — we're only resolving which control owns the URL state on this route, not changing the behavior. |
| `search_results-UX-3` | **P2** | **Only Products section renders; no Quotes/Orders/Customers headings or empty-state hints** — The baseline specifies sections for Quotes, Orders, Customers, and Products & Batches with 'empty-state operational guidance when none match.' The rendered page shows only 'Products (10)' with no indication that other result types exist or that they returned zero. The user cannot tell whether 'batch' simply has no Quote/Order/Customer matches or whether those sections aren't implemented. | Always render all four section headers (Quotes, Orders, Customers, Products & Batches) with counts, and when a section is empty show a single muted line: 'No quotes match "batch".' Add result-type filter chips above the list ('All · Quotes · Orders · Customers · Products') so users can narrow without re-querying. | Preserves the `search.global` contract which already returns all four result types; we're rendering the empty sections the router already supplies rather than hiding them. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: 'Search Results' H1 with muted 'Results for "batch" · 10 matches' caption. Below it, one input (no duplicate submit button) with type-filter chips directly underneath: [All 10] [Quotes 0] [Orders 0] [Customers 0] [Products 10]. Results area is a single bordered panel with sticky section headers ('Products & Batches · 10') and dense 44px-tall rows: left-aligned type badge, monospace batch code, em-dashed product descriptor, right-aligned Qty and Price columns in a fixed grid. Empty sections collapse to a one-line muted row ('No orders match "batch".'). Remove the per-row 'Product' pill (redundant under the section header). Keep top-bar CTRL-K palette but restyle as a compact 'Jump to…' button on this route so it reads as navigation, not search input.

#### Help — `/help` (lightweight)

![Help](screenshots_all/help.png)

*The Help Center lands with a clean title, a prominent search input, and a 2-column grid of section cards that map directly to the baseline's six help areas — this is a solid, scannable structure. However, the experience wastes its most valuable real estate: every section card is collapsed-by-default with a chevron, yet the topics are already visible inside the card, so the chevron reads as broken or redundant. The section cards are also visually heavy (large icons, lots of padding) while the topics themselves are tiny bulleted text with no affordance that they are navigable — users won't know whether clicking 'Customizing data cards' takes them to long-form training copy or does nothing. Finally, the search input has no placeholder guidance about what it searches (titles only? body copy?) and no results state is hinted at.*

**Keep.** Clear H1 'TERP Help Center' with a plain-English subtitle sets expectations immediately; Six baseline sections are all surfaced above the fold in a predictable 2-column grid with recognizable icons; Top-level search field is the first interactive element, matching user intent for a help page

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `help-UX-1` | **P1** | **Topic bullets don't look clickable** — Inside each section card (e.g., 'Customizing data cards', 'Creating and managing batches', 'Fulfillment workflow…'), topics render as small grey bulleted text with no link color, underline, hover chevron, or cursor affordance. They look like marketing copy, not navigation into the long-form training content the baseline promises. | Style topic rows as list-group links: left-aligned, medium weight, primary text color, subtle right-chevron that appears on hover, full-row hover background, and cursor:pointer across the whole row. Drop the decorative bullet. | Preserves the Help page's six-section topic list structure defined in FUNCTIONAL_BASELINE §Help; only visual affordance changes, no topic is removed or rerouted. |
| `help-UX-2` | **P2** | **Chevron on each card is ambiguous — expanded content is already visible** — Each section card header (Dashboard, Inventory Management, Orders & Fulfillment, Client Management) shows a down-chevron suggesting it expands, yet the topics list is already rendered inside the card. Clicking the chevron either does nothing visible or collapses content the user just scanned. | Either (a) remove the chevron and keep cards always-expanded since there are only six sections, or (b) make the chevron the single source of truth: start cards collapsed showing description only, expand to reveal topics, and animate smoothly. Pick one model and apply consistently. | Preserves all six baseline sections and their description + topics list; only the disclosure pattern is disambiguated. |
| `help-UX-3` | **P2** | **Search input lacks scope hint and keyboard shortcut parity** — The in-page 'Search for help topics…' field gives no indication of what it searches (topic titles? body text?) and offers no keyboard shortcut, while the global 'CTRL K' palette sits 200px above it. Users land on /help via the `?` shortcut (per runtime supplement) but have no fast way to focus the help search itself. | Autofocus the help search on page load, sharpen the placeholder to 'Search topics and training articles…', and show a small '/' shortcut badge inside the input. Add a visible empty-results state with 'No topics match — try the Command Palette (Ctrl+K)' fallback. | Preserves the Help page's local search (no tRPC, client-side per baseline) and the global Command Palette shortcut; only adds focus + copy. |

**Redesign sketch.** Heading stays: 'TERP Help Center' with subtitle and a full-width search bar (autofocused, placeholder 'Search topics and training articles…', '/' shortcut badge). Below, replace the heavy collapsible cards with a 2-column grid of six always-expanded section panels. Each panel: small colored icon + section name (H3) on one line, one-line description in muted text, then a clean list-group of topics where each row is a full-width clickable link (topic title left, right-chevron on hover, row hover background). Panels are equal-height with consistent padding so Dashboard/Inventory/Orders/Clients/Analytics/Accounting align in a clean 3-row, 2-column layout. Remove redundant card-level chevrons. When a search query is active, collapse the grid into a single flat result list grouped by section with matched snippets highlighted; show 'No topics match — try Ctrl+K' when empty.

#### AccountPage — `/account` (lightweight)

![AccountPage](screenshots_all/account.png)

*The page cleanly separates Profile, Security, and Preferences, and the callout directing users to System Settings is a smart disambiguation move. However, the hierarchy is noisy: 'Profile Information' appears twice back-to-back (once as an H2 section header, once as a card header with identical icon and copy), the Save Changes button reads as disabled (muted peach) when the form is actually idle/valid, and the page icon avatar is a generic placeholder rather than reflecting the logged-in user. The 'Personal' badges next to each H2 are decorative noise given every section on this page is personal by definition.*

**Keep.** Prominent contrast banner routing org-level questions to /settings prevents the classic 'wrong settings page' dead-end.; Clear vertical stacking of Profile → Security → Preferences → Notifications matches user mental model of account self-service.; Password fields expose a visibility toggle, which is table stakes but correctly implemented.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `account-UX-1` | **P2** | **Duplicated 'Profile Information' header wastes vertical space** — The string 'Profile Information' appears twice within 60px of itself — once as the H2 section title with a user icon and 'Personal' tag, then again immediately inside the card as a second header with the same icon plus the subtitle 'Update your personal information'. Same pattern likely repeats for Security ('Change Password' card inside 'Security' H2). | Keep the outer H2 ('Profile Information' with icon and 'Personal' tag) as the section anchor and strip the redundant inner card header, promoting the subtitle 'Update your personal information' to sit directly under the H2. Apply the same collapse to Security → Change Password. | Preserves the Profile and Security sections defined in the AccountPage baseline — only removes a duplicate visual label; no fields, actions, or routes change. |
| `account-UX-2` | **P2** | **Save Changes button reads as disabled when form is valid** — The 'Save Changes' button under the Profile form renders in a muted peach/tan with low-contrast white text, visually identical to a disabled state, even though Name and Email are populated with valid values. | Reserve the muted peach exclusively for the disabled/pristine state (no dirty fields) and use the app's saturated primary brand color for the active/dirty state. Additionally, disable the button by default until a field actually changes, then enable with full-contrast styling. | Preserves the Profile save action wired to the existing profile-update mutation — only the visual token and dirty-check gating change, not the submit behavior. |
| `account-UX-3` | **P3** | **'Personal' tag next to every H2 is noise** — Each section H2 (Profile Information, Security, and presumably Preferences/Notifications below the fold) carries a small 'Personal' pill. Every section on /account is personal by definition; the contrast is already established by the top banner pointing to /settings for org-level settings. | Drop the 'Personal' pill from all section headers on this page. If scoping context is ever needed (e.g., future shared preferences), reintroduce the badge only on the non-personal row. | Preserves all AccountPage sections listed in the baseline (Profile, Security, Preferences, Notification Preferences); the pill is purely decorative and has no behavior to lose. |

**Redesign sketch.** Single-column settings page, max-width ~760px, left-aligned with a sticky mini TOC on the right at ≥1280px (Profile · Security · Preferences · Notifications · Command Palette) that deep-links to each section. Top: H1 'My Account' with subtitle 'Manage your personal settings and preferences', and the existing contrast banner linking to /settings kept as-is. Each section uses one H2 with a leading icon — no duplicate inner card header, no 'Personal' pill. Under each H2, a short helper sentence (e.g., 'Update your personal information'), then the form fields in a bordered card. Primary buttons ('Save Changes', 'Change Password', 'Save Preferences') use the saturated brand color only when the form is dirty; otherwise render disabled in muted peach. Avatar in the page header reflects the user's initials ('QA') instead of a generic silhouette.

### Admin & System

#### Settings — `/settings` (full)

![Settings](screenshots_all/settings.png)

*The Settings page has the right bones — a clean four-group top nav (Access Control, Master Data, Organization, Developer) and sub-tabs under each — but the Access Control landing wastes the entire first viewport on a Create-User form while hiding the thing admins actually come here for: the existing user list. Hierarchy is muddled (the page title, top tab label, and H2 below all read 'Access Control'; tabs and sub-tabs look visually similar), and core admin moves like resetting a password or granting a role force the user to hand-type a username rather than pick from a list. Master Data and Organization tabs are unvisited on this capture but the pattern would repeat. The shell (breadcrumb, Back-to-Dashboard link, deep-link `?tab=` support) is solid and must be preserved.*

**Keep.** Four-group segmented nav (Access Control / Master Data / Organization / Developer) is the right mental model and matches `SETTINGS_GROUPS`; deep-link via `?tab=` means links can be shared.; Sub-tab row under each group (Users / User Roles / Roles / Permissions) keeps the admin surface shallow instead of sprawling into a tree.; The workspace header pattern (H1 + one-line subtitle) is consistent with the rest of TERP, so users are not learning a new chrome here.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `settings-UX-1` | **P1** | **Users tab leads with a creation form, not the user list** — On `/settings?tab=access-control` → Users, the entire first viewport is the 'Create New User' card. The 'All Roles / 10 per page / Roles' controls suggested by the runtime DOM (which belong to the existing users table) are pushed below the fold, along with 'Reset Password'. An admin landing here to audit, disable, or role-assign an existing user has to scroll past a create form every single time. | Flip the order: render the existing users table (search, 'All Roles' filter, paginator, per-row actions) as the primary surface at the top of the Users sub-tab, with a single 'New User' button in the section header that opens the Create-New-User form in a right-side drawer or inline expansion. Reset Password becomes a per-row action in the table, not a separate card. | The `UserManagement` component's Create User inputs (Username min-3, Password min-8, Display Name optional) and the Reset Password form are both retained verbatim — only their entry point and position change; no tRPC call signatures shift. |
| `settings-UX-2` | **P1** | **Reset Password requires hand-typing the username** — The 'Reset Password' card under Users exposes a free-text 'Username' input with placeholder `username` instead of a user picker. There is a separate users list elsewhere on the page (the 'All Roles / 10 / page' controls confirm it), yet the reset flow forces the admin to re-type an identifier they just read from that list. | Replace the free-text username input with an autocomplete combobox bound to the same user list shown above (search by username or display name, show avatar + role chips in the result row). Keep the existing 'New Password' input and validation. When the workflow moves into the row-action drawer from UX-1, the user is already resolved. | The reset mutation contract (username + new password) is unchanged; the combobox resolves to the same `username` string the current textbox submits, so the `UserManagement` reset handler keeps its current payload shape. |
| `settings-UX-3` | **P2** | **Triple-stacked 'Access Control' label creates navigational noise** — The word 'Access Control' appears three times in the first 350 px: as the active top tab chip, as the H2 section heading inside the card, and implicitly again in the sub-tab row context. The H2 subtitle 'Manage users, role assignments, and system permissions' also paraphrases the page subtitle 'Manage system configurations and master data'. | Drop the duplicate H2 'Access Control' heading and its paraphrased description. Keep the top tab as the single source of truth for the active group, and let the sub-tab row (Users / User Roles / Roles / Permissions) be the next visible element, with each sub-tab rendering its own scoped H2 ('Users', 'Roles', etc.) and one-line description only when that description adds information not already on the tab label. | The `SETTINGS_GROUPS`/`SETTINGS_SECTIONS` routing and `?tab=` deep-linking are untouched — this is a purely layout/copy change inside the existing component tree. |
| `settings-UX-4` | **P2** | **Top-level group tabs and sub-tabs use nearly identical styling** — The top tabs (Access Control / Master Data / Organization / Developer) and the sub-tabs (Users / User Roles / Roles / Permissions) both render as light pill/segmented chips in the same tonal family, separated only by ~70 px and the 'Access Control' H2 in between. There is no visual weight distinction between 'switch settings group' and 'switch subsection within a group'. | Style the top row as full-width segmented control with a filled active state (the current chromed look), and restyle the sub-tab row as underline tabs (text-only, 1 px underline on active) tucked tight under a thin divider. This gives a clear 'primary / secondary' gradient that matches the rest of TERP's workspace-header pattern (title → blue band → tab chips). | Both tab rows still fire the same route/state transitions and respect `SETTINGS_SECTIONS` gating; only CSS classes and the vertical spacing between the two rows change. |
| `settings-UX-5` | **P2** | **Create New User collects no role at creation time** — The Create New User card has exactly three fields: Username, Password, Display Name. There is no role picker. To actually give the account any capability, the admin must create the user, switch to the Permissions sub-tab, find the user again, and assign a role — a three-step dance with no in-form guidance that the created user is currently access-less. | Add an 'Initial Role' multi-select (populated from `RoleManagement`) to the Create New User form, defaulting to an org-wide 'Default' role if configured. Below the Create User button, show a one-line confirmation: 'User will be created with role: Sales'. Keep the Permissions tab for later re-assignment exactly as-is. | The existing Create User tRPC call keeps its current fields; the new `initialRoles` argument is optional and — if empty — reproduces today's 'create then assign' flow, so the `PermissionAssignment` surface keeps its authority over role changes. |
| `settings-UX-6` | **P2** | **Password field has no confirm, strength, or show/hide** — The Password input shows placeholder `password`, a 'Minimum 8 characters' helper, and nothing else: no confirm-password field, no strength meter, no show/hide eye icon. The same applies to the Reset Password card's 'New Password' input. | Add a 'Confirm Password' input next to 'Password', a show/hide toggle (eye icon) on both password inputs, and a lightweight strength hint ('Weak / Medium / Strong') driven locally. Validation block the Create/Reset button until Password === Confirm and length ≥ 8. | The Create User and Reset Password mutations keep their single-password contract; confirm and strength are client-side only, so `UserManagement`'s server handlers don't change. |
| `settings-UX-7` | **P3** | **'Back to Dashboard' link duplicates the breadcrumb home icon** — Directly above the 'System Settings' H1 sits a '← Back to Dashboard' link. The topbar already shows the Home icon + 'Settings' breadcrumb two rows up, which is the canonical back-affordance on every other TERP page. | Remove the 'Back to Dashboard' link from the page body and rely on the existing topbar breadcrumb `Home ▸ Settings`. If the breadcrumb's home icon doesn't currently route to the Dashboard, fix the href there so a single affordance does both jobs. | No baseline component is removed — the route `/` (dashboard) is still reachable via the top breadcrumb, which is the documented shell chrome across every protected page. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep the existing workspace header (H1 'System Settings', subtitle 'Manage system configurations and master data') and the topbar breadcrumb as the only back-affordance. Directly below the subtitle, render a single full-width **segmented control** with the four group tabs (Access Control · Master Data · Organization · Developer), filled active state, matching TERP's blue workspace band. Drop the duplicate H2 and its paraphrased description. Under the segmented control, a thin divider, then an **underline-tab** row for the group's sub-sections (Users · User Roles · Roles · Permissions) — clearly secondary. For the Users sub-tab specifically: (1) section header 'Users' with a right-aligned primary button **+ New User** and a search box + 'All Roles' filter + paginator; (2) the existing users table as the primary surface — columns: Username, Display Name, Roles (chips), Last Login, Status, with a row-level kebab exposing 'Reset password…', 'Change roles…', 'Disable'. (3) Clicking **+ New User** opens a right drawer with Username, Display Name, Password + Confirm Password (both with show/hide), a strength hint, and an **Initial Role** multi-select; footer action 'Create user'. (4) 'Reset password…' from the kebab opens the same drawer pre-filled with the user, showing only New Password + Confirm. Master Data, Organization, and Developer tabs follow the same pattern: search + list first, creation in a drawer, one H2 per sub-tab. `?tab=` deep links and unsaved-changes guard are preserved.
