#### Settings.locations — `/settings?tab=locations` (lightweight)

![Settings.locations](screenshots_all/settings_locations.png)

*The Locations tab does its job at a basic CRUD level — you can add a hierarchical location and see existing ones — but the hierarchy is buried under a field matrix that reads like a flat form. Five equally-weighted inputs (Site, Zone, Rack, Shelf, Bin) suggest all fields matter equally, when in fact only Site is required and the rest are nested children. The existing locations list is a tiny card with cryptic `A > 1 > 1 > 1` path strings and no grouping by Site, which will collapse the moment a warehouse has more than a handful of bins. There is no search, no bulk import, and no way to add a child to an existing parent — every new bin forces you to retype the whole Site.*

**Keep.** Clear site/zone/rack/shelf/bin mental model is surfaced as column labels with `(optional)` hints on non-required fields.; Master Data sub-tabs (Product Metadata, Locations, Categories, Grades, Tags) keep reference-data tools co-located and predictable.; Edit and delete affordances on each existing location row are immediate and discoverable.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `settings_locations-UX-1` | **P1** | **Flat 5-column form hides the hierarchy and forces re-entry of parents** — The Add New Location card shows Site, Zone, Rack, Shelf, Bin as five equal-weight inputs side by side. Nothing in the UI signals that these are nested, and there is no way to pick an existing Site/Zone and append a child — every new bin requires retyping `WH1 > A > R1 > S1` from scratch. | Replace the flat row with a cascading picker: Site becomes a combobox of existing sites plus a 'Create new site' option; Zone/Rack/Shelf/Bin become dependent comboboxes that auto-fill from the selected parent. Add an 'Add child to…' action on each row in Existing Locations that pre-fills the parent chain. | Preserves the Locations master-data entity (`SETTINGS_SECTIONS` Master Data › Locations) — all five fields remain writable, the `Add Location` submit still posts the full Site/Zone/Rack/Shelf/Bin tuple, and manual free-text creation stays available via the 'Create new' option. |
| `settings_locations-UX-2` | **P1** | **Existing Locations list is unreadable at scale — no grouping, search, or decoded path** — The Existing Locations section shows a single card 'Main Warehouse — A > 1 > 1 > 1' with no Site grouping, no search input, no pagination, no column headers naming what A/1/1/1 are, and no counter of total locations. With 50+ bins this becomes a scroll wall of indistinguishable breadcrumb strings. | Group Existing Locations by Site with collapsible sections and a count ('Main Warehouse · 24 locations'). Add a search input above the list ('Search by site, zone, rack…'). Change each row to show labeled segments ('Zone A · Rack 1 · Shelf 1 · Bin 1') instead of a raw `>` string, and keep the pencil/trash icons on the right. | Preserves the Locations listing/edit/delete behavior — the same records render, and the existing pencil (edit) and trash (delete) controls remain on every row; only grouping, labeling, and search are layered on top. |

**Redesign sketch.** Keep the 'System Settings' H1 and Master Data › Locations tab chain. Replace the 'Add New Location' card with a compact two-line composer: line 1 is a Site combobox (existing sites + 'Create new'); line 2 reveals Zone → Rack → Shelf → Bin as dependent comboboxes that cascade from the selection, ending in a primary 'Add Location' button. Below, 'Existing Locations' becomes a searchable, grouped tree: a search box, then collapsible Site headers ('Main Warehouse · 24 bins') each containing rows labeled 'Zone A · Rack 1 · Shelf 1 · Bin 1' with a hover 'Add child' action plus the existing edit/delete icons. Footer hint: 'Tip: only Site is required — leave deeper levels blank for site-level storage.'

---

#### Settings.roles — `/settings?tab=roles` (lightweight)

![Settings.roles](screenshots_all/settings_roles.png)

*The Roles tab is functional but visually undifferentiated from the sibling sub-tabs (Users, User Roles, Permissions) and wastes enormous vertical space before showing the actual role table. 'Role Management' is a full-width card whose only job is to hold a single 'Create New Role' button — that's a header-action, not a section. The 'All Roles' table is what matters here, yet it's pushed below the fold; a user arriving on the tab sees two nearly identical shield-icon cards with generic descriptions before any data. The table itself has clear columns (Role Name, Description, Type, Permissions, Users) but the permission/user counts are rendered as chip-like boxes that read as interactive when they may not be, and row actions are clipped at the right edge.*

**Keep.** Clear two-level tab hierarchy (Access Control → Users / User Roles / Roles / Permissions) keeps related access surfaces together.; Role table exposes Type (System) and both Permissions and Users counts, which is the right information density for an admin landing.; Descriptions on system roles (Super Admin, Owner/Executive, Operations Manager) are written in plain language and explain the safety posture.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `settings_roles-UX-1` | **P1** | **Role Management card is a 180px-tall wrapper around one button** — The 'Role Management — Create and manage roles to organize permissions' card consumes the entire initial viewport width and ~180px of height purely to host the 'Create New Role' button. The 'All Roles' table, which is the actual content of this tab, is pushed below the fold. | Collapse the 'Role Management' card into a header-action row: keep the 'Create New Role' button but anchor it to the right of the 'All Roles' heading (or to the right of the sub-tab strip). Let the 'All Roles' table render in the first viewport. Move the 'Create and manage roles to organize permissions' copy into the Access Control section subtitle or drop it — the page H1 and tab label already convey this. | The `Create New Role` CTA in the `RoleManagement` component is preserved verbatim; only its container chrome is removed. No router call or create flow changes. |
| `settings_roles-UX-2` | **P2** | **Permission and user counts look like editable inputs** — In the All Roles table, the Permissions column renders values like `331`, `44`, `102` inside thin bordered boxes, and the Users column renders `3`, `1`, `2` inside similar boxes with a user icon. They visually match text-input fields more than read-only counts or links. | Render both counts as plain numeric cells with a trailing label ('331 permissions', '3 users') and make them actual links that deep-link to `?tab=permissions&role=<id>` and `?tab=users&role=<id>`. Remove the input-style border; use a subtle underline on hover to signal navigability. | The `UserRoleManagement` / `PermissionAssignment` sub-sections remain unchanged; this fix only restyles the count cells in `RoleManagement` and adds a querystring filter that those components can already consume via the existing `?tab=` deep-link pattern. |
| `settings_roles-UX-3` | **P2** | **Row actions clipped at right edge of the table** — On each role row, a partial control is visible at the right edge (a cut-off circle icon next to the Users count on Super Admin, Owner/Executive, and Operations Manager rows). The actions column is being cropped by the card's right padding. | Pin an explicit 'Actions' column at the right with a fixed width (~96px), show full-size icon buttons (View · Edit · Duplicate) with tooltips, and disable Edit/Delete on rows where `Type = System` with a tooltip 'System roles cannot be modified'. Ensure the table container has `overflow-x: auto` as a fallback instead of clipping. | Preserves the existing row-action handlers in `RoleManagement` and the `Type = System` business rule (Super Admin / Owner/Executive / Operations Manager remain protected); only the column layout and disabled-state affordance change. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header stays: 'System Settings' / 'Manage system configurations and master data' / top tabs (Access Control · Master Data · Organization · Developer). Inside Access Control, sub-tabs Users · User Roles · Roles · Permissions remain. The Roles panel collapses to a single card: a row with 'All Roles' on the left, count ('5 roles · 3 system, 2 custom') underneath, and 'Create New Role' button pinned right. Directly below: the roles table with columns Role | Description | Type (chip) | Permissions (linked count) | Users (linked count) | Actions (pinned right, icon buttons, disabled on System). Kill the separate 'Role Management' wrapper card entirely. First viewport now shows all ~5 roles without scrolling.

#### Settings.users — `/settings?tab=users` (lightweight)

![Settings.users](screenshots_all/settings_users.png)

*This is a bare-bones admin form page masquerading as a user management surface. The tab hierarchy works (Access Control → Users sub-tab), but the primary affordance a Settings.users page needs — the list of existing users — is pushed below the fold behind two stacked creation/reset forms. An admin landing here to audit who has access, change a role, or deactivate an offboarded employee has to scroll past 'Create New User' and 'Reset Password' cards to even see the roster. The forms themselves are serviceable (clear labels, helper text on length, required markers) but the page reads like a form-first admin tool from 2014 rather than a list-first management surface.*

**Keep.** Two-level tab structure (top tabs for Settings sections, inner tabs for Users/User Roles/Roles/Permissions) correctly mirrors the SETTINGS_GROUPS / Access Control taxonomy.; Create User form has inline constraint hints ('Minimum 3 characters', 'Minimum 8 characters') and required-field asterisks, so validation expectations are visible before submit.; Breadcrumb 'Back to Dashboard' plus persistent top-tab row gives a clear escape hatch from deep settings navigation.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `settings_users-UX-1` | **P1** | **User roster is buried below two forms** — The initial viewport shows 'Create New User' and the top of 'Reset Password', with the actual user list (implied by the 'All Roles' filter and '10 / page' paginator in the DOM) rendered further down the page. | Flip the page order: render the user table (with the 'All Roles' filter and '10 / page' paginator) immediately below the inner tabs, and collapse 'Create New User' into a top-right 'New User' button that opens a drawer/modal containing the existing fields. Move 'Reset Password' into a per-row row-action (kebab menu → Reset password) that pre-fills the username. | `UserManagement` component still owns Create User and Reset Password; fields, validation (min 3 / min 8 chars), and the Create User tRPC call are untouched — only their entry points move from always-visible cards to a button-triggered drawer and a row action. |
| `settings_users-UX-2` | **P2** | **Inner tab group is visually indistinguishable from the outer one** — The four outer tabs (Access Control, Master Data, Organization, Developer) and the four inner Access Control tabs (Users, User Roles, Roles, Permissions) use similar chip styling and sit within ~150px of each other, with no grouping label on the inner row. | Demote the inner row to a segmented control pinned to the left of the 'Access Control' card header, and tighten its type (smaller, medium weight). Keep the outer tabs as the primary navigation band. Add a thin divider and a 'Section: Access Control' eyebrow above the inner control so the nesting is explicit. | Both tab groups still drive the same `SETTINGS_SECTIONS` routing with `?tab=users`; only visual weight and placement change, and all four inner sub-sections (`UserManagement`, `UserRoleManagement`, `RoleManagement`, `PermissionAssignment`) remain reachable. |
| `settings_users-UX-3` | **P2** | **Create User form wastes a full row on three short fields** — Username, Password, and Display Name each take ~1/3 of the content width (~400px each) despite being short inputs, pushing the Create User button and everything below further down. | Constrain the form to a max-width of ~640px, stack the three fields in two rows (Username + Display Name on row 1, Password on row 2 with a show/hide toggle), and right-align the Create User button. When moved into a drawer per UX-1, this layout fits natively. | Same three fields bound to the same Create User mutation; helper text ('Minimum 3 characters', 'Minimum 8 characters') and required markers are kept verbatim. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header unchanged: 'System Settings' H1 + subtitle + outer tab row (Access Control / Master Data / Organization / Developer). Inside the Access Control card, replace the current chip row with a left-aligned segmented control labeled with an 'Access Control' eyebrow: [Users · User Roles · Roles · Permissions]. Body becomes list-first: a toolbar row with a search input, the existing 'All Roles' filter, a '10 / page' paginator on the right, and a primary 'New User' button that opens a right-side drawer containing the current Create New User form (Username, Display Name, Password with show/hide, min-char hints, Create User CTA). Below the toolbar, a user table with columns Username · Display Name · Role · Last Login · Status · actions (kebab → Reset password [pre-filled], Edit roles, Deactivate). Reset Password is no longer a separate top-level card; it lives in the row kebab and reuses the same form fields inside a small modal. Microcopy: empty state 'No users match these filters — clear filters or create a new user.' Drawer heading 'Create user'; reset modal heading 'Reset password for {username}'.

#### SystemMetricsPage — `/admin/metrics` (lightweight)

![SystemMetricsPage](screenshots_all/system_metrics.png)

*The page delivers the core monitoring data in scannable cards, but it reads like a raw dump of `monitoring.*` fields rather than a health dashboard. There is no overall status verdict, no thresholds/color-coding, no timestamp for when the metrics were captured, and no indication that the data refreshes. The baseline promises event-loop lag but it is not surfaced anywhere visible. Disk Used is already at 70% yet rendered in the same neutral black as Uptime, so the one number that actually matters gets no visual weight.*

**Keep.** Clear card grid with label + one-line description + big value is easy to scan.; Back to Dashboard affordance at the top gives an obvious exit from this admin detour.; Grouping CPU Usage into its own titled panel separates cumulative counters from point-in-time gauges.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `system_metrics-UX-1` | **P1** | **No overall health verdict or threshold coloring** — Every metric card uses the same neutral typography. Disk Used at 65.0 GB (70%) looks identical in weight/color to Uptime at 1h 43m 19s, and there is no summary banner telling the admin whether the instance is Healthy/Degraded/Critical. | Add a status pill next to the H1 ('Healthy' green / 'Degraded' amber / 'Critical' red) derived from the same `monitoring.*` payload, and color the value text on Disk Used, Heap Used/Total ratio, and event-loop lag amber ≥70% and red ≥90%. Keep the numeric value and label unchanged. | Consumes the existing `monitoring.*` tRPC response; only the presentation layer adds derived status — no router or field is removed. |
| `system_metrics-UX-2` | **P2** | **No 'as of' timestamp or refresh control** — The subtitle says 'Runtime health and resource usage for the current TERP instance' but nothing tells the user when these numbers were sampled or how to refresh. Values like Uptime '1h 43m 19s' are stale the moment the page renders. | Add a small right-aligned 'Updated Xs ago · Refresh' control under the H1, wired to re-invoke `monitoring.*` on click and auto-poll every 15s. Show the timestamp in the user's locale on hover. | Uses the existing `monitoring.*` query; auto-poll is a client-side refetch, does not alter the router contract. |
| `system_metrics-UX-3` | **P2** | **Event-loop lag promised by baseline is not visible** — Baseline lists 'event loop lag' as a first-class purpose of this page, but the rendered cards only show Uptime, Heap Used/Total, RSS, Disk Used/Free/Status, and CPU User/System. There is no event-loop lag card on screen. | Add an 'Event Loop Lag' card to the top row (next to Heap/RSS) showing current ms with the same label/description/value pattern, sourced from the existing `monitoring.*` lag field. | Surfaces an existing `monitoring.*` field already guaranteed by the baseline; adds a card rather than touching data or routing. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row: H1 'System Metrics' with a status pill ('Healthy' / 'Degraded' / 'Critical') inline, subtitle unchanged, and a right-aligned 'Updated 4s ago · Refresh' control. Below it, a 4-column card grid in three logical bands: (1) Process — Uptime, Event Loop Lag, Heap Used (of Total, with % bar), RSS; (2) Disk — Disk Used (with % bar), Disk Free, Disk Status, of Total; (3) CPU Usage panel retained as today with User/System counters side by side plus a tiny 'cumulative since boot' footnote. Threshold coloring applied to the value text on Heap%, Disk%, and Lag. Back to Dashboard link stays at the top-left. No functionality removed; every card binds to an existing `monitoring.*` field.

#### FeatureFlagsPage — `/settings?tab=feature-flags` (lightweight)

![FeatureFlagsPage](screenshots_all/feature_flags.png)

*The page buries a critical power-user surface (57 feature flags controlling module access) under three stacked levels of tabs — Settings tabs → Developer sub-tabs → Controls/Change Log — with no search, filter, or category jump. The table design is reasonable (clear Active / On by Default / Requires / Access columns), but with 57 controls grouped into lowercase category headers ('accounting', 'beta'…) and no way to find a flag except scrolling, a super-admin toggling a single module has to navigate a deep path and then hunt. 'Initialize Defaults' sits next to 'Refresh' and 'Add Control' with no warning copy, which is dangerous given it can mass-reset system-wide behavior.*

**Keep.** Row layout cleanly separates 'Active' (system state) from 'On by Default' (rollout policy) with machine ID (`module-accounting`) and plain-language description visible together.; Controls count badge 'Controls (57)' gives immediate scale awareness, and Change Log is a peer tab rather than buried in a menu.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `feature_flags-UX-1` | **P1** | **No search or category filter across 57 flags** — The 'Controls (57)' view renders every flag inline grouped under lowercase category cards ('accounting', 'beta', …) with no search box, category filter chips, or sticky jump nav. To toggle a known flag an admin must scroll through the entire list. | Add a search input and a category filter row directly above the Controls list (left of the 'Initialize Defaults / Refresh / Add Control' button cluster). Search should match feature name, machine ID, and description. Add a left-rail or sticky chip strip of category anchors (accounting, beta, …) using the same grouping the page already computes. | Purely additive client-side filter over the `featureFlags.*` list query — the full table, toggles, overrides, and create-flag dialog remain intact; filtering only narrows which rows render. |
| `feature_flags-UX-2` | **P1** | **Three stacked tab levels obscure Feature Flags** — Reaching flags requires Settings tab 'Developer' → sub-tab 'Feature Flags' → inner tab 'Controls (57)'. The outer Settings tabs render with almost no selected-state contrast (Developer looks the same weight as Access Control / Master Data / Organization), and the sub-tab row ('Feature Flags / VIP Access / Database') sits visually identical to the outer row. | Collapse the Developer sub-tab row into a segmented control placed inside the 'Developer' panel header ('Feature Flags \| VIP Access \| Database'), and visually demote it (smaller, muted background) so the top Settings tabs read as the primary nav. Give the active Settings tab a clear filled pill or underline so 'Developer' is unambiguous. Inline 'Controls / Change Log' as a smaller secondary toggle beside the 'Feature Controls' heading rather than a third tab strip. | All four Settings panes (Access Control, Master Data, Organization, Developer), the three Developer views (Feature Flags, VIP Access, Database), and the Controls vs. Change Log split are all retained — the change is visual weight and grouping, not routing. Baseline 'audit history dialog' and tabbed structure stay. |
| `feature_flags-UX-3` | **P1** | **'Initialize Defaults' is a destructive-looking button with no guardrail** — 'Initialize Defaults' sits in the header button cluster next to benign 'Refresh' and 'Add Control', with identical styling and no subtitle, tooltip, or confirmation affordance visible. Its effect on 57 live flags is unclear from the label alone. | Demote 'Initialize Defaults' to a secondary/ghost button positioned at the far left of the cluster (separated from Refresh/Add Control), add helper copy under it like 'Seeds any missing flags from code — will not overwrite existing values' (use the actual behavior), and require a confirm dialog listing the number of flags that would be created vs. untouched before commit. | The underlying `featureFlags.*` initialize mutation still runs; only its button styling, placement, microcopy, and confirmation step change. No behavior is removed. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header: 'System Settings' H1 with the four Settings tabs rendered as a clearly-selected pill row (Developer highlighted). Inside the Developer panel, replace the sub-tab strip with a compact segmented control beside the panel title: 'Developer · [Feature Flags] VIP Access  Database'. Below it, a single 'Feature Controls' section with: left — H2 + subtitle; right — button cluster ordered [Add Control] (primary), [Refresh] (ghost), [Initialize Defaults] (ghost, separated, with helper text). Under that, a toolbar row: search input ('Search flags, module ID, description…'), category filter chips (accounting, beta, …, All), and a small 'Controls (57) | Change Log' toggle. Table groups collapse/expand by category with Title Case headers and a sticky category jump rail on the left at ≥lg breakpoints. Row layout unchanged: Feature + machine ID + description | Active toggle | On by Default toggle | Requires | Access (overrides) icon.

#### WorkflowQueuePage — `/workflow-queue` (lightweight)

![WorkflowQueuePage](screenshots_all/workflow_queue.png)

*The kanban board is legible and the column counts give a quick sense of load, but the page wastes the most valuable real estate on redundant chrome (sub-page nav as buttons, giant sidebar, 'Back to Dashboard') and the cards repeat information without surfacing what an operator actually needs to triage: age in stage, priority, assignee, and order linkage. The raw enum badge 'AWAITING_INTAKE' on every card in the Awaiting Intake column is pure visual noise, and the fourth column ('Live') is clipped off the right edge because the board doesn't horizontally scroll or fit the viewport.*

**Keep.** Column header count chips with status-colored underlines make per-stage volume scannable at a glance.; Drag handle + card structure (batch ID, strain, qty, updated-at) maps cleanly to the WorkflowBoard DnD model.; View switcher (Board / Analytics / History / Settings) is surfaced as top-right actions rather than buried.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `workflow_queue-UX-1` | **P1** | **Fourth column clipped; board doesn't fit viewport** — The 'Live' column is cut off at the right edge of the screenshot — only the drag handle and truncated batch IDs are visible. With four fixed-width columns plus a 240px sidebar, the board overflows at common laptop widths and there is no visible horizontal scroll affordance. | Make the board container horizontally scrollable with a persistent scrollbar and sticky column headers, and add a collapse toggle on the left sidebar (the `«` control is already drawn but inert here) so operators can reclaim ~240px. Tighten column min-width to ~280px and let columns flex so 4–5 fit on a 1440px screen. | Does not touch `WorkflowBoard` DnD or `workflowQueue.*` data — purely a layout/overflow change on the board wrapper, so all statuses configured in WorkflowSettings remain reachable. |
| `workflow_queue-UX-2` | **P2** | **Redundant status badge on every card duplicates the column** — Each card inside 'Awaiting Intake' shows a pill reading `AWAITING_INTAKE`; cards in 'In Photography' show `LIVE` (incorrectly, per the column), and 'Photography Complete' shows `PHOTOGRAPHY_COMPLETE`. The pills use raw SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE enum values and in at least one column disagree with the column title. | Remove the in-card status pill when the card is in its matching column and replace the freed row with a priority chip + 'Updated 2mo ago' with a warning color when stale. If status must remain visible (e.g., during an optimistic drop), render it only when `card.status !== column.status`, and render the human label from the same WorkflowSettings color/name config used by the column header. | Preserves `WorkflowSettings` status labels/colors and the `workflowQueue.*` status field on each batch; the pill is conditionally rendered, never dropped from the data model or drag payload. |
| `workflow_queue-UX-3` | **P2** | **View switcher reads as unrelated actions, not a tab set** — Board, Analytics, History, and Settings are rendered as four equally-weighted outlined buttons alongside the primary 'Add to Queue' CTA, with no selected state indicating the current view is Board. The DOM also exposes zero tabs (`Tabs: []`). | Convert Board / Analytics / History / Settings into a segmented control (or underline tabs) immediately under the H1, with the active view filled. Keep 'Add to Queue' as the only primary-colored button in the header row. | Still drives the same `?view=board\|analytics\|history\|settings` query param and renders the same `WorkflowBoard`, `WorkflowAnalytics`, `WorkflowHistory`, `WorkflowSettings` components — only the control's visual grouping changes. |

**Redesign sketch.** Header row: H1 'Workflow Queue' with subtitle, single primary 'Add to Queue' button right-aligned. Directly beneath, a segmented tab bar: [Board] Analytics History Settings, with active state. Board area becomes a full-width horizontally-scrollable flex container with sticky column headers (name + count chip + colored underline sourced from WorkflowSettings). Sidebar gets a working collapse toggle. Card template (top to bottom): drag handle + batch ID + priority chip on row 1; strain name on row 2; qty + linked order number on row 3; footer with assignee avatar and relative updated-at that turns amber past an SLA threshold. Status pill is hidden when card.status matches its column; 'Back to Dashboard' moves into the breadcrumb only.

### Auth & Fallback

#### Login — `/login` (lightweight)

![Login](screenshots_all/login.png)

*This is a functional but completely generic sign-in card floating in a cream void. It authenticates, the button is clearly the primary action, and the form is short enough that nobody will get lost. But it wastes the one moment where TERP establishes brand and environment context: the wordmark is set in a default system stack, there's no indication this is a STAGING environment (the tab title says [STAGING] but the UI doesn't), and the card is vertically mis-centered — it sits in the upper third of the viewport with a huge empty band below the submit button. For an internal B2B tool where operators log in daily and sometimes across staging/prod, these are small but real misses.*

**Keep.** Single-column form with exactly two fields and a full-width primary button — zero ambiguity about what to do.; Labels sit above inputs with clear placeholder copy ('Enter your username' / 'Enter your password'), so the form is readable without focus state.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `login-UX-1` | **P1** | **No staging environment indicator in the UI** — The browser tab reads 'TERP [STAGING]' but the login card itself shows only 'TERP'. Once the tab is in a background window or pinned, there is no visual cue the user is authenticating against staging rather than production. | Render an environment badge next to or beneath the TERP wordmark when `import.meta.env.MODE !== 'production'` — e.g. a small amber pill reading 'STAGING' under the 'Sign in to your account' subtitle. Optionally tint the card border amber in non-prod. | Purely additive to the existing login card layout; does not touch `POST /api/auth/login`, the username/password fields, or the returnUrl handoff. |
| `login-UX-2` | **P2** | **TERP wordmark is unstyled and the card floats high on the page** — The 'TERP' heading is rendered in the default sans stack at a modest weight, and the entire card is pinned to roughly the upper third of the viewport, leaving a large empty band below the Sign in button. The brand moment is flat and the composition looks unfinished. | Vertically center the card in the viewport (flex min-h-screen, items-center). Set the TERP wordmark in the app's display face at ~32–36px, letter-spacing tightened, matching the sienna accent used on the Sign in button. Tighten the subtitle 'Sign in to your account' to a muted foreground color. | Only typography and container alignment change; the form fields, submit handler, and dev `VITE_SKIP_LOGIN_LOCAL` auto-redirect behavior are untouched. |
| `login-UX-3` | **P2** | **Password field has no show/hide toggle and no caps-lock hint** — The password input is a plain masked field with no trailing affordance. There is no way to verify what was typed and no warning if Caps Lock is on. | Add a trailing eye icon button inside the password input that toggles `type` between `password` and `text`, and show a small 'Caps Lock is on' helper line beneath the field when the keyboard event reports caps lock active. | The field still submits the same `password` value to `POST /api/auth/login`; only the input's presentation layer is enhanced. |

**Redesign sketch.** Full-viewport flex container, vertically and horizontally centered. Card is ~420px wide, white, soft shadow, 12px radius. Inside the card, top-to-bottom: (1) TERP wordmark in the app's display face, 34px, sienna-tinted, letter-spacing -0.02em; (2) directly beneath, when non-prod, a small amber pill 'STAGING'; (3) muted subtitle 'Sign in to your TERP account'; (4) 24px gap; (5) Username label + input; (6) Password label + input with a trailing eye toggle, and a reserved 16px helper slot that surfaces 'Caps Lock is on' or the server auth error in red; (7) full-width sienna 'Sign in' button, with a subtle loading spinner state; (8) small footer line 'Having trouble? Contact your TERP admin.' in muted text. No extra links, no social auth — this is an internal tool and the minimalism is correct; we're only fixing brand, environment clarity, and password ergonomics.

---

#### NotFound — `/definitely-does-not-exist` (lightweight)

![NotFound](screenshots_all/not_found.png)

*The 404 page is functional and friendly: a clear '404' heading, explanatory copy, and a 'Go Home' CTA. But for an internal ERP, it's a dead-end — the user who mistyped a URL or clicked a stale bookmark has exactly one escape hatch (home) and no way to search, jump to a recent module, or report the broken link. The breadcrumb showing 'Definitely Does Not Exist' as if it's a real page is also misleading. The visual treatment (large red alert icon) also overstates severity for what is usually a stale link.*

**Keep.** Clear, human microcopy ('Sorry, the page you are looking for doesn't exist. It may have been moved or deleted.') instead of a raw stack trace.; Global shell (sidebar, search, command palette, notifications) stays mounted so the user isn't fully stranded.; Single obvious primary action ('Go Home') with a matching home icon.

| ID | Sev | Finding | Fix | Preserved |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `not_found-UX-1` | **P2** | **Only one recovery path from a dead-end page** — The 404 card offers just 'Go Home'. For an ERP where users land here from stale bookmarks, Slack links, or mistyped order IDs, there's no 'Go Back', no link into the command palette, and no link to Active Orders / Sales / Recent pages. | Under the 'Go Home' button, add a secondary 'Go Back' button (history.back) and a third-tier text link 'Search with ⌘K' that focuses the existing global search/command palette. Keep 'Go Home' as the visual primary. | Uses the existing global Command Palette (CTRL K button already in the DOM) and browser history; no new routes or tRPC calls — the NotFound route at `/404` and its fallback behavior (TER-902) remain unchanged. |
| `not_found-UX-2` | **P3** | **Breadcrumb legitimizes the bad URL** — The top breadcrumb renders 'Definitely Does Not Exist' (the slugified bad path) as if it's a valid page node, next to the home icon. | On the NotFound route, replace the dynamic slug crumb with a static 'Not Found' label (muted) or suppress the second crumb entirely so the trail reads Home › Not Found. | Only the breadcrumb label for the NotFound route changes; the shared breadcrumb component and its behavior on valid routes are untouched. |
| `not_found-UX-3` | **P3** | **Alert-red iconography overstates severity** — A large red exclamation-in-circle icon sits above the 404 — the same visual vocabulary used for destructive errors and system failures elsewhere in TERP. | Swap the red alert icon for a neutral compass/map or muted search-empty illustration in the app's existing neutral/brand palette, and keep '404 · Page Not Found' as the heading pair. | Purely a visual asset swap inside the NotFound component; routing and TER-902 fallback logic are not affected. |

**Redesign sketch.** Centered card on the neutral background, max ~560px wide. Top: small neutral illustration (compass/empty-state, not red alert). Heading stack: eyebrow '404' (muted), H1 'We can't find that page', then one line of body copy: 'The link may be outdated or the record was deleted.' Below, a horizontal action row: primary 'Go Home' (filled), secondary 'Go Back' (outline), and a tertiary text link 'Search TERP  ⌘K' that triggers the existing command palette. Breadcrumb at the top reads simply Home › Not Found. No other layout changes to the global shell.

---

## 4. Functionality-Preserved Matrix

Every finding below is annotated with the exact baseline entity it must not disturb. This table is the contract: any PR that closes a ticket must pass a reviewer check that the named entity still works exactly as the baseline describes.

| Finding ID | Page | Severity | Baseline entity preserved | How the fix preserves it |
|---|---|---|---|---|

### P3 — cosmetic (count only)

_18 P3 findings across 17 pages. Full list is in the per-page audits in §3._

## 6. Rollout Plan

Four sprint-sized waves. Each wave is independently shippable and testable; each ends with a build that is a net-positive on every surface it touches.

### Wave 1 — 'Fix the primitives' (1 sprint, ~2 engineers)

Deliver T-02 (EmptyState / ErrorState / Skeleton variants on `ComponentErrorBoundary`), T-05 (numeric alignment in `SheetNativeTable`), T-07 (standardized `Sheet` drawer with Esc + close X + focus-return), T-10 (`FreshnessBadge` primitive), T-12 (retry wiring), T-13 (keyboard-hint bar on every `SheetNativeTable`). Each is a single-PR primitive that the remaining waves depend on.

### Wave 2 — 'Daily-use workspaces' (1 sprint, ~3 engineers)

Apply the Wave-1 primitives to Owner Command Center, Sales, Inventory, Procurement, Accounting Dashboard, Accounting Invoices, Analytics, Warehouse Pick-Pack, Client Profile. Also deliver T-03 (one primary button per surface), T-04 (persist sidebar group state), T-06 (deduplicate filter strips), T-09 (breadcrumbs on detail pages). This wave is where users feel the difference.

### Wave 3 — 'Tabs, views, and command palette' (1 sprint, ~2 engineers)

Deliver T-01 (column presets + saved views), T-08 (regroup workspace tabs — Accounting from 10→4 + pill bar, Sales from 7→4), T-11 (register all 20 admin pages in the Command Palette), T-15 (canonicalize terminology). These are higher-lift but unlock the admin long-tail and let us confidently delete duplicate surfaces.

### Wave 4 — 'Mobile + VIP polish' (1 sprint, ~2 engineers)

Deliver T-14 (mobile treatment: sidebar drawer below 768px, horizontal-scroll sticky-first-column tables, priority-ordered dashboard stack) and the remaining P2/P3 per-page items that weren't covered by cross-cutting themes. This is the right moment to also ship the VIP Portal redesign items (see per-page audits under 'VIP Portal').

## 7. Methodology

1. **Baseline ingestion.** Pulled `docs/FUNCTIONAL_BASELINE.md` and `docs/FUNCTIONAL_BASELINE_RUNTIME.md` from `github.com/EvanTenenbaum/TERP@main`. Parsed the 63 `### Page:` sections into per-page excerpts; matched the 65 inventory entries (workspaces count as multiple entries because their tabs are distinct baseline pages) by component name with fuzzy fallback.
2. **Capture.** Drove Playwright (real Chromium, not headless-shell) against `terp-staging-yicld.ondigitalocean.app` authenticated as `qa.superadmin@terp.test`. Each page captured at 1440×900; 17 full-depth pages captured a second scrolled viewport. Also harvested each page's `<h1>`, `<h2>`, `[role=tab]`, and visible `<button>` text into a runtime note.
3. **Opus 4.7 analysis.** For each page, sent the baseline excerpt + runtime note + screenshot(s) to `claude-opus-4-7` with adaptive extended thinking, `xhigh` effort for full-depth and `high` for lightweight, under a senior-design-critic system prompt that forbids removing baseline functionality and requires every finding to cite the preserved entity. Concurrency 5, 3-retry backoff on rate-limit.
4. **Aggregation.** 270 findings collected. 15 cross-cutting themes identified by reading the Opus output end-to-end and collapsing surface-agnostic patterns (T-01 through T-15). Per-page audits kept verbatim from Opus.
5. **No functionality removed.** Every fix proposed here is either (a) visual / layout / copy / default-state, (b) a new primitive that additively wraps existing behavior, or (c) a reorganization that preserves every current route and procedure.

## 8. Reproducibility

All scripts, screenshots, excerpts, and per-page JSON are in the `terp-ux-review/` bundle attached with this report:

- `scripts/page_inventory.json` — 65-entry inventory with route + depth
- `scripts/capture_all.py` — Playwright capture script (real Chromium)
- `scripts/build_excerpts.py` — baseline → per-page excerpt extractor
- `scripts/run_all_critiques.py` — async parallel Opus 4.7 runner (concurrency 5, xhigh thinking)
- `scripts/assemble_report.py` — this file's generator
- `screenshots_all/` — 65 base + 17 scrolled PNGs
- `runtime_notes/` — 65 DOM observation markdown files
- `excerpts_all/` — 65 baseline-excerpt markdown files
- `findings/` — 65 Opus 4.7 per-page JSON critiques

To re-run against a fresher staging deployment, replay `capture_all.py` then `run_all_critiques.py` (skip-existing on) and re-assemble with `assemble_report.py`. Total wall-time on a fresh run: ~35 minutes. Anthropic API cost at current rates: ~$9–12.
